## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/logging.py

Description:
1. This module centralizes logging configuration for the Captain Claw application using structlog and Python's logging.
2. It provides a file-like sink wrapper to forward formatted log lines into a callback for an external system UI.
3. The module exposes functions to set a custom system log sink, configure structured logging, and obtain configured loggers.
4. It builds a pipeline of structlog processors to merge contextvars, add log levels, timestamp events, render stack info, and format exceptions.
5. Depending on configuration it chooses either a console renderer for human-friendly output or a JSON renderer for machine consumption.
6. A helper class _SinkWriter implements write/flush semantics to integrate structlog's PrintLoggerFactory with a callback sink.
7. The configure_logging function reads logging settings from the global configuration to determine logging level and format.
8. The module uses a module-level get_logger helper to simplify retrieving structlog bound loggers by name.
9. The log variable at module scope provides a ready-to-use logger instance for code that imports this module.
10. Overall, the module separates platform-specific log output handling from application code by providing pluggable sinks and standard configuration.

Purpose:
1. The primary purpose of this file is to provide a single place to define how structured logs are produced and delivered across Captain Claw components.
2. It aims to ensure consistent log formatting, context propagation, and error rendering across different runtime environments.
3. The module supports redirecting structured logs to both developer-friendly console output and machine-readable JSON for aggregation systems.
4. It enables integration with an external UI or system panel through a callback sink so logs can be displayed in an application console rather than only stderr.
5. By centralizing configuration, the module lets other components simply call get_logger and rely on configured processors and formatting.
6. The _SinkWriter class purposefully decouples structlog's interface from arbitrary sink implementations by providing a minimal file-like adapter.
7. configure_logging reads runtime configuration and applies it to structlog so operators can change log verbosity and format without code changes.
8. The module also enforces best practices such as attaching timestamps, log levels, and stack information to logs for improved observability.
9. Another important purpose is to make it easy to include structured context (via contextvars) in all log events which supports tracing across async tasks.
10. It serves as a small abstraction layer that ensures application code does not need to know about the logger factory, processors, or sinks—only how to get a logger.
11. Additionally, it provides a hook (set_system_log_sink) that higher-level UI or platform code can call to route logs into different renderers or live displays.
12. It thereby improves developer ergonomics and operational flexibility when running Captain Claw in different deployment contexts.

Key elements:
- _system_log_sink: module-level optional callback sink for routing log lines.
- class _SinkWriter: file-like adapter with write() and flush() used by structlog's PrintLoggerFactory.
- set_system_log_sink(sink): function to set the optional sink used by the sink writer.
- configure_logging(): main function that reads configuration and configures structlog processors, renderer and logger factory.
- get_logger(name=None): convenience function returning a structlog BoundLogger optionally named.
- log: module-level BoundLogger instance created with get_logger(__name__).
- structlog processors list: merge_contextvars, add_log_level, TimeStamper, StackInfoRenderer, format_exc_info, ConsoleRenderer/JSONRenderer.
- use of get_config() from captain_claw.config to obtain logging.level and logging.format.

Key logic:
1. The module begins by declaring a global _system_log_sink that may be set by other parts of the platform; this sink is used for forwarding lines.
2. _SinkWriter buffers text written to it and splits on newlines so that each complete log line is forwarded to the sink callback; partial lines are retained until completed.
3. The flush method ensures any buffered text is sent to the sink if the writer is flushed, preventing lost messages on shutdown or formatter flushes.
4. set_system_log_sink simply assigns the provided callable to the module-level variable, enabling runtime reconfiguration of the log destination.
5. configure_logging retrieves the configuration object, translates the configured level string to a logging.Level value, and constructs a list of structlog processors.
6. It conditionally appends either a human-friendly ConsoleRenderer or a JSONRenderer to the processor pipeline depending on configuration.
7. The structlog.configure call assembles processors, picks a wrapper class that filters by the configured level, sets a simple dict context class, and supplies a PrintLoggerFactory.
8. When creating the PrintLoggerFactory it passes either an instance of _SinkWriter wrapping the system sink or sys.stderr so logs flow to the chosen destination.
9. get_logger returns a structlog logger bound to an optional name, which allows other modules to call get_logger(__name__) and produce structured events consistently.
10. The combination of contextvars merging and processors ensures that contextual data (like request ids or trace ids) is included in every emitted event without manual passing.
11. By centralizing renderer selection and log level, the module allows runtime toggling between debug/production styles of logging without code modifications.
12. The module exposes a module-level log instance so typical modules can import log and use it immediately without explicitly obtaining a named logger.

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/platform_lifecycle.py

Description:
1. This module provides helpers to initialize and tear down chat platform bridges for Telegram, Slack, and Discord.
2. It reads runtime configuration and uses it to enable or disable each platform and to obtain bot tokens and API base URLs.
3. For each enabled platform with a non-empty token it constructs a platform-specific Bridge object and a PlatformAdapter to load and save persisted state.
4. The initialization routine also cleans up expired pairings stored in platform state and starts background polling tasks for incoming updates.
5. Telegram initialization additionally registers bot commands and menu button commands before starting its long-poll loop.
6. Each platform's poll loop repeatedly requests updates from its bridge, updates stored offsets, and schedules asynchronous tasks to handle individual platform messages.
7. Polling loops catch and ignore cancellation to allow graceful shutdown and log other exceptions to the system UI, pausing briefly on errors.
8. The teardown function cancels any running poll tasks and attempts to close open bridge connections, suppressing exceptions during shutdown.
9. Throughout initialization and polling the module updates the UI with informational messages about enabled platforms, token problems, and registration results.
10. The module delegates actual message handling to a remote command handler and relies on external Bridge and PlatformAdapter implementations for platform-specific behavior.

Purpose:
1. The file centralizes lifecycle management for external chat platform integrations used by the application.
2. It exists to translate configuration state into running platform bridges, persistent adapter state, and background poll tasks.
3. By consolidating startup logic here, the rest of the codebase can assume a uniform platform state object and running poll loop for each enabled platform.
4. The module enforces a simple enablement check that considers both an explicit enabled flag and the presence of a bot token to avoid spurious starts.
5. It uses PlatformAdapter to load and save per-platform persistent state so that pairing information and offsets survive restarts.
6. Cleanup of expired pairings is performed during initialization to keep pairing lists current and to avoid leaking stale state.
7. Telegram receives extra setup by registering bot commands and menu buttons, reflecting platform-specific requirements placed in one location.
8. Background poll loops are started as asyncio tasks so updates are consumed concurrently and dispatched to the application's message handler.
9. The teardown routine provides a controlled shutdown path that cancels tasks and attempts to close network connections while tolerating errors.
10. The module reports status back to the user interface to make startup and error conditions visible to operators or users.
11. It intentionally delegates message processing to the remote_command_handler to keep platform polling separate from command execution logic.
12. Overall, this file exists to encapsulate the platform orchestration concerns—configuration interpretation, resource initialization, periodic polling, state persistence, error handling, and graceful shutdown—in a single well-defined place.

Key elements:
- init_platforms(ctx) (initializes Telegram, Slack, and Discord bridges and starts poll tasks)
- teardown_platforms(ctx) (cancels poll tasks and closes bridge connections)
- _register_telegram_commands(ctx) (registers Telegram bot commands and chat menu button commands)
- _telegram_poll_loop(ctx) (long-poll loop that fetches Telegram updates and dispatches them)
- _slack_poll_loop(ctx) (poll loop that fetches Slack updates and dispatches them)
- _discord_poll_loop(ctx) (poll loop that fetches Discord updates and dispatches them)
- get_config (external configuration provider used to read platform settings)
- PlatformAdapter (used to load and save per-platform persisted state)
- cleanup_expired_pairings (utility to remove stale pairing entries)
- TelegramBridge, SlackBridge, DiscordBridge (bridge classes instantiated for each platform)
- remote_command_handler.handle_platform_message (entry point for dispatched platform messages)
- ctx attributes used (ctx.telegram, ctx.slack, ctx.discord, ctx.ui, ctx.telegram_command_specs, ctx.platform_names)
- asyncio.create_task (used to run poll loops and to dispatch handlers concurrently)
- bridge.get_updates, bridge.set_my_commands, bridge.set_chat_menu_button_commands, bridge.close (bridge API surface used)

Key logic:
1. init_platforms begins by obtaining global configuration and then configures each platform by writing platform-specific config into the runtime context and computing an enabled flag from config.enabled or the presence of a bot token string.
2. For an enabled platform with a non-empty token the function constructs the appropriate Bridge (Telegram/Slack/Discord) passing token and API base URL, initializes offsets where applicable, and creates a PlatformAdapter for persistence.
3. The adapter's load_state method is awaited to restore persisted state, cleanup_expired_pairings is invoked to prune stale pairings, and the adapter's _save_state is awaited to persist any changes resulting from cleanup.
4. Telegram receives an extra registration step where the code calls set_my_commands and set_chat_menu_button_commands on the bridge and logs success or failure to the UI.
5. After initialization the module starts a background polling task for each platform via asyncio.create_task and appends a system message to the UI indicating the platform's polling status.
6. If a platform is marked enabled but its token string is empty, the code appends a UI message and deliberately skips constructing a bridge or starting polling for that platform.
7. teardown_platforms iterates over the available platform names, cancels any running poll_task, awaits the task while ignoring asyncio.CancelledError, and then attempts to close the bridge connection while suppressing exceptions to ensure a robust shutdown.
8. Each poll loop asserts the bridge exists and then enters an infinite loop that calls the bridge's get_updates API; Telegram uses an offset and timeout, while Slack and Discord receive updates plus next_offsets pairs.
9. Telegram's loop updates a numeric offset using update.update_id + 1 and preserves monotonic progression using max to combine offsets; Slack and Discord assign the returned next_offsets to the context offsets dictionary.
10. For each received update the loops schedule an asynchronous task to call the shared remote_command_handler.handle_platform_message with the platform name and update payload so message processing occurs concurrently and does not block polling.
11. Poll loops pause between iterations using either a configured poll timeout or a minimal sleep to control polling frequency and use brief sleeps after exceptions to avoid tight error loops.
12. All poll loops break cleanly on asyncio.CancelledError to support shutdown and log any other exceptions to the UI before sleeping and retrying.

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/platform_adapter.py

Description:
1. This module provides a unified async wrapper around platform-specific chat bridges for Telegram, Slack, and Discord.  
2. It implements multiple small text and audio helper functions to sanitize, truncate, and analyze chat content.  
3. The module extracts and collects MP3 file paths produced by a pocket_tts tool from tool output and from session tool messages.  
4. It manages ephemeral pairing tokens and a pending/approved user mapping with expiration cleanup and token generation.  
5. The PlatformAdapter class encapsulates per-platform operations including sending messages, audio files, chat actions, and marking messages read.  
6. The adapter also records outgoing events as tool outputs into the agent session and persists platform-specific state via a session manager.  
7. A typing-heartbeat helper runs a periodic chat-action while awaiting long-running work to give users a typing indicator.  
8. The adapter can automatically request TTS via a pocket_tts tool when a remote user requests audio and then send generated audio files.  
9. There are methods to issue pairing tokens to unknown users and to approve pairing tokens, moving users into an approved map and notifying them.  
10. A top-level approve_chat_pairing_token function provides a convenience entry point to approve tokens for the supported platforms.

Purpose:
1. The module exists to consolidate duplicated platform-specific logic into a single, reusable adapter that standardizes interactions across Telegram, Slack, and Discord.  
2. It centralizes message sending, audio delivery, chat-action signaling, and read-marking so higher-level command handlers need not handle platform differences.  
3. The helper functions provide deterministic text normalization and audio-path extraction so that TTS outputs can be discovered and sent reliably.  
4. Pairing token management is implemented here to control which remote users may interact with the system, including issuance, expiration, and approval flows.  
5. Persisting approved and pending user state via the agent session manager allows pairing state to survive process restarts and be shared with the session-backed storage.  
6. The monitor_event method records platform interactions into the agent session as tool messages, enabling auditing and model-context enrichment.  
7. The run_with_typing facility improves user experience by periodically emitting a platform-specific typing indicator while asynchronous work completes.  
8. By routing platform-specific bridge calls via the adapter, the rest of the codebase can treat sending/receiving actions uniformly and avoid conditional platform code duplication.  
9. The adapter integrates with the agent tool execution flow to request and handle TTS generation when a user explicitly requests audio output.  
10. Error handling and UI notifications are concentrated here so failures in platform operations are surfaced consistently to the operator UI.  
11. The module also exposes a convenience function to approve tokens without needing to construct an adapter elsewhere, simplifying administrative commands.  
12. Overall, the file exists to both simplify cross-platform support and to provide consistent stateful behavior for pairing and tool-driven outputs.

Key elements:
- truncate_chat_text (function; trims and collapses whitespace, limits characters).  
- chat_user_display (function; formats user display name from user record).  
- remote_user_requested_audio (function; detects audio/tts request keywords in user text).  
- extract_audio_paths_from_tool_output (function; parses tool output lines beginning with "Path:" and returns resolved .mp3 Paths).  
- collect_turn_generated_audio_paths (function; scans session messages from a turn start index for pocket_tts tool outputs).  
- cleanup_expired_pairings (function; removes expired tokens using now_utc and ISO timestamps).  
- generate_pairing_token (function; produces unique 8-char token from restricted alphabet).  
- PlatformAdapter (class; primary adapter encapsulating platform operations and state).  
- PlatformAdapter.__init__ (constructor; binds RuntimeContext and platform name and loads platform state).  
- PlatformAdapter.send (async method; sends text messages via platform bridge and logs outgoing event).  
- PlatformAdapter.send_chat_action (async method; sends typing/upload indicators to platform).  
- PlatformAdapter.mark_read (async method; marks messages read with platform-specific bridge calls).  
- PlatformAdapter.monitor_event (async method; logs events to UI and writes tool messages to agent session).  
- PlatformAdapter.run_with_typing (async method; runs coroutine while periodically sending typing actions).  
- PlatformAdapter.send_audio_file (async method; uploads audio per-platform and records outgoing_audio or error).  
- PlatformAdapter.maybe_send_audio_for_turn (async method; orchestrates pocket_tts invocation, result handling, and sending audio).  
- PlatformAdapter.pair_unknown_user (async method; issues or reuses pairing tokens, persists pending_pairings, and notifies user).  
- PlatformAdapter.approve_pairing_token (async method; validates token, moves entry to approved_users, persists state, notifies user).  
- PlatformAdapter._save_state / load_state (async methods; persist and restore approved/pending maps via session_manager JSON).  
- _message_user_id, _message_channel_id, _message_reply_id, _channel_kwargs, _reply_kwargs (helpers; normalize platform-specific message fields).  
- approve_chat_pairing_token (async function; convenience wrapper that creates adapter and approves a token).  
- External dependencies (get_config, now_utc, to_utc_iso, asyncio, secrets, pathlib.Path, json via runtime import, runtime context and agent interfaces).

Key logic:
1. The top-level text helpers normalize incoming strings, truncate long messages for previews, and determine whether user input requests audio using keyword matching.  
2. Audio-path extraction scans tool output lines that start with "Path:", strips any appended "(requested:" annotations, resolves file paths, filters for existing .mp3 files, and deduplicates results.  
3. collect_turn_generated_audio_paths iterates session messages from a provided index, selects tool messages produced by pocket_tts that are not error lines, and aggregates MP3 paths found by the extractor.  
4. Pairing cleanup computes the current UTC timestamp and removes pending pairing tokens whose ISO-formatted expires_at timestamps are in the past or unparsable.  
5. generate_pairing_token produces an 8-character token from a restricted alphabet and ensures uniqueness against the current pending map by regenerating on collision.  
6. PlatformAdapter stores a reference to the runtime context, platform name, and platform-specific state obtained from the context for later operations.  
7. Sending text routes to platform-specific bridge methods with appropriate parameter names (e.g., chat_id vs channel_id, reply identifiers) and on success records an outgoing_message tool event; failures append a system UI line.  
8. send_chat_action and mark_read use platform-conditional branches to call bridge APIs with the correct parameter sets and handle exceptions with UI logging.  
9. monitor_event assembles a payload and body text, appends it to the UI tool output, and, if there is an active agent session, adds a tool message to that session and triggers session persistence.  
10. run_with_typing creates an asyncio task that periodically sends a chat action until an Event is set, awaits the provided work coroutine, and then cancels and awaits the heartbeat task to shut it down cleanly.  
11. send_audio_file adapts upload semantics per platform, records outgoing_audio metadata including size, and on exception records an outgoing_audio_error and notifies the UI.  
12. maybe_send_audio_for_turn first attempts to reuse any MP3 files already generated during the turn; if none, it checks whether the user requested audio and whether pocket_tts is available, truncates source text to tool limits, invokes pocket_tts via agent tool execution, treats the tool output as a session tool message, persists the session, and sends any resulting MP3 files; errors are monitored and reported.  
13. pair_unknown_user ensures expired tokens are cleaned, reuses existing tokens per user when present, otherwise generates a new token with an expiration derived from configuration or defaults, saves the pending pairing, persists state, and sends a pairing instruction message to the originating channel.  
14. approve_pairing_token canonicalizes the provided token, ensures it exists and contains a user_id, promotes the pending record into approved_users with metadata and approval timestamp, persists both maps, and notifies the approved chat if a bridge is available.  
15. State persistence is implemented by serializing approved_users and pending_pairings to JSON using the agent.session_manager.set_app_state and restored via get_app_state with defensive parsing.  
16. A small convenience function approve_chat_pairing_token validates platform argument, constructs an adapter, and delegates approval, centralizing administrative token approval behavior.

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_reasoning_mixin.py

Description:
1. This mixin provides helper methods for clarification handling, contract planning, and list-task reasoning used by an agent.  
2. It includes heuristics to detect when users request clarifications, ask to cover all sources, or request fresh fetches.  
3. It can merge a short follow-up user reply with a previous assistant anchor or assistant response to form an effective user input for planning.  
4. The mixin tracks clarification state in session metadata and updates pending or cleared flags based on assistant prompts and user replies.  
5. It supplies a source-report prefetch pipeline that iterates source URLs, invokes a web_fetch tool when available, and records tool outputs and success/failure counts.  
6. There are utilities to count per-source sections, detect a conclusion heading, and validate a source-by-source report for completeness.  
7. The module extracts JSON objects from noisy model outputs (including fenced code blocks) to interpret planner and critic responses.  
8. Contract generation uses LLM-based planner prompts with token-limit-aware retry logic, normalization of tasks and requirements, and a fallback default contract when needed.  
9. A critic pass evaluates candidate responses against contract requirements by calling the model, parsing JSON checks, and assembling completion judgments.  
10. The mixin also supports list-extraction, member normalization, execution-strategy selection (direct vs script), coverage evaluation, and feedback generation.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to centralize reasoning patterns and planning utilities that are shared across agent behaviors.  
2. It encapsulates clarification heuristics so the agent can avoid unnecessary re-research and sensibly merge short user replies into context.  
3. By tracking clarification state in session metadata the mixin enables multi-turn clarification workflows to persist across messages.  
4. It provides a structured contract generation flow so the agent can decompose complex requests into tasks, requirements, and prefetch URLs before execution.  
5. The normalized contract representation makes downstream execution, retries, and critic evaluation more deterministic and machine-readable.  
6. Prefetch and source-report helpers let the agent proactively fetch and record web sources when the web_fetch tool is available, improving evidence collection.  
7. The critic evaluation step enforces contract requirements and yields per-requirement checks so the agent can gate completion or produce targeted corrections.  
8. List-processing helpers support extracting list members from context, normalizing them, choosing an execution strategy, and verifying coverage after execution.  
9. Rephrasing logic reduces downstream parsing complexity by optionally rewriting complex free-form prompts into structured, extractable formats.  
10. Deterministic utilities—JSON extraction, id normalization, and simple regex-based detectors—stabilize LLM-driven workflows and reduce brittle parsing.  
11. The mixin integrates with instruction templates, model completion guards, and the tools subsystem to keep LLM interactions consistent and observable.  
12. Overall, it lets higher-level agent code focus on orchestration while delegating planning, validation, and list reasoning to a single reusable component.

Key elements:
- AgentReasoningMixin class (mixin container for reasoning helpers).  
- _request_references_all_sources (heuristic to detect "check all sources" intent).  
- _assistant_requests_clarification (heuristic to detect agent clarification questions).  
- _should_apply_pending_clarification (heuristic to decide whether to merge a pending clarification).  
- _resolve_effective_user_input (merges anchor/assistant text into the user's input when appropriate).  
- _update_clarification_state (updates session.metadata clarification_state).  
- _should_run_source_report_pipeline (decide whether to run per-source report).  
- _run_source_report_prefetch (async prefetch that iterates URLs, calls web_fetch via _execute_tool_with_guard, records outputs).  
- _count_source_sections / _has_conclusion_section / _validate_source_report_response (report validation helpers).  
- _extract_json_object (parses first JSON object from raw model text, including fenced blocks).  
- _should_use_contract_pipeline (mode/planning toggle logic).  
- _normalize_contract_tasks / _normalize_contract_requirements (normalize planner output into stable task DAG and requirement list).  
- _default_task_contract (fallback contract construction).  
- _generate_task_contract (async planner call with retries, token caps, normalization, and prefetch URL merging).  
- _evaluate_contract_completion (async critic that calls model and parses JSON checks).  
- _build_completion_feedback (compose retry guidance from critic output).  
- _should_rephrase_task / _rephrase_task (detect and perform prompt rephrasing via LLM).  
- _normalize_list_members / _generate_list_task_plan / _choose_list_execution_strategy (list extraction and strategy selection).  
- _collect_list_extraction_context / _evaluate_list_member_coverage / _build_list_coverage_feedback / _apply_list_requirements (list coverage evaluation and requirement augmentation).  
- External integrations: get_config (config access), Message (instruction/LLM message wrapper), self.tools (tool discovery and saved paths), self.instructions (template loading), and various self.* helpers (_complete_with_guards, _execute_tool_with_guard, _emit_tool_output, _add_session_message).

Key logic:
1. The mixin first applies lightweight regex-based heuristics to user text to detect intents like "check all sources," list-processing requests, explicit script generation, or requests to refetch data.  
2. For pending clarification flows it inspects session.metadata.clarification_state and, when the user's reply is short and not a command, merges either the original anchor or the last assistant response into an augmented effective input.  
3. The merge records whether the user explicitly requested a fresh fetch and annotates the merged prompt to allow re-research when requested.  
4. Clarification state is updated after assistant outputs: if the assistant asked clarifying questions the pending flag and anchor are set; otherwise any pending flag is cleared and timestamps updated.  
5. Source-report prefetching first checks for web_fetch availability, then iterates source URLs, calls a guarded tool execution, records tagged tool messages into the session, emits telemetry, and counts fetched/failed totals.  
6. Contract generation builds system and user prompt messages from instruction templates, configures max token budgets with first and retry attempts, calls the model via a guarded completion function, and attempts to parse an emitted JSON object.  
7. If planner output is invalid the logic falls back to a deterministic default contract and emits a planner_fallback tool output.  
8. Task normalization traverses planner-provided structures recursively, extracts titles, children, dependencies, retry limits, and timeouts, enforces depth and total-node caps, and assigns stable ids.  
9. Prefetch URL handling merges planner-provided URLs with recent sources and truncates to configured limits; when require_all_sources is set, missing URLs may be added to requirements.  
10. The critic evaluation constructs a critic prompt, calls the model with token limits, extracts JSON checks, maps checks to the original requirement ids, and derives a boolean completion result based on check outcomes.  
11. Feedback construction composes human-readable retry instructions by combining critic feedback and enumerating missing requirement reasons, instructing the agent to return only corrected final answers when appropriate.  
12. Rephrase logic computes complexity signals (multiple URLs, list-language markers, format mentions, line counts, list punctuation) and only calls the rephraser when the signal threshold is met; rephrased text is sanity-checked for length and stripped of code fences.  
13. List extraction calls an LLM extractor, normalizes and deduplicates members, selects a strategy (direct tool usage or script) based on explicit script requests or recommended strategy, and emits tool outputs summarizing the plan.  
14. After execution the mixin evaluates coverage by scanning assistant/tool messages and saved artifact filenames for aliases of each member, classifies covered vs missing members, and either adds per-member requirements or composes coverage feedback advising script regeneration or continued direct looping.  
15. Throughout the flows the mixin relies on small deterministic helpers (regex-based JSON/URL parsing, id normalization, alias generation) and emits structured telemetry via _emit_tool_output to integrate with the broader agent tooling and session systems.

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/session_orchestrator.py

Description:
1. This module implements SessionOrchestrator, a coordinator that decomposes complex user requests into task graphs, dispatches tasks to worker agents, and synthesizes final results.  
2. It uses an LLM provider to decompose the user's input into a JSON plan and to synthesize a combined answer from task outputs.  
3. The orchestrator builds a TaskGraph from the plan and tracks task metadata, dependencies, statuses, retries, and results.  
4. An AgentPool is used to obtain per-task worker agents which run task-specific prompts and return outputs.  
5. The module manages session assignment by creating new sessions when tasks lack an existing session_id and can honor preview overrides.  
6. It executes tasks in parallel across sessions, monitoring progress, handling timeouts, retries, cancellations, and restart logic.  
7. A shared FileRegistry is provided so tasks can share and discover files produced by upstream dependencies within a run.  
8. The orchestrator supports saving and loading workflows to disk, extracting and substituting template variables in task text, and exporting run outputs as Markdown.  
9. It broadcasts structured events and emits tool output callbacks to inform external listeners of decomposition, execution progress, timeouts, and completion.  
10. Utility parsing logic extracts JSON blobs from noisy LLM responses, stripping code fences and searching for brace-delimited blocks.  

Purpose:
1. The purpose of this file is to provide a high-level orchestration layer that enables multi-session, parallel execution of decomposed tasks in Captain Claw.  
2. By splitting complex requests into a DAG of smaller tasks, it lets specialized worker agents run isolated subtasks while the orchestrator manages dependencies and ordering.  
3. This separation improves scalability and allows independent tasks to run concurrently without contaminating each other's session context.  
4. The orchestrator exists to coordinate interactions between the LLM provider, agent pool, session manager, instruction templates, and file registry so these components can work together.  
5. It exposes a prepare step for decomposition and preview, and an execute step that applies overrides, assigns sessions, and runs the full execution lifecycle, making it suitable for both synchronous and asynchronous use.  
6. Workflow save/load and variable extraction features let users persist reusable task plans and parameterize workflows without manual reconstruction.  
7. The module centralizes timeout handling, pause/edit/resume semantics, retry behavior, and restart cascades to provide robust execution control and to surface meaningful events to UI or API layers.  
8. It also collects usage and context metrics from workers and emits these through callbacks for telemetry or user feedback.  
9. By keeping a shared FileRegistry, the orchestrator enables cross-task file discovery and produces comprehensive manifests for synthesis and reporting.  
10. The JSON parsing utilities and prompt rendering protect downstream steps from noisy LLM output formats, improving resilience of the decomposition and synthesis stages.  
11. Finally, the orchestrator provides programmatic methods for task management (pause, edit, update, restart, resume, postpone) and lifecycle operations (reset, shutdown) that the rest of the application can call.  
12. Overall, this file exists to encapsulate the complex control flow, concurrency, and persistence concerns needed to run multi-step, multi-session workflows reliably.  

Key elements:
- SessionOrchestrator class (primary orchestrator implementing preparation, execution, synthesis, and lifecycle).  
- _decompose (method that builds prompts, calls LLM provider, and parses JSON plans).  
- _assign_sessions (method that assigns or creates sessions via session_manager).  
- _execute_graph (main execution loop driving parallel task execution and timeout handling).  
- _run_worker (per-task worker runner that uses AgentPool and agent.complete).  
- _synthesize (method that formats task results and calls provider.complete for final answer).  
- prepare / execute / orchestrate (public API methods for decomposition preview and full run).  
- pause_task, edit_task, update_task, restart_task, resume_task, postpone_task (task control methods).  
- save_workflow, load_workflow, list_workflows, delete_workflow, _save_run_output (persistence and reporting functions).  
- _parse_json_response (robust JSON extraction from LLM output including fence and brace handling).  
- _extract_variables, _substitute_variables, _safe_filename, _generate_workflow_name (utility functions for variable and filename handling).  
- AgentPool, InstructionLoader, FileRegistry, get_session_manager, LLMProvider/get_provider, TaskGraph/OrchestratorTask (notable external classes/dependencies).  
- Callbacks: status_callback, tool_output_callback, broadcast_callback (external integration hooks).  

Key logic:
1. prepare(user_input) first creates a FileRegistry for the run, calls _decompose to obtain a JSON plan from the LLM, validates the plan, and constructs a TaskGraph of OrchestratorTask objects for preview.  
2. The _decompose flow renders system and user prompts with InstructionLoader, appends an available-sessions summary, invokes the provider.complete call with a planner timeout, and parses the returned text with _parse_json_response.  
3. During graph construction the orchestrator skips invalid tasks (empty id), logs warnings, and assembles a previewable tasks list while extracting {{variable}} placeholders for templating.  
4. execute applies variable substitutions and per-task overrides, optionally applies a workflow-level model override, and then assigns sessions for tasks that lack session_id via _assign_sessions which may call session_manager.create_session.  
5. _execute_graph manages concurrency by activating ready tasks from the TaskGraph, creating asyncio tasks for _run_worker, and tracking them in _pending_futures while enforcing a poll loop using asyncio.wait with FIRST_COMPLETED.  
6. The execution loop uses graph.tick_timeouts to detect warning, restart, and failure conditions and broadcasts timeout events; it also supports waiting on a resume_event when no tasks are active to allow user-driven edits/postpones.  
7. _run_worker obtains an Agent from AgentPool, applies per-task model overrides, composes a worker prompt including a file manifest from FileRegistry, awaits agent.complete, and on success calls graph.complete_task with captured output and usage metrics.  
8. Worker exceptions, timeouts, and cancellations are handled to mark tasks failed, emit tool output and broadcast task_failed events, and always release the agent back to the pool in a finally block.  
9. Timeout-handling semantics include emitting warnings, cancelling and restarting timed-out attempts, and exhausting retries to mark tasks as failed when necessary.  
10. Task control methods (pause/edit/update/restart/resume/postpone) manipulate graph state, cancel or await pending worker futures, evict cached agents when descriptions change, and signal the execution loop to re-evaluate activatable tasks.  
11. After all tasks complete or fail, _synthesize collects formatted task results via _format_results_for_synthesis, attaches a file manifest if present, renders a synthesis prompt, and calls the provider for a final aggregated answer, falling back to raw results or timeout/failure messages on error.  
12. Workflow persistence writes and reads JSON files under a workspace workflows directory, serializing task definitions, variables, and model metadata, and rebuilding TaskGraph objects when loading.  
13. _parse_json_response implements a tiered strategy to recover a dict from LLM output: direct json.loads, stripping and parsing code fences, then extracting the first brace-delimited block as a last resort.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/config.py

Description:
1. This module defines typed configuration models and utilities for Captain Claw using Pydantic BaseModel and BaseSettings.  
2. It declares default filesystem locations for the user config YAML and session database and a local config filename.  
3. The file contains many nested configuration classes covering model, context, memory, tools, skills, guards, session, workspace, UI, logging, messaging integrations, and orchestration.  
4. The Config class centralizes application settings and configures environment variable handling via SettingsConfigDict with an env prefix and nested delimiter.  
5. Helper methods implement loading from YAML, sanitizing legacy YAML constructs, reading simple .env files, and mapping legacy top-level keys into the nested model.  
6. The load() method overlays environment variables and .env values onto the parsed YAML to ensure sensitive tokens can be injected securely.  
7. The save() method persists the active configuration to disk as JSON-safe YAML and ensures parent directories exist.  
8. A resolved_workspace_path() utility converts the workspace path into an absolute path anchored to a runtime base or the current working directory.  
9. The module exposes a module-level singleton pattern with get_config() and set_config() to share a global Config instance across the application.  
10. Several defaults, fallback behaviors, and provider compatibility rules are encoded so common environment variables are honored when appropriate.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a single authoritative source of runtime configuration for Captain Claw and to enforce typing, defaults, and validation for all subsystems.  
2. It centralizes the mechanics of reading configuration from persistent YAML files while still allowing secure, operational overrides from environment variables or a .env file.  
3. By modeling each subsystem as its own Pydantic model, it makes defaults explicit and simplifies consumption by other modules that require structured settings.  
4. The legacy compatibility helpers allow the project to accept older flat configuration formats and sanitize legacy YAML serialization artifacts without forcing manual user migrations.  
5. Environment-overlay logic is specifically designed to keep secrets out of repository YAML by allowing tokens, API keys, and credentials to be provided at runtime instead.  
6. The module codifies provider-specific fallback rules (for example, mapping OPENAI_API_KEY to the model.api_key for OpenAI providers) to reduce operator configuration friction.  
7. The save method enables programmatic updates to configuration to be written back to disk in a stable, JSON-safe YAML format.  
8. resolved_workspace_path prevents ambiguous relative workspace references by anchoring non-absolute workspace paths to a given runtime base or CWD.  
9. The SettingsConfigDict configuration on the Config class standardizes environment variable prefixing and nested delimiter behavior for predictable env-driven overrides.  
10. Exposing get_config and set_config implements a straightforward global accessor pattern so modules can share a single config instance without repeated parsing.  
11. The module bundles many tool-, memory-, and integration-specific defaults so a freshly-installed environment has sensible behavior without extensive operator setup.  
12. Overall, this file reduces duplication, improves upgrade tolerance, and centralizes security-sensitive configuration concerns for the whole application.

Key elements:
- DEFAULT_CONFIG_PATH, DEFAULT_DB_PATH, LOCAL_CONFIG_FILENAME (module-level path constants).  
- ModelConfig (Pydantic model for LLM/provider settings; includes nested AllowedModelConfig).  
- ContextConfig, MemoryEmbeddingsConfig, MemorySearchConfig, MemoryConfig (memory-related settings and defaults).  
- ShellToolConfig (includes ExecPolicy StrEnum for shell execution policies).  
- WebFetchToolConfig, WebSearchToolConfig, PocketTTSToolConfig, SendMailToolConfig, TypesenseToolConfig (tool-specific configuration models).  
- ToolsConfig (aggregates enabled tools and tool-specific subconfigs).  
- SkillEntryConfig, SkillsLoadConfig, SkillsInstallConfig, SkillsConfig (skill subsystem configuration).  
- GuardTypeConfig, GuardConfig (guard behavior toggles for input/output/script tools).  
- SessionConfig, WorkspaceConfig, UIConfig, ExecutionQueueConfig, LoggingConfig (runtime and UI settings).  
- TelegramConfig, SlackConfig, DiscordConfig (messaging integration configs).  
- TodoConfig, AddressBookConfig, ScriptsMemoryConfig, ApisMemoryConfig (cross-session memory settings).  
- ScaleConfig, DeepMemoryConfig, OrchestratorConfig, GoogleOAuthConfig, WebConfig (advanced and integration settings).  
- Config (BaseSettings central settings class with methods: _apply_legacy_top_level_config, _read_dotenv_file, resolve_default_config_path, from_yaml, load, save, resolved_workspace_path).  
- _config (module-level singleton), get_config(), set_config() (singleton accessors).  
- External dependencies: yaml.safe_load/safe_dump, pydantic.BaseModel/BaseSettings, pydantic_settings.SettingsConfigDict, os, re, pathlib.Path.

Key logic:
1. Loading begins with Config.from_yaml which determines the config file path (local config in CWD preferred) and returns a default Config if no file exists.  
2. from_yaml reads the YAML file text and attempts yaml.safe_load; if a ConstructorError referencing python/object/apply appears it applies a regex-based sanitization to strip legacy python/object/apply tags and retries parsing.  
3. If sanitization changed the content, from_yaml attempts to write the sanitized YAML back to disk (best-effort, swallow exceptions).  
4. After parsing YAML, _apply_legacy_top_level_config is invoked to map legacy flat keys like openai_api_key and ollama_base_url into the nested model dict under "model", and to remove the old keys.  
5. Config.load first calls from_yaml then reads simple KEY=VALUE pairs from a .env file using _read_dotenv_file which strips comments, supports optional leading "export ", and unquotes quoted values.  
6. load builds an env_overlay = cls() instance so that Pydantic's SettingsConfigDict behavior can surface any environment-prefixed variables set in the runtime environment.  
7. The method then checks for sensitive values (Telegram, Slack, Discord tokens, Brave API key, Typesense key, and mail/SMPP credentials) and overlays non-empty environment/.env values into the loaded Config instance, preserving YAML values unless env values are present.  
8. For mail and other mapped keys, load iterates a small mapping and conditionally sets attributes, converting smtp_port to int when appropriate and ignoring invalid conversions.  
9. Provider compatibility logic checks the configured model.provider and if the model.api_key is empty it will look for common provider environment variables (OPENAI_API_KEY, ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, GEMINI_API_KEY/GOOGLE_API_KEY) and set model.api_key accordingly.  
10. Additional provider fallback logic sets an Ollama base_url from OLLAMA_BASE_URL if the provider is ollama and base_url is empty.  
11. Google OAuth environment overrides are applied for client id/secret/project id and GOOGLE_OAUTH_ENABLED is interpreted from truthy strings; google_oauth.enabled is auto-enabled if both client id and secret are present.  
12. The save() method converts the Pydantic model to a JSON-safe dict via model_dump(mode="json", exclude_none=True), ensures the parent directory exists, and writes YAML using yaml.safe_dump with consistent formatting.  
13. resolved_workspace_path converts the configured workspace.path into an absolute Path by expanding user and either returning it directly for absolute paths or joining it to a provided runtime_base or current working directory for relative paths.  
14. The module-level singleton uses get_config to lazily load and cache a Config instance via Config.load and set_config to replace it, providing a simple global accessor pattern for the rest of the application.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_skills_mixin.py

Description:
1. This module provides a mixin class AgentSkillsMixin containing helpers for loading, ranking, invoking, and managing skills for an agent.  
2. It includes utilities to parse LLM payloads to extract selected candidate IDs.  
3. The mixin offers functions to resolve and cache a workspace skills snapshot with session-aware caching and optional watch/debounce behavior.  
4. There is logic to build a skills section suitable for inclusion in a system prompt that instructs the model how to pick and read SKILL.md files.  
5. It can list invocable skill command specifications and rewrite user prompts to direct the model to use a specific skill.  
6. The module supports invoking skill commands either by dispatching to a tool or running a script and handles tool execution results and session message recording.  
7. It includes workflows to install a skill from a GitHub URL and to install a skill's declared dependencies.  
8. A search routine queries a configured skill catalog, ranks candidates lexically, optionally reranks with an LLM, and returns top results.  
9. Helper methods handle applying and restoring environment overrides defined by skills before running tasks.  
10. The implementation relies on external helper functions and classes imported from captain_claw.skills, the runtime provider for LLM calls, session manager methods, and configuration utilities.  

Purpose:
1. The mixin centralizes skill-related functionality so an Agent implementation can manage skills without duplicating logic.  
2. It exists to bridge skill metadata, catalog search, and runtime dispatch mechanisms into a coherent API used by higher-level agent code.  
3. Snapshot resolution and caching reduce expensive filesystem or network operations by preserving a skills snapshot tied to workspace state and session metadata.  
4. Building a skills system prompt section ensures the agent can present available skills to an LLM in a consistent, constrained format so the model knows how to select and read skill documentation.  
5. The search and ranking facilities let the agent find relevant skills by combining fast lexical ranking with optional LLM-based semantic re-ranking for higher quality suggestions.  
6. Manual invocation and dispatch handling enable users to run skill commands as tools or scripts while the mixin builds commands, runs them through guarded execution, and records outputs.  
7. Installation helpers keep skill acquisition and dependency installation inside agent workflows, returning structured results and errors for the caller to surface.  
8. Environment override application makes skill-provided environment variables and API keys available during execution and provides a restore callback to confine their scope.  
9. Session-aware snapshot restoration allows agents to reuse previously computed skill snapshots stored in session metadata when appropriate.  
10. Error handling and fallbacks (for example when provider or catalog sources are unavailable) are included so higher-level code can present clear failure states.  
11. The mixin is provider-aware and only attempts LLM re-ranking when a configured provider exists, avoiding unnecessary exceptions.  
12. Overall, it exists to provide a reusable, testable surface for skill discovery, selection, invocation, installation, and environment management within the agent runtime.

Key elements:
- AgentSkillsMixin (class; central mixin providing all skill helpers).  
- _extract_skill_search_ids (method; parses LLM payloads to integer candidate IDs).  
- _rank_skill_search_entries_with_llm (async method; builds prompts and calls provider.complete to semantically rank candidates).  
- _resolve_skills_snapshot (method; computes, caches, and restores SkillSnapshot instances using session metadata and watch/debounce settings).  
- _build_skills_system_prompt_section (method; returns a formatted skills block for inclusion in system prompts).  
- list_user_invocable_skills (method; returns current SkillCommandSpec entries).  
- rewrite_prompt_for_skill (method; produces a prompt that instructs the model to use a specific skill).  
- _resolve_script_dispatch_command (static method; resolves script dispatch to a shell command and script path, handling interpreters and argument quoting).  
- invoke_skill_command (async method; dispatches commands to tools or scripts or returns a rewritten prompt).  
- install_skill_from_github (async method; wraps install_skill_from_github_url and returns metadata).  
- install_skill_dependencies (async method; calls install_skill_dependencies_for_entry and normalizes the result).  
- search_skill_catalog (async method; loads catalog, does lexical ranking, optional LLM re-ranking, and returns structured results).  
- _apply_skill_env_overrides_for_run (method; applies skill env overrides via apply_skill_env_overrides and returns a restore callback).  
- External dependencies (functions/classes used): get_config, Message, get_logger, build_workspace_skill_snapshot, compute_skills_snapshot_version, apply_skill_env_overrides, load_skill_catalog_entries, rank_skill_catalog_entries, install_skill_from_github_url, install_skill_dependencies_for_entry, find_skill_command, snapshot_from_dict, snapshot_to_dict.  
- Expected host attributes/methods referenced on self: provider (LLM provider), workspace_base_path, session, session_manager.save_session, _execute_tool_with_guard, _add_session_message, _emit_tool_output.

Key logic:
1. Payload extraction first collects several possible keys from an LLM response (selected_ids, top_ids, ids, selected, results) and normalizes values into positive integer IDs while ignoring invalid values.  
2. LLM-based ranking composes a candidate JSON payload and two prompts (system and user) instructing the model to return strict JSON with selected_ids, then calls provider.complete with low temperature and a token limit.  
3. The ranking method attempts to parse a JSON response and falls back to an internal _extract_json_object hook if the direct parse fails, then maps returned indices back to catalog entries within bounds.  
4. Snapshot resolution uses configuration-controlled watch behavior and debounce timing to decide whether to return a cached SkillSnapshot or recompute it by computing a version hash and building a workspace snapshot.  
5. When session metadata contains a stored snapshot, the resolution routine may restore the snapshot via snapshot_from_dict and reuse it if versions match or watch is disabled.  
6. After building a new snapshot with build_workspace_skill_snapshot the method caches it and writes a snapshot and timestamp into session.metadata["skills"] when a session exists.  
7. The skills system prompt section prepends mandatory instructions about scanning available skills and constraints, then appends the snapshot-provided prompt block if present.  
8. invoke_skill_command resolves a command by name and, depending on dispatch.kind, either constructs a tool call (packing command, commandName, skillName) or resolves a script command into a quoted shell command and delegates execution to _execute_tool_with_guard.  
9. Tool and script dispatch paths capture execution success or error, add a corresponding session message with role "tool", emit tool output events, and persist the session via session_manager.save_session when available.  
10. If a command is neither a tool nor a script dispatch, invoke_skill_command returns a rewritten prompt instructing the model to use the specified skill, enabling prompt-based skill invocation.  
11. The install_skill_from_github method calls install_skill_from_github_url and then refreshes the snapshot to list aliases for the newly installed skill, wrapping exceptions into structured error responses.  
12. install_skill_dependencies delegates to install_skill_dependencies_for_entry and returns either a detailed success dictionary including stdout/stderr/command info or a normalized error structure on failure.  
13. search_skill_catalog validates configuration for a source URL, loads catalog entries via load_skill_catalog_entries in a thread, constructs a lexical pool and fallback ranks with rank_skill_catalog_entries, optionally invokes the LLM reranker on an expanded pool, and assembles a deduplicated top-N result list to return.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/skills.py

Description:
1. This module implements skill discovery, parsing, metadata representation, and command invocation metadata for Captain Claw.  
2. It defines many dataclasses to model skill install specifications, metadata, invocation policies, command dispatch and snapshot structures.  
3. It parses SKILL.md frontmatter using YAML/JSON rules to extract skill name, description, metadata and invocation policies.  
4. The module discovers skills from multiple configured roots including bundled, managed, workspace, plugin and extra directories with ordered precedence.  
5. It can parse GitHub URLs to identify a skill folder or SKILL.md location and download skill content either through the GitHub Contents API or by cloning the repository.  
6. The code supports installing declared runtime dependencies using multiple installers (brew, node, go, uv, download) and can extract archives safely.  
7. It builds a prompt-friendly XML-like representation of available skills, constructs invocable command specs, and resolves slash-style command invocations.  
8. Snapshot utilities compute a deterministic snapshot version, serialize and restore snapshots, and assemble a prompt payload for model injection.  
9. Filtering routines evaluate metadata requirements, platform constraints, environment and config prerequisites to determine eligible skills.  
10. Various helper functions perform path normalization, security checks, archive normalization, GitHub API interactions, and environment override application.  

Purpose:
1. The module centralizes all logic required to locate, load, describe and expose skills to the rest of the application.  
2. It exists to discover SKILL.md files from a configurable set of roots so skills provided by the workspace, plugins, bundled packages and managed installs are available with a clear precedence.  
3. By parsing frontmatter and an embedded metadata block it extracts runtime requirements, install instructions and invocation controls that determine whether and how a skill may be used.  
4. The file supplies installation helpers that can fetch skill content from GitHub either by the API (directory download) or by cloning the repository and validating the selected SKILL.md.  
5. It implements dependency installation flows that choose an appropriate installer based on declared install specs and platform constraints, then run commands or extract archives and return structured results.  
6. Snapshot and serialization functions let the runtime build a compact representation of available skills and commands for injection into model prompts or storing in session metadata.  
7. Command-spec builders translate skill declarations into user-invocable commands and encode dispatch behavior to tool invocation or script execution as declared in frontmatter.  
8. Filtering and ranking helpers enforce configuration allowlists, platform compatibility and declared requirements so only usable skills are presented to users and models.  
9. Security-oriented utilities normalize repository subpaths, prevent path traversal, validate archive members and refuse extraction of symlinks or entries that escape the target directory.  
10. The module is shaped to integrate with the project's Config and logging layers so user preferences (installer selection, prompt size limits, plugin dirs) are honored and diagnostics are emitted.  
11. Lightweight HTTP interactions using httpx support catalog fetching and GitHub contents retrieval, while simple lexical ranking provides a fallback for catalog search.  
12. In sum, the module exists to make skill discovery, installation, dependency orchestration and runtime exposure robust, inspectable and configurable for the Captain Claw tooling.  

Key elements:
- SkillInstallSpec (dataclass representing a single installer option declared by a skill).  
- SkillRequires, SkillMetadata, SkillInvocationPolicy (dataclasses modeling metadata and invocation rules).  
- SkillEntry, SkillCommandDispatch, SkillCommandSpec, SkillSnapshot, SkillSnapshotSkill (dataclasses for loaded skill entries, command specs and snapshot structures).  
- GitHubSkillSource, SkillInstallResult, SkillDependencyInstallResult, SkillCatalogEntry (dataclasses for GitHub parsing and installation/catalog results).  
- parse_github_skill_source (parses supported GitHub URLs into owner/repo/ref/skill_path).  
- install_skill_from_github_url (high-level installer that downloads/clones and copies a skill into managed_dir).  
- install_skill_dependencies (selects and runs installers for a skill's declared install specs and returns structured results).  
- _install_download_spec, _run_install_command, _resolve_node_install_command (helpers for download/extract and running install commands).  
- _run_git_clone, _fetch_github_contents, _download_github_directory, _download_file_to_path (GitHub API and git fallbacks for fetching skill files).  
- _extract_zip_archive, _extract_tar_archive, _normalize_archive_member_path (safe archive extraction routines).  
- _parse_frontmatter, _parse_metadata_block, _parse_metadata, _parse_install_spec (frontmatter and metadata parsing utilities).  
- _resolve_skill_roots, _iter_skill_md_candidates, load_workspace_skill_entries, _load_skill_entry (discovery and loading of SKILL.md files from configured roots).  
- filter_skill_entries, _meets_requires, _is_config_path_truthy (filtering by requirements, env and config).  
- build_workspace_skill_command_specs, find_skill_command, resolve_skill_command_invocation (command spec construction and slash-invocation resolution).  
- build_workspace_skill_snapshot, compute_skills_snapshot_version, snapshot_to_dict, snapshot_from_dict (snapshot assembly, hashing and serialization).  
- apply_skill_env_overrides (applies temporary env/apiKey overrides for a snapshot run).  
- fetch_skill_catalog_markdown, parse_skill_catalog_entries, rank_skill_catalog_entries (catalog fetching and fallback lexical ranking).  
- External dependencies (httpx, yaml, shutil, subprocess, tarfile, zipfile, hashlib, os, re, json).  

Key logic:
1. The module first establishes an ordered set of skill roots by combining user-configured extra directories, plugin-inferred skill dirs, bundled package skills, managed installs, agent-specific directories and the workspace skills directory, while deduplicating results.  
2. For each root it enumerates candidate SKILL.md files by checking a top-level SKILL.md or scanning child directories up to configured limits, then it loads each candidate only if under configured size limits.  
3. Loading a SKILL.md involves parsing a YAML frontmatter block, extracting name and description (with fallbacks), parsing an embedded metadata block (JSON or YAML inline), and resolving an invocation policy.  
4. Filtering runs against the merged entries to remove skills that fail platform checks, bundled allowlists, explicit disabled config entries, or declared requirements for binaries, environment variables or config paths.  
5. Command specs are produced for user-invocable skills by sanitizing names, ensuring uniqueness, and reading frontmatter keys to choose tool dispatch or script dispatch, resolving absolute script paths safely against the skill base directory.  
6. Snapshot construction composes a prompt fragment by formatting available skills into an XML-like block, then applies character and item count limits via a binary-search truncation strategy to respect max chars while maximizing included items.  
7. GitHub URL parsing supports repository, /tree/<ref>/<path> and /blob/<ref>/<path-to-SKILL.md> forms; downloads prefer the GitHub Contents API for directory pulls and fall back to a shallow git clone when necessary.  
8. Dependency installation normalizes declared install specs, filters by current runtime platform, selects a preferred installer according to configuration and availability (e.g., prefer brew or node manager), and executes the corresponding command or download/extract flow returning a SkillDependencyInstallResult.  
9. Downloaded archives are written to controlled target directories and extracted with tight normalization: path components can be stripped, entries validated to avoid escapes, symlinks/hardlinks refused and file writes resolved relative to the target root.  
10. Error handling communicates failures either via raised exceptions for high-level install problems or through structured result objects that include stdout/stderr/code and human messages for installer failures.  
11. Snapshot versioning computes a deterministic SHA-1 hash over resolved SKILL.md file paths, sizes and modification times to detect changes across the set of discovered skill files.  
12. Environment overrides apply per-skill configured env values and API keys by setting missing variables temporarily and returning a reverter closure to restore the original environment after the run.  
13. Additional utilities support catalog fetching by attempting README.md candidates for a configured source URL, parsing markdown bullet lists into entries, and providing a simple lexical ranking fallback based on token matches in name and description.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/memory.py

Description:
1. This module implements layered and working memory primitives used by Captain Claw for managing conversational context.  
2. It defines a WorkingMemory class that stores a sequence of role/content messages and a text summary representing older context.  
3. A small WorkingMemorySnapshot dataclass is declared to serialize a summary plus a list of messages.  
4. The WorkingMemory provides simple token estimation, message counting, and logic to decide when compaction is needed.  
5. Compaction summarizes older messages into a short human-readable summary and retains a configurable recent window of messages.  
6. The snapshot method can inject the accumulated summary as an assistant message with a tool_name marker for later consumption.  
7. A LayeredMemory facade composes the WorkingMemory with an optional SemanticMemoryIndex to provide long-term, searchable memory.  
8. LayeredMemory exposes session management, recording of messages that triggers semantic sync scheduling, and delegates semantic search and note building.  
9. A factory function create_layered_memory builds the layered memory from runtime config and will attempt to initialize a semantic memory index.  
10. The module includes a Memory alias for backward compatibility and logs warnings if semantic memory initialization fails.

Purpose:
This file exists to centralize short-term and long-term conversational state handling for the application. It provides an in-turn working memory that retains recent turns and a consolidated summary of earlier context so prompts can include relevant history without exceeding token budgets. By offering token estimation and a threshold-based compaction policy, it helps prevent prompt size blowups while preserving salient context. The compaction routine produces concise human-readable snippets of dropped messages and merges them into the stored summary to maintain continuity. The snapshot functionality formats the summary as an assistant message so downstream components or the model can consume it explicitly. LayeredMemory integrates an optional SemanticMemoryIndex to allow persistent, searchable memory that can be synchronized in the background and used to build context notes for queries. The facade also manages an active session identifier and ensures that the semantic index is aware of the current session. Error handling in the factory function ensures the system continues operating with only working memory if semantic initialization fails, with a logged warning. This separation enables other parts of the system to record messages, request compaction, perform semantic searches, and schedule syncs through a simple, consistent API. Overall, the module exists to balance immediate conversation detail with scalable persistent memory while keeping interfaces small and robust.

Key elements:
- WorkingMemorySnapshot (dataclass) (serializable container for summary and messages).  
- WorkingMemory (class) (stores messages, summary; compaction and snapshot logic).  
- WorkingMemory.add_message(role, content) (append message to working buffer).  
- WorkingMemory.clear() (reset messages and summary).  
- WorkingMemory.estimate_tokens(text) (heuristic token estimator: len//4 with min 1).  
- WorkingMemory.get_token_count() (computes combined summary + messages token estimate).  
- WorkingMemory.should_compact(threshold=0.8) (decides if compaction is needed).  
- WorkingMemory.compact(keep_recent_ratio=0.4) (summarizes older messages and retains recent window).  
- WorkingMemory.snapshot(include_summary_message=True) (returns WorkingMemorySnapshot and can prepend summary as assistant message with tool_name).  
- LayeredMemory (class) (facade combining working and semantic memories; session management).  
- LayeredMemory.set_active_session(session_id) (sets active session and forwards to semantic index).  
- LayeredMemory.record_message(role, content) (adds to working memory and schedules semantic sync for user/assistant roles).  
- LayeredMemory.search_semantic(query, max_results) (delegates to semantic index or returns empty).  
- LayeredMemory.build_semantic_note(query, ...) (delegates to semantic.build_context_note).  
- LayeredMemory.schedule_background_sync(reason) (delegates schedule_sync to semantic index).  
- create_layered_memory(config, session_db_path, workspace_path) (factory to create WorkingMemory and optional SemanticMemoryIndex).  
- Memory (alias) (backward-compatible alias for WorkingMemory).  
- Dependencies: captain_claw.semantic_memory.create_semantic_memory_index and SemanticMemoryIndex, captain_claw.logging.get_logger, re module.

Key logic:
The module uses a simple length-based heuristic to estimate tokens by dividing character count by four and ensuring at least one token. WorkingMemory accumulates messages as dicts containing role and content and maintains a separate summary string representing older context. get_token_count sums an estimated token count for the summary (if present) and each message entry to produce a lightweight measure of memory size. should_compact compares that token count against a fraction of max_tokens to decide whether to trigger compaction. compact keeps a configurable recent fraction of messages and treats the rest as candidates for summarization; it limits summary sources to the last ten dropped messages and produces one-line snippets (up to 180 characters) per dropped message. New summary lines are prefixed with role and merged with any existing summary using a blank-line separator so historical summaries accumulate over multiple compactions. After compaction the internal messages list is replaced with the recent window and an info log records counts and whether a summary exists. snapshot optionally injects the stored summary as an assistant message with tool_name "working_memory_summary" before returning a WorkingMemorySnapshot containing the summary and current messages. LayeredMemory composes a WorkingMemory and an optional SemanticMemoryIndex; set_active_session updates an internal active_session_id and forwards it to the semantic index if present. record_message always appends to working memory and only schedules a semantic sync when the role is "user" or "assistant" to avoid indexing irrelevant tool/system logs. search_semantic and build_semantic_note return empty results or empty strings when no semantic index is configured, providing safe no-op behavior. schedule_background_sync and close are thin delegations to the semantic index when available. create_layered_memory reads configuration to determine whether to enable semantic memory, constructs WorkingMemory with a max_tokens value taken from config.context (or a default), and attempts to initialize the semantic index while catching exceptions and logging a warning to fall back to working-only memory.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_pool.py

Description:
1. This module implements an AgentPool class that manages a collection of worker Agent instances for parallel session orchestration.  
2. The pool maps agents by session_id and tracks last-used timestamps to enable idle eviction.  
3. Agent creation is coordinated with a global lock for lookups and per-session locks to avoid duplicate concurrent creation for the same session.  
4. get_or_create provides a fast path for cached agents and a safe creation path that evicts idle agents when the pool hits capacity.  
5. The heavy work of instantiating and configuring a worker agent is performed outside the global lock to allow parallel creation for different sessions.  
6. _create_worker_agent constructs an Agent bound to a specific session, auto-approves tool calls, and shares provider, instruction cache, and optional file registry.  
7. Worker agents bypass the normal initialization flow, are marked as workers with tuned limits, and are flagged initialized to allow completion calls.  
8. The pool exposes explicit eviction, release (mark idle), and bulk idle eviction based on configurable idle timeout.  
9. Internal eviction logic iterates over last-used timestamps and removes agents that exceed the idle threshold while logging actions.  
10. A shutdown method clears the pool and logs the number of released agents.

Purpose:
This file exists to provide a concurrent-safe, bounded pool of worker Agents used by orchestration code that needs per-session workers. It centralizes lifecycle responsibilities such as creating, registering, and removing agents so other parts of the system can request a ready-to-use agent by session id without duplicating setup logic. The pool enforces a maximum number of active agents to control resource usage and implements eviction strategies to reclaim idle workers. Per-session locks prevent race conditions where multiple coroutines would otherwise create duplicate agents for the same session. Performing the expensive agent setup outside the global lock improves throughput by allowing different sessions to be provisioned in parallel. Sharing an InstructionLoader instance across workers reduces redundant template caching and conserves memory. The pool also coordinates sharing of the LLM provider instance and an optional file registry so worker agents can resolve files produced by other tasks during an orchestration run. Worker-specific configuration (auto-approval, lowered iteration limits, and skipping heavy pipelines) tailors agents for short-lived orchestration tasks rather than interactive sessions. The class exposes simple lifecycle operations (evict, release, evict_idle, shutdown) so the rest of the application can manage agent reclamation explicitly when needed. Logging calls provide operational visibility into pool events like creation, eviction, and shutdown. Overall, the module encapsulates concurrency, resource bounds, and worker specialization to make parallel session execution safe and efficient within the project.

Key elements:
- AgentPool class (core pool manager for worker agents).  
- __init__ (configures max_agents, idle_evict_seconds, provider, callbacks, and internal structures).  
- size property (returns current agent count).  
- get_or_create(session_id, file_registry) (public async entrypoint to obtain or create a worker agent).  
- _create_worker_agent(session_id, file_registry) (async helper that constructs and configures a bound Agent).  
- evict(session_id) (remove a specific agent from the pool).  
- release(session_id) (mark agent as recently used/idle reset).  
- evict_idle() (async method to evict agents unused beyond the idle threshold).  
- _evict_idle_locked() (internal eviction implementation that inspects last-used timestamps).  
- shutdown() (clear the pool and metadata).  
- _creating (per-session asyncio.Lock map to prevent duplicate creation).  
- _shared_instructions (InstructionLoader instance shared across workers).  
- External dependencies: InstructionLoader, get_provider (LLM provider getter), get_session_manager (session loader/creator), Agent import done inside method, logging via get_logger.

Key logic:
The pool uses a two-layer locking strategy: a global asyncio.Lock guards access to the agent and last-used dictionaries for quick atomic lookups and registrations, while a per-session lock in the _creating map ensures only one coroutine creates an agent for a given session. get_or_create first acquires the global lock and returns a cached agent immediately when present, updating the last-used timestamp and optionally refreshing the agent's file registry. If no agent exists, it ensures a per-session lock exists, releases the global lock, and awaits the per-session lock so other session creations may proceed concurrently. After acquiring the session lock it re-checks under the global lock to handle the race where another coroutine finished creation in the interim. When the pool is at capacity, the code invokes _evict_idle_locked to remove entries idle beyond the configured threshold; if that doesn't free space, it forcibly evicts the oldest agent by last-used timestamp. Heavy-weight agent construction is performed by _create_worker_agent outside the global lock to avoid blocking other operations; this method imports the Agent class lazily, creates an agent with auto-approval semantics, ensures a provider is set, and loads or creates the bound session via the session manager. The created agent receives shared resources: the provider, the instruction loader cache, and an optional file registry; it also synchronizes runtime flags from session metadata and registers default tools. Worker-specific flags and limits are applied (e.g., marking _is_worker, lowering max_iterations, setting _initialized) to tailor behavior for orchestration tasks. After creation, the agent is registered under the global lock and the per-session creation lock is removed. Eviction operations compute which sessions exceed the idle threshold by comparing monotonic timestamps and remove their agents and last-used entries while logging the number evicted. The evict method can explicitly remove a single session's agent (useful after edits), and release updates last-used to mark activity. Shutdown obtains the global lock, clears both agent and last-used mappings, and logs how many agents were released. Throughout, logging statements capture lifecycle events for observability.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_guard_mixin.py

Description:
1. This module defines an AgentGuardMixin class that provides guard evaluation and guarded completion/tool execution helpers for an Agent.  
2. It includes utilities to build compact trace payloads for pipeline events and to truncate large text payloads for guard evaluation.  
3. The mixin can serialize outbound prompt messages into a concise text form used by input guards.  
4. It reads guard configuration from a central config and normalizes enabled flags and enforcement levels.  
5. The mixin implements parsing logic to interpret guard model outputs, attempting JSON parsing and heuristic fallbacks.  
6. It runs guard evaluations by rendering system and user prompt templates and calling the configured provider to get a classifier response.  
7. Depending on configuration, the mixin can block, allow, or request human approval for flagged content.  
8. The mixin wraps LLM completions with pre- and post-guard checks and emits diagnostic traces and session messages.  
9. It also enforces a script/tool guard before invoking tools and forwards context like session id and approval callbacks to the tools layer.  
10. Errors from guard enforcement are surfaced as GuardBlockedError exceptions when a guard blocks an action.

Purpose:
This mixin exists to centralize and standardize content-safety checks around LLM interactions and tool invocations for agents. It provides a single place to interpret guard configuration, run classifier-style guard checks, and enforce policy decisions consistently across completions and tool executions.
