3. The WebServer exposes many HTTP endpoints and delegates request handling to specialized functions in the captain_claw.web package.  
4. It provides callbacks to broadcast agent status, thinking updates, tool outputs, and approval notices to connected WebSocket clients.  
5. The WebServer lazily initializes a SessionOrchestrator, an AgentPool for OpenAI-compatible API proxying, and a GoogleOAuthManager when configured.  
6. The module contains logic to integrate a Telegram bridge and queue inbound Telegram messages for processing.  
7. The create_app method registers routes for instructions, config, sessions, orchestrator, cron jobs, entities, workflows, loops, OAuth, and static assets.  
8. The _run_server coroutine handles event loop setup, signal handling, agent initialization, starting services (Telegram, cron scheduler), and graceful shutdown.  
9. A helper _get_web_runtime_context constructs a minimal RuntimeContext object suitable for running cron jobs in web mode.  
10. The file provides run_web_server and main entry points that configure logging, load configuration, ensure workspace/session directories, and start the server process.

Purpose:
1. The file centralizes web server orchestration so the Captain Claw application can be accessed via a browser and websocket clients.  
2. It exists to expose the application's capabilities (instructions, sessions, orchestrator controls, cron, entities, workflows, loops, OAuth and more) over HTTP and WebSocket endpoints.  
3. By delegating route handlers to the captain_claw.web package, it keeps HTTP routing and high-level lifecycle concerns separate from request-specific logic.  
4. The WebServer class unifies lifecycle management for core components (Agent, orchestrator, API agent pool, OAuth manager, Telegram bridge) and coordinates their initialization and shutdown.  
5. The broadcasting callbacks provide a simple mechanism for the agent and related components to push real-time updates to any connected UI clients.  
6. Conditional initialization (API pool, OAuth manager, static assets) allows the server to adapt to configuration and environment without modifying route code.  
7. The module also acts as the main program entry point for running the web UI, performing startup sequencing, workspace preparation, and top-level exception handling.  
8. Integrating the cron scheduler and providing a lightweight runtime context enables cron jobs to run within the same process while receiving agent-based utilities.  
9. Signal handling and the stop_event pattern implemented in _run_server support graceful termination initiated by external signals or user interrupt.  
10. The WebServer's helpers and delegated endpoints provide a stable interface that other modules (e.g., web handlers, orchestrator, telegram bridge) can rely on during runtime.  
11. The design keeps resource cleanup explicit: it cancels tasks, shuts down pools and orchestrators, stops Telegram, closes websockets, and calls runner.cleanup before exiting.  
12. Overall, this module ties together networking, async orchestration, authentication, real-time UI broadcasts, and lifecycle management for the web-facing part of Captain Claw.

Key elements:
- STATIC_DIR (Path) (static assets folder used when present).  
- COMMANDS (list[dict]) (help/suggestion command definitions surfaced to the UI).  
- class WebServer (main server class that holds state and methods).  
- WebServer.__init__ (initializes agent-related state, queues, tasks, and configuration-derived flags).  
- WebServer._init_agent (async; creates Agent, SessionOrchestrator, optional AgentPool, and GoogleOAuthManager).  
- WebServer._status_callback (broadcasts status updates).  
- WebServer._thinking_callback (broadcasts thinking/reasoning updates).  
- WebServer._tool_output_callback (broadcasts tool output; may emit rephrase chat messages and thinking summaries).  
- WebServer._approval_callback (handles tool approval requests and broadcasts notices).  
- WebServer._broadcast (serialize message to JSON and send to all connected websockets).  
- WebServer._send (send message to a single websocket).  
- WebServer._get_web_runtime_context (builds minimal RuntimeContext for cron).  
- Delegated async handlers (ws_handler, list_instructions, get_instruction, put_instruction, revert_instruction, many _* methods that import and forward to captain_claw.web.* modules).  
- WebServer.create_app (registers routes with aiohttp.web.Application, including conditional routes for API proxy and static pages).  
- _run_server (async entrypoint: setup, signal handling, start services, cron, and shutdown).  
- run_web_server and main (synchronous entrypoints that configure logging, load config, ensure directories, and start the server).  
- Integration points: imports of Agent, AgentPool, SessionOrchestrator, GoogleOAuthManager, InstructionLoader, TelegramBridge/TelegramMessage, aiohttp.web, and cron_scheduler_loop.

Key logic:
1. On instantiation, WebServer captures configuration, prepares state containers (websocket clients set, locks, queues), and computes flags for optional features like Telegram and API proxying.  
2. _init_agent asynchronously constructs the main Agent and then creates a SessionOrchestrator that shares provider and callbacks; if enabled it also creates an AgentPool and a GoogleOAuthManager, injecting stored tokens into the provider when applicable.  
3. Status, thinking, tool output, and approval callbacks are simple adapters that format messages and call _broadcast so all connected WebSocket clients receive real-time UI updates.  
4. _tool_output_callback applies a silent-tools filter, sends monitor messages, emits a rephrase chat message when the "task_rephrase" tool completes, and synthesizes brief thinking summaries for non-silent tools.  
5. _broadcast serializes the message to JSON and iterates over the clients set, scheduling asynchronous sends and pruning any closed or failing websockets to keep the client set clean.  
6. Many HTTP endpoints are thin delegators: each route handler imports the actual implementation from captain_claw.web.* on demand and awaits its result, keeping the router lightweight and lazily resolving dependencies.  
7. create_app wires a comprehensive set of routes for APIs, orchestrator controls, cron management, entity CRUD, workflow browsing, loop runner endpoints, OAuth flows, and optionally the OpenAI-compatible API endpoints and static file serving.  
8. _run_server prepares the asyncio event loop, installs signal handlers that set an asyncio.Event to trigger shutdown, initializes the agent and starts Telegram integration, then constructs and starts an aiohttp site on the configured host and port.  
9. If configured, it starts an in-process cron scheduler task using a minimal RuntimeContext that supplies non-blocking UI methods and auto-confirmation behavior for web-mode cron execution.  
10. The main server wait loop blocks on the stop_event; when signaled it cancels the cron worker, attempts graceful shutdown of orchestrator and agent pool, stops Telegram, closes active websockets, cleans up the aiohttp runner, and finally calls os._exit(0) to terminate the process.  
11. run_web_server wraps _run_server in asyncio.run and handles KeyboardInterrupt gracefully; main sets up logging, loads and applies configuration, ensures session and workspace directories exist, and invokes run_web_server while reporting fatal errors.  
12. Throughout, the module prefers defensive exception handling during startup and teardown so failures in auxiliary components do not prevent the web server from attempting best-effort cleanup.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/task_graph.py

Description:
1. This module implements a standalone directed acyclic graph (DAG) scheduler for orchestrating tasks.  
2. It defines an OrchestratorTask dataclass that represents a unit of work with metadata such as dependencies, status, retries, timeouts, and results.  
3. The TaskGraph class manages a collection of OrchestratorTask instances and maintains ordering, readiness, running, completed, failed, and held sets.  
4. A stable topological sort is implemented using a variant of Kahn's algorithm to produce deterministic activation order.  
5. The graph can activate ready tasks up to a configurable max_parallel concurrency limit while respecting editing and hold states.  
6. Task lifecycle operations include completing, failing with retry semantics, pausing, resuming, editing, restarting, and updating descriptions.  
7. Timeout management uses a two-phase approach where tasks that exceed timeout_seconds enter a TIMEOUT_WARNING grace period before being restarted or failed.  
8. The module exposes query methods to retrieve results, summaries, counts, and flags indicating completion or failures.  
9. State refresh recomputes topology and categorizes tasks as ready, blocked, running, completed, failed, or held based on dependency resolution and statuses.  
10. Overall, the code provides deterministic orchestration primitives suitable for session orchestration and parallel task management.  

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a focused, reusable scheduler component that can be used by higher-level orchestrators to run tasks with dependency and concurrency constraints.  
2. By encapsulating task state, ordering, activation, and timeout/retry logic, it separates orchestration mechanics from business logic.  
3. TaskGraph centralizes rules about when tasks become runnable, how failures propagate, and how retries are applied, reducing duplication in the codebase.  
4. The OrchestratorTask dataclass standardizes the task payload expected by the orchestrator and carries execution metadata needed for control decisions.  
5. The topological sort ensures tasks are started in a deterministic order consistent with declared dependencies, which aids reproducibility and debugging.  
6. Concurrency control via max_parallel lets the system limit resource usage and coordinate parallel workers without external coordination.  
7. Timeout handling with a warning grace period gives an operator or UI a chance to postpone restarts instead of immediately failing long-running tasks.  
8. Retry semantics allow transient errors to be retried automatically while still surfacing permanent failures after a configured number of attempts.  
9. Control methods such as pause, resume, edit, and restart provide interactive capabilities for human-in-the-loop workflows and editing of instructions.  
10. Graph-level query methods produce compact summaries and results suitable for dashboards, logging, or driving orchestration decisions.  
11. The module is written to be self-contained and deterministic, making it straightforward to test in isolation from other services.  
12. Its design supports use by a SessionOrchestrator or similar component that can poll activate_next, run tasks, report completions, and call tick_timeouts periodically.  

Key elements:
- PENDING, QUEUED, RUNNING, COMPLETED, FAILED, PAUSED, EDITING, TIMEOUT_WARNING (status constants).  
- TIMEOUT_GRACE_SECONDS (global grace period between warning and automatic restart).  
- OrchestratorTask (dataclass carrying id, title, description, depends_on, session info, status, retries, timeouts, timestamps, result, error, editing flag, etc.; includes is_terminal()).  
- TaskGraph class (core scheduler managing tasks, order, and state sets).  
- TaskGraph._topological_sort (static method implementing Kahn's algorithm for stable ordering).  
- TaskGraph.refresh (recomputes order and categorizes tasks into ready/blocked/running/completed/failed/held).  
- TaskGraph.activate_next (traffic-light activation up to max_parallel, honors editing/hold states).  
- TaskGraph.complete_task and fail_task (completion and failure with retry/reset behavior).  
- Task control methods: pause_task, resume_task, edit_task, update_task_description, restart_task.  
- TaskGraph.tick_timeouts and postpone_task (two-phase timeout handling with warning, grace countdown, restart/fail behavior, and postponement).  
- Query and summary methods: tasks, task_count, is_complete, has_failures, running_count, ready_count, get_results, get_summary.  
- Dependencies: time module for monotonic timestamps; dataclasses and typing for type and structure.  

Key logic:
1. Tasks are stored in a dictionary keyed by id and the graph maintains multiple derived sets (ready, blocked, running, completed, failed, held) that are recalculated by refresh.  
2. The _topological_sort method builds forward and reverse dependency maps, seeds a sorted ready list of zero-dependency tasks, and processes dependents in deterministic order, appending any cyclic leftovers at the end.  
3. refresh uses the topological order and each task's status and declared dependencies to determine whether dependencies are satisfied, failed, or still blocking, and it cascades failures to dependents when a dependency is in FAILED.  
4. activate_next first calls refresh, computes available slots from max_parallel minus currently running tasks, and then transitions ready tasks (in topological order) to RUNNING while skipping tasks marked editing.  
5. When a task is activated its started_at timestamp is set with time.monotonic(), and it is added to the running set; activate_next returns newly activated tasks for worker consumption.  
6. complete_task sets status to COMPLETED, records result and completion timestamp, and leaves activation of dependents to the orchestrator loop to avoid races.  
7. fail_task increments retries and resets tasks back to PENDING if retries remain, otherwise marks them FAILED and stamps completed_at; error messages encode retry counts or exhaustion.  
8. Pause/resume/edit/restart/update operations manipulate status, editing flags, timestamps, and error fields with guards to ensure valid transitions and to support human edits and interactive control.  
9. tick_timeouts iterates currently running tasks and implements a two-phase timeout: once elapsed > timeout_seconds a task enters TIMEOUT_WARNING and timeout_warning_at is set, and during the grace period a countdown is reported.  
10. If the grace period expires and retries remain the task is reset to PENDING with retries incremented and appropriate error text; if retries are exhausted the task is moved to FAILED and completed_at is recorded.  
11. postpone_task allows an externally triggered postponement by returning a TIMEOUT_WARNING task back to RUNNING with a fresh started_at, effectively granting another full timeout interval.  
12. Graph-level query methods recompute state as needed and return compact structures that summarize counts, completion/failure flags, and per-task result metadata for UI, logging, or orchestration decision-making.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/semantic_memory.py

Description:
1. This module implements a SQLite-backed semantic memory index with hybrid retrieval combining keyword full-text search and vector search.  
2. It defines dataclasses for search hits, documents, and chunks to represent indexed content and results.  
3. Multiple embedding provider implementations and a provider chain are provided to generate normalized vector embeddings, with failover behavior.  
4. The SemanticMemoryIndex class encapsulates configuration, database schema creation, indexing, background synchronization, caching, and search APIs.  
5. The indexer can walk a workspace directory and read a session SQLite DB to collect documents, applying include/exclude filters and size limits.  
6. Documents are chunked into overlapping line-based pieces, stored in memory_chunks and an FTS5 virtual table, and optionally have embeddings persisted.  
7. Keyword search uses FTS5 with a fallback LIKE query, returning BM25-based text scores for candidates.  
8. Vector search embeds queries, computes cosine similarity against stored embeddings, and ranks candidates by vector score.  
9. A hybrid merge routine combines text and vector scores with configurable weights, applies optional temporal decay, enforces a minimum score, and sorts results.  
10. Background synchronization runs in a separate daemon thread to keep the SQLite index in sync with workspace and session sources, while cache and locks manage concurrency and staleness.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a durable, local semantic memory for the application so other components can retrieve contextually relevant text snippets from both workspace files and session histories.  
2. It centralizes the logic for scanning sources, creating and maintaining an index schema optimized for fast keyword and vector queries, and persisting both textual chunks and numeric embeddings.  
3. By supporting multiple embedding providers and a provider chain with automatic failover, the module enables semantic search when external models are available while falling back to a local hashing approach otherwise.  
4. The implementation exposes configuration knobs (chunk size, overlap, file limits, inclusion rules, caching and decay parameters) so different deployments can tune retrieval behavior.  
5. Background synchronization decouples indexing from search calls, allowing searches to trigger non-blocking updates and reducing latency in user-facing query operations.  
6. The class-level locking strategy isolates database access and sync state, providing safe concurrent use from multiple threads within the same process.  
7. The hybrid scoring and merging logic lets the system leverage complementary signals from keyword and vector matches to produce more relevant results than either approach alone.  
8. Temporal decay of scores biases results toward recent content, which helps prioritize up-to-date context in interactive sessions.  
9. The module offers utility methods to upsert ad-hoc documents (useful for tests or manual memory injection) and to format top hits into prompt-friendly context notes and debug strings.  
10. It provides a single factory function to construct a configured SemanticMemoryIndex from a higher-level memory configuration object, simplifying integration with application configuration systems.  
11. Error handling and fallbacks (FTS fallback, embedding provider fallbacks, and robust parsing) make the component resilient to partial failures in external dependencies or corrupt inputs.  
12. Overall, the file exists to make local textual context discoverable, ranked, and consumable by other parts of the system while remaining configurable and robust.

Key elements:
- SemanticMemoryResult (dataclass: represents a single search hit with scores and metadata).  
- _Document (dataclass: in-memory representation of a document to index).  
- _Chunk (dataclass: representation of a document chunk including line ranges).  
- _EmbeddingProvider (Protocol: interface describing embed_batch).  
- _LocalHashEmbeddingProvider (class: local hashing/token-based embedding fallback).  
- _OllamaEmbeddingProvider (class: HTTP-based embedding provider using Ollama).  
- _LiteLLMEmbeddingProvider (class: embedding provider integrating LiteLLM).  
- _EmbeddingProviderChain (class: manages multiple providers and failover rotation).  
- SemanticMemoryIndex (class: core index manager, syncing, search, and DB operations).  
- Methods on SemanticMemoryIndex: __init__, set_active_session, close, schedule_sync, upsert_text, search, build_context_note, _sync_worker, _ensure_db, _sync_once, _collect_workspace_documents, _collect_session_documents, _sync_documents, _upsert_document, _delete_document, _delete_chunks_for_doc, _chunk_document, _upsert_embeddings_for_chunks, _keyword_search, _vector_search, _merge_hybrid, _clear_cache.  
- Utility functions: _utcnow_iso, _normalize_embedding, _cosine_similarity, _tokenize_fts, _build_fts_query, _parse_iso_to_timestamp, _hash_text, _build_embedding_chain, create_semantic_memory_index.  
- External dependencies and notable calls: sqlite3 (persistent store and FTS5), httpx (HTTP client for Ollama), litellm (optional embedding client, imported lazily), math, json, re, threading, datetime, and logging via captain_claw.logging.get_logger.

Key logic:
1. Initialization ensures the SQLite database file and schema exist, configures parameters, builds an embedding provider chain, and schedules an initial background sync.  
2. Sync scheduling marks the index as dirty and spawns a daemon thread if no sync is running; the background thread runs _sync_worker which calls _sync_once until the index is clean.  
3. _sync_once collects document lists from the workspace (by walking the workspace_path with include/exclude rules and file size limits) and from the session DB (by reading session rows and converting messages into text), then delegates to _sync_documents.  
4. _sync_documents compares incoming documents against existing memory_documents rows using signatures; it upserts changed documents and deletes stale documents that are no longer present.  
5. Upserting a document stores metadata, deletes any prior chunks, chunks the document text into line-based pieces with a configurable character target and overlap, inserts chunks and their FTS entries, and triggers embedding upserts.  
6. Chunking iterates lines, accumulates characters until the chunk_chars target is reached, ensures at least one line per chunk, and computes overlap by walking backward to include overlap_chars worth of lines for the next chunk's start.  
7. Embedding upserts run in batches, call the embedding chain's embed_batch (which rotates providers and fails over across configured providers), normalize vectors, and store JSON-serialized embeddings with provider keys and dimensionality.  
8. Keyword search builds an FTS query from tokenized, filtered tokens, runs a MATCH query using bm25 ranking, and falls back to a LIKE-based search when FTS fails; results include a computed text_score derived from bm25.  
9. Vector search embeds the query, retrieves embeddings with the matching provider key and dimensionality, computes cosine similarity against each stored vector, sorts by vector_score, and will schedule a sync if there are no rows for the active provider (provider mismatch).  
10. The hybrid merge combines hits by chunk_id, fills missing text/vector scores, optionally replaces snippets with vector-provided text, and computes a combined score as a weighted sum of vector and text scores.  
11. If temporal decay is enabled the merged scores are multiplied by an exponential decay factor derived from document updated timestamps and a configurable half-life in days, which reduces scores for older content.  
12. Results below the configured min_score are filtered out, the remaining SemanticMemoryResult objects are sorted by score and truncated to max_results; search results are cached with a TTL to avoid recomputation on frequent identical queries.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/file_registry.py

Description:
1. This module implements a thread-safe registry mapping logical file paths to physical on-disk locations.
2. It defines a FileRegistry class that stores normalized logical paths, physical paths, and a filename index for fuzzy lookup.
3. The registry provides methods to register mappings, resolve logical paths to physical paths, and list or serialize entries.
4. Normalization removes surrounding quotes, trims whitespace, resolves path components, and strips leading slashes.
5. Resolution attempts an exact normalized match, a fallback after stripping common prefixes like "saved/", and a filename-only fuzzy match when unambiguous.
6. Registrations update both a mappings dictionary and a filename-to-logical-paths index under a threading lock.
7. The class supports merging mappings from another registry without overwriting existing entries (first-writer wins).
8. Helper methods allow building a human-readable manifest and serializing/deserializing registry state to and from dictionaries.
9. The module uses a logger for debug messages when files are registered.
10. Threading locks protect internal state to ensure safe concurrent access by multiple tasks.

Purpose:
The FileRegistry exists to decouple logical file references used by orchestration components or language model prompts from the actual session-scoped physical file locations on disk. It enables downstream tasks to access outputs produced by upstream tasks without needing to know session IDs or internal folder layouts. By maintaining normalized logical paths and a fuzzy filename index, the registry handles inconsistent or abbreviated file references that may appear across steps. Thread-safety allows a single registry instance to be shared across concurrent tasks within an orchestration run or a single-agent session. Serialization and deserialization methods permit registry state to be persisted, inspected, or included in diagnostics and tooling. The build_manifest method generates a human-readable list of available files that can be injected into prompts so an LLM knows what files are available from previous steps. The resolve_or_passthrough convenience method simplifies callers by returning the original path when no mapping is found, avoiding errors for unmapped references. Merging from another registry supports combining file sets from different contexts while preserving original writers' mappings. Normalization and prefix-stripping implement practical matching policies (e.g., removing "saved/") to increase match robustness. The compact public API (register, resolve, list_files, to_dict, from_dict, merge_from) keeps integration straightforward for orchestration components that need file lookup and provenance. Debug logging on registration assists in tracing file provenance and diagnosing mismatches during multi-step runs.

Key elements:
- FileRegistry (class) — central registry object managing mappings and index.
- __init__ (method) — initializes orchestration_id, lock, mappings dict, and filename index.
- register (method) — record a logical -> physical mapping and update filename index (logs debug).
- resolve (method) — resolve logical paths using exact match, prefix-stripped fallback, and filename-only fuzzy match.
- resolve_or_passthrough (method) — returns resolved path or original input if not found.
- list_files (method) — returns a list of registered entries as dicts with "logical" and "physical".
- build_manifest (method) — returns a human-readable, sorted manifest suitable for prompt injection.
- to_dict / from_dict (methods) — serialize and restore registry state.
- merge_from (method) — merge another registry's mappings without overwriting existing entries.
- __len__ / __bool__ (methods) — provide size and truthiness checks.
- _normalize (staticmethod) — normalizes input paths (strip quotes/whitespace, resolve components, strip leading slash).
- _strip_common_prefixes (staticmethod) — strips configured prefixes such as "saved/" for fallback matching.
- _mappings (dict) — internal normalized logical -> physical mapping store.
- _filename_index (dict) — filename -> list of logical keys for fuzzy lookup.
- _lock (threading.Lock) — protects concurrent access to internal state.
- get_logger from captain_claw.logging (external call) — used for debug logging.

Key logic:
The registry normalizes any provided logical path before use by trimming whitespace, removing surrounding quotes, splitting into path components via pathlib.Path, and stripping leading slashes to create a consistent lookup key. When register is called, the normalized logical path and the stringified physical path are stored under a lock; the filename (last path component) is used to populate a filename index that maps filenames to lists of logical keys for fuzzy resolution. register logs a debug message including the normalized logical and physical paths and an optional task_id. resolve first normalizes the input and then checks for an exact mapping in the mappings dictionary under the same lock to ensure thread safety. If no exact mapping exists, resolve attempts a fallback by stripping configured common prefixes (currently "saved/") and checking the mappings again. If still not found, resolve performs a filename-only fuzzy lookup: it retrieves the candidate logical keys from the filename index and returns a mapping only if there is exactly one candidate, avoiding ambiguous resolutions. resolve_or_passthrough simply calls resolve and returns the original path when resolve yields no mapping, providing a convenient no-op fallback for callers. list_files iterates the mappings under lock and returns a list of dictionaries containing logical and physical path pairs for inspection or consumption by other components. build_manifest constructs a sorted, human-readable multi-line string that lists available logical files alongside their on-disk hints, suitable for inclusion in LLM prompts. to_dict produces a snapshot containing the orchestration_id and a copy of mappings for persistence or debugging, while from_dict recreates a FileRegistry and re-registers entries to rebuild index structures. merge_from reads another registry's mappings while holding the other registry's lock, then inserts any keys that do not already exist in this registry (first-writer wins) and updates the filename index accordingly. Length and boolean checks are implemented to reflect the number of mappings and to allow easy truthiness testing of registry content. Overall, the logic prioritizes deterministic matching, safe concurrent updates, and simple, predictable fallbacks for LLM-driven file references.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_orchestration_mixin.py

Description:
1. This module implements orchestration logic for an agent handling complete and streaming LLM requests.  
2. It defines multiple scale-advisory templates and a helper to build advisories tailored to different output strategies.  
3. It contains heuristics and regex patterns to detect inputs that suggest large-scale list or file-processing tasks.  
4. The AgentOrchestrationMixin class provides methods to run preflight scale checks and a comprehensive complete() coroutine that drives a multi-iteration agent turn.  
5. complete() initializes per-turn state, enforces guards, constructs messages, and manages planning pipelines and iteration budgets.  
6. The mixin integrates with a tools subsystem to retrieve tool definitions, detect explicit or embedded tool calls, and execute tools under session and task policies.  
7. It supports an early micro-loop and a scale micro-loop that process items incrementally to avoid blowing the LLM context window.  
8. The file implements completion gates, validation against task contracts, and mechanisms for auto-writing or running python workers for list tasks.  
9. The module emits structured telemetry/tool_output events, persists assistant responses, and auto-captures todos, scripts, contacts, and APIs.  
10. Robust error handling and logging are included for guard blocks, LLM failures, tool fallback behaviors, and environment restoration.

Purpose:
The file centralizes high-level orchestration so that agent classes can reuse consistent, scale-aware request handling logic. It exists to detect when a user request implies large or repetitive work and to inject explicit, machine-readable guidance (scale advisories) so the LLM adopts an incremental, safe processing strategy. By formalizing the detection of list tasks and inline URL lists, the mixin helps avoid context-window exhaustion and unnecessary repeated globbing or reprocessing. The complete() coroutine is the main entry point for a user turn and is responsible for combining prompt construction, policy/guard enforcement, tool discovery, and iterative LLM interaction. It also coordinates planning pipelines and can spawn subagent contexts to enable multi-step, managed workflows. Scale progress tracking and micro-loop facilities are provided so the agent can switch from a conversational LLM loop to a direct item-by-item processing loop when appropriate. The mixin supports fallback behaviors (e.g., friendly tool-output responses, python worker auto-run) to handle script-style or large-list jobs robustly. Completion gates and task-contract validation enforce that outputs satisfy explicit requirements before finalizing a turn. Iteration budgeting, stagnation detection, and controlled extensions prevent infinite loops while allowing additional iterations when measurable progress occurs. Overall, the module exists to encapsulate complex orchestration concerns—safety, tooling, scaling, planning, and telemetry—so higher-level agent implementations remain focused on domain logic.

Key elements:
- _SCALE_ADVISORY_SINGLE_FILE, _SCALE_ADVISORY_FILE_PER_ITEM, _SCALE_ADVISORY_NO_FILE (scale advisory text templates).  
- _build_scale_advisory(item_count, output_strategy, filename_template, final_action) (helper to format the correct advisory).  
- _LARGE_SCALE_INPUT_PATTERNS (list of compiled regex patterns for detecting large-scale input language).  
- _INLINE_URL_RE (regex to count inline URLs in input).  
- AgentOrchestrationMixin (class that provides orchestration methods to an agent).  
- AgentOrchestrationMixin._input_suggests_large_scale(user_input) (heuristic to detect list/large tasks).  
- AgentOrchestrationMixin._preflight_scale_check(effective_user_input, list_task_plan) (decides whether to inject scale advisory and emits task_contract events).  
- AgentOrchestrationMixin.complete(user_input) (async coroutine implementing the full turn lifecycle and main control flow).  
- Internal helpers defined inside complete(): _restore_skill_env_once, finish, attempt_finalize_response (manage environment, finalization, and auto-write behavior).  
- Calls to external subsystem methods (examples: self.tools.list_tools, self.tools.get_definitions, self._run_scale_micro_loop, self._generate_list_task_plan, self._generate_task_contract, self._build_task_pipeline, and various _emit_* / _add_session_message / _handle_tool_calls helpers).  
- External module dependencies: get_config (for scale thresholds), GuardBlockedError (error handling), Message (LLM message wrapper), get_logger (logging).

Key logic:
1. On entry complete() ensures the agent is initialized and sets up per-turn state including usage counters, cancel events, and duplicate tool-call tracking.  
2. The method normalizes the user input, applies clarification context or rephrasing when helpful, and enforces input guards before recording the user message.  
3. It attempts to extract a structured list_task_plan (or augments it by parsing raw URLs) so the orchestration layer can treat list-processing requests specially.  
4. A preflight scale check uses both explicit member counts and text-pattern heuristics (plus URL/list-line counting) to decide whether to append a scale advisory to the prompt.  
5. If a scale advisory is activated the mixin initializes _scale_progress metadata (items, done_items, output strategy) so subsequent logic can track progress and produce percentage updates.  
6. When prepopulated items and per-member actions are available the code may early-takeover and run a micro-loop that processes items directly without invoking the main LLM loop, producing a summary afterward.  
7. Otherwise the main loop constructs messages, fetches tool definitions, and calls the LLM repeatedly within an iteration budget that can be extended when observable progress occurs.  
8. Each LLM response is inspected for explicit tool_calls, embedded tool-call patterns in content, or inline commands; detected actions are executed via guarded tool invocation and their outputs are recorded into the session.  
9. After tool execution the mixin can trigger a scale micro-loop takeover if conditions are met (e.g., scale_progress active and first items done), or let the LLM continue and follow up on tool results when supported.  
10. Completion gating logic evaluates coverage of list members, cross-references scale-progress done_items, and runs contract validation checks; failing checks generate feedback and controlled retries rather than immediate finalization.  
11. The loop maintains progress snapshots and a stagnation detector; repeated non-progress behavior causes graceful termination with an explanatory message.  
12. Finalization handles optional auto-write behavior, running python-worker workflows if required, persisting assistant output, auto-capturing artifacts (todos, contacts, scripts, APIs), emitting telemetry events, and returning the final assistant text.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/local_command_dispatch.py

Description:
1. This module implements a large async command dispatcher for local console commands.  
2. It exposes a single coroutine, dispatch_local_command, which inspects a parsed command token and performs the associated action.  
3. The function consults the runtime context, agent, and UI objects to operate on sessions, cron jobs, to‑dos, contacts, scripts, APIs, skills, and monitor settings.  
4. It recognizes commands by exact matches and by prefix checks, parsing JSON payloads or tokenized arguments when needed.  
5. For session and resource operations it delegates persistence and lookup work to agent.session_manager and enqueues longer tasks via the project's task queue helpers.  
6. Cron-related commands compute scheduling information, trigger cron monitoring events and can execute saved scripts or tools in the context of a session.  
7. Skill installation and invocation paths call agent methods that may rewrite prompts or dispatch actions, sometimes resulting in nested prompt execution.  
8. Many branches return "continue" to indicate the main loop should prompt again, "break" to exit, or None to indicate the input should be treated as a normal prompt.  
9. The module uses the UI to display success, error, warning, and system messages and to populate monitor panes.  
10. It contains extensive input validation, error handling, and small helper flows such as session procreation, export, and compaction.  

Purpose:
The file centralizes the console command handling logic that was originally embedded in an interactive loop so the rest of the application can remain modular.  
By mapping textual command tokens to asynchronous side effects it provides a single place to interpret user directives and maintain consistent UI feedback.  
It exists to translate high-level user commands into operations on sessions, persisted objects (todos, contacts, scripts, APIs), scheduled jobs, and runtime flags.  
Because many operations involve I/O and background work the dispatcher coordinates enqueuing tasks and invoking utility functions that perform the heavy lifting.  
The dispatcher enforces preconditions such as the presence of an active session, valid payloads, or enabled integrations before delegating work.  
It also centralizes common parsing patterns like JSON payload decoding and shlex-based argument splitting to produce consistent error messages.  
Integration points with cron machinery, the session orchestrator, and skill management are exposed here so console commands can trigger project-level orchestration.  
Monitor and pipeline toggles are surfaced in the same place to provide immediate feedback and to persist runtime configuration through agent APIs.  
By returning explicit control signals ("continue", "break", or None) the coroutine cleanly informs the interactive loop how to proceed after handling a command.  
This separation improves testability and allows the interactive REPL to remain focused on prompt management rather than branching logic.  
The dispatcher also records structured tool output and monitor events so other subsystems can render or persist the results.  
Overall, it exists to be the authoritative translator between textual user requests typed in the local console and the asynchronous service operations they intend to perform.  

Key elements:
- dispatch_local_command (async function) — main entrypoint that maps parsed command results to actions and returns control tokens ("break", "continue", or None).  
- ctx / agent / ui (runtime objects) — environment used throughout to access session state, queues, and presentation methods.  
- agent.session_manager (object) — used extensively for listing, selecting, creating, updating, and deleting sessions, todos, contacts, scripts, APIs, and cron jobs.  
- enqueue_agent_task, run_cancellable, dispatch_prompt_in_session, run_prompt_in_active_session (prompt/task helpers) — used to schedule or run prompts and background tasks.  
- cron helpers: cron_monitor, cron_monitor_event, execute_cron_job, parse_cron_add_args, resolve_saved_file_for_kind (cron-related utilities).  
- scheduling utilities: compute_next_run, schedule_to_text, to_utc_iso (compute and format next-run timestamps).  
- CommandLane and resolve_session_lane (execution queue abstractions) — used when enqueuing or clearing lanes.  
- approve_chat_pairing_token (platform adapter) — validates and approves chat pairing tokens for integrations.  
- export_session_history (session export helper) — used to write and return exported session files.  
- shlex, json, datetime (standard libs) — used for argument parsing, payload decoding, and timestamping.  
- UI methods referenced: print_error, print_success, print_message, print_session_info, print_session_list, print_model_list, print_cron_jobs, print_cron_job_history, load_monitor_tool_output_from_session, append_tool_output, set_monitor_mode, clear_monitor_tool_output, clear_monitor_chat_output, scroll_monitor_pane, etc.  
- SessionOrchestrator (lazily imported) — used by the "ORCHESTRATE" flow to run higher-level orchestration logic.  

Key logic:
The coroutine receives a runtime context, a parsed command token (result), and the original user_input; it then enters a large chain of conditional branches that match exact tokens or prefixes.  
For each recognized command it validates preconditions (e.g., active session present, integrations enabled), attempts to parse any JSON payload or tokenized arguments, and then delegates to the appropriate subsystem.  
Most branches respond to success or failure by emitting UI messages (success, error, warning, or system) and typically return "continue" to signal the caller to prompt again.  
Exit is handled early by returning "break" when the EXIT token is seen.  
Session management branches create, select, rename, describe, export, run prompts in, procreate, and clear sessions while updating session runtime flags and monitor panes as needed.  
Cron flows parse schedules and payloads, validate saved script/tool paths, compute next-run times, create or modify cron job records, trigger monitor events, and can manually execute cron jobs or one-off prompts.  
Resource CRUD flows (todos, contacts, scripts, APIs) call into agent.session_manager for list/select/create/update/delete and format human-readable listings or detailed info blocks for the UI.  
Skill-related branches handle catalog search, installation (from GitHub or dependency installs), invocation (dispatch mode vs prompt rewrite), and surface errors returned by agent helper methods.  
Some operations that are potentially long-running are wrapped in enqueue_agent_task to run on appropriate lanes (often CommandLane.NESTED) and use run_cancellable to allow user cancellation of orchestrations.  
Argument parsing uses json.loads for structured payloads and shlex.split for shell-like tokenization (notably in the /cron run branch), with try/except blocks to provide friendly usage errors on malformed input.  
When manipulating queues the dispatcher interacts with followup_queue and command_queue through helper functions like resolve_session_lane and update_active_session_queue_settings to reflect per-session queue policies.  
Monitoring and tracing toggles call agent methods or UI setters to change runtime behavior and then confirm the change via a success message.  
If a command is not recognized by any branch the function returns None so the interactive loop can treat the original input as a normal prompt to be executed.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/discord_bridge.py

Description:
1. This module provides a minimal bridge to Discord's REST API for polling direct messages and guild text channels and for sending messages and files.  
2. It defines a DiscordMessage dataclass to normalize incoming message payloads into a consistent structure.  
3. It wraps an httpx.AsyncClient to perform authenticated GET and POST requests to the Discord API.  
4. It includes helper methods to list DM channels and to enumerate guild text channels accessible to the bot.  
5. It caches and exposes the bot user id to detect when the bot is mentioned in messages.  
6. Its get_updates coroutine polls channels, applies per-channel offsets, filters and normalizes incoming messages, and returns new updates with updated offsets.  
7. The send_message coroutine splits large text into chunks and posts them sequentially to a channel, optionally as a reply.  
8. It implements a send_chat_action method to send a typing indicator to a channel.  
9. The send_audio_file method uploads an MP3 file as a multipart POST with an optional caption and reply reference.  
10. Throughout the module it performs basic validation, error handling, and API response status checks using response.raise_for_status.  

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a compact, reusable abstraction over Discord's HTTP API for use by the larger Captain Claw application.  
2. It centralizes token handling, base URL configuration, and the asynchronous HTTP client so other parts of the project can interact with Discord without duplicating network code.  
3. By normalizing messages into the DiscordMessage dataclass it simplifies downstream processing and decouples application logic from Discord's raw JSON payloads.  
4. The polling-oriented get_updates method implements offset tracking so the application can resume polling without reprocessing already-seen messages.  
5. Low-level request helpers (_api_get and _api_post_json) isolate HTTP mechanics and response status checking from higher-level behaviors.  
6. Channel discovery helpers enable the module to discover both direct message channels and guild text channels the bot can access.  
7. The module intentionally suppresses mentions in outgoing messages via allowed_mentions to avoid unintentionally pinging users when relaying content.  
8. Chunking logic in send_message exists to respect Discord's message length limits while attempting to preserve readability by preferring newline splits.  
9. The send_audio_file method exists to support features that produce audio output by uploading attachments as multipart form data.  
10. Caching the bot user id reduces redundant API calls and enables correct handling of messages that explicitly mention the bot.  
11. The file raises explicit errors for missing audio files and relies on response.raise_for_status to surface HTTP errors for calling code to handle.  
12. Overall, the module provides a focused integration layer so other components can consume and produce Discord messages without managing HTTP details or Discord-specific formatting logic.

Key elements:
- DiscordMessage dataclass (id, channel_id, user_id, username, text, guild_id, mentioned_bot).  
- DiscordBridge class (primary integration class encapsulating Discord functionality).  
- __init__ (initializes token, api_base_url, httpx.AsyncClient, and bot user id cache).  
- enabled property (boolean indicating whether a token is configured).  
- close coroutine (closes the httpx.AsyncClient).  
- _url and _auth_headers (helpers to build API URLs and authentication headers).  
- _api_get and _api_post_json (HTTP helpers that raise on non-success and return parsed JSON).  
- _list_dm_channels (filters user channels by Discord types for DMs).  
- _get_bot_user_id (fetches and caches the bot's user id via users/@me).  
- _list_guild_text_channels (enumerates guilds and selects text channels by type).  
- _id_to_int, _format_username, _strip_leading_mentions (utility functions for id parsing and formatting).  
- get_updates coroutine (polls channels, applies offsets, filters/normalizes incoming messages).  
- send_message coroutine (chunks and posts textual messages, supports reply reference).  
- send_chat_action coroutine (posts typing indicator).  
- mark_read coroutine (no-op placeholder for read-marking).  
- send_audio_file coroutine (uploads audio as multipart with payload_json).  
- dependency on httpx.AsyncClient and standard json and pathlib APIs.

Key logic:
1. Initialization stores the provided token and base URL, creates an httpx.AsyncClient with a fixed timeout, and prepares an empty bot id cache.  
2. The enabled property simply checks whether a token string is present to allow conditional use of the bridge.  
3. Low-level API methods (_api_get and _api_post_json) construct full URLs, attach Bot authorization headers, perform requests, call raise_for_status to surface HTTP errors, and return parsed JSON or empty dicts for no content.  
4. Channel discovery for DMs calls users/@me/channels and filters channel entries by numeric type values representing DM-like channels.  
5. Guild channel discovery first lists guilds via users/@me/guilds, then queries each guild's channels and keeps channels whose type indicates standard text or announcement channels.  
6. The bot user id is fetched from users/@me, cached on success, and returned for use in mention detection to avoid repeated API calls.  
7. get_updates builds a list of channels from DM and optionally guild channels, tracks seen channel ids, and for each channel requests recent messages with a limit and an optional after parameter sourced from current offsets.  
8. Incoming message lists are sorted by numeric id using _id_to_int to order messages chronologically before processing and to compute the last seen id per channel for next_offsets.  
9. Message filtering excludes entries without a valid author or content and ignores messages flagged as sent by bots; mention detection uses the mentions array and the cached bot id.  
10. For guild messages where the bot is mentioned, leading mention tokens are stripped from content to produce a cleaner prompt text.  
11. Normalized DiscordMessage objects are created with formatted usernames produced by _format_username which prefers global_name and falls back to username#discriminator when appropriate.  
12. After processing channels, get_updates sorts the accumulated updates by numeric id and returns them along with updated per-channel offsets for subsequent polling.  
13. send_message enforces a maximum chunk size, attempts to split on the last newline before the limit for readability, and falls back to splitting at the hard limit if necessary; it posts each chunk and attaches a message_reference for the first chunk when replying.  
14. send_chat_action posts to the typing endpoint when the action equals "typing", while mark_read is implemented as a no-op because bots cannot mark messages read.  
15. send_audio_file validates the file path, constructs a payload_json field with caption and allowed_mentions, attaches the file under files[0] with audio/mpeg content type, posts the multipart request, and raises on non-successful responses.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_session_mixin.py

Description:
1. This module defines AgentSessionMixin, a mixin that encapsulates session token accounting, message compaction, and runtime-flag synchronization for an agent.  
2. It provides utilities to count tokens using an optional provider and a safe fallback heuristic when provider counting fails.  
3. The mixin ensures per-message token metadata exists and can compute total token usage across a session.  
4. It formats conversation excerpts with truncation and total-character limits to prepare prompts for compaction summaries.  
5. The module offers both an LLM-driven summarization path using instruction templates and a deterministic fallback summary generator for resiliency.  
6. It implements destructive compaction that summarizes older messages, keeps recent context, updates compaction metadata, and persists the session.  
7. A non-destructive snapshot compaction routine performs the same summarization logic on a copied message list and returns compaction statistics.  
8. The mixin supports session memory protection toggles stored in session metadata and methods to enable or disable that protection.  
9. It can merge compacted memories from two parent sessions to create a new child session and emits monitoring/tool output throughout the process.  
10. The class also provisions isolated subagent child sessions for pipeline tasks, synchronizes runtime flags from session metadata, and exposes helpers to change pipeline and tracing modes.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to centralize and reuse session lifecycle mechanics required by agents, avoiding duplication across different agent implementations.  
2. It encapsulates token measurement and per-message bookkeeping so higher-level logic can make compaction and model-selection decisions based on accurate token accounting.  
3. By implementing both destructive and snapshot compaction, the mixin supports workflows that need to preview compaction results or actually reduce session memory.  
4. The LLM-integrated summarization path leverages instruction templates and guarded completions to produce compact conversation summaries while retaining a robust fallback path.  
5. Compaction logic is driven by configurable thresholds and ratios from the global configuration, enabling tunable memory management across deployments.  
6. The module records detailed compaction metadata to the session to assist auditing, monitoring, and potential undo/analysis operations.  
7. Procreation (merging) of sessions is provided so users or systems can create combined contexts from two existing sessions, with provenance recorded in metadata.  
8. Subagent context management ensures pipeline tasks can run in isolated or child sessions with controlled spawn depth, active-child caps, and execution-context defaults.  
9. Synchronizing runtime flags from session metadata allows per-session customization of pipeline behavior and monitoring verbosity without changing global runtime configuration.  
10. The mixin connects session-level settings to other subsystems (memory, model selection) by applying model choices or setting the active session in memory.  
11. It emits structured tool/monitoring messages during important operations to improve observability of compaction, procreation, and subagent provisioning.  
12. Overall, the module exists to provide a consistent, configurable, and resilient approach to session memory management and runtime configuration within the Captain Claw agent framework.

Key elements:
- AgentSessionMixin (class) — central mixin implementing session memory and flag helpers.  
- _count_tokens(text) — token counting with provider support and fallback heuristic.  
- _ensure_message_token_count(msg) — ensures a message dict has a token_count entry.  
- _session_token_count(messages=None) — totals tokens across a message list or current session.  
- _compact_role(role) — normalizes role labels for compaction output.  
- _format_compaction_messages(messages, max_total_chars, max_item_chars) — prepares truncated, size-limited conversation excerpts.  
- _fallback_compaction_summary(messages) — deterministic short summary generator for compaction fallback.  
- _summarize_for_compaction(messages) (async) — builds prompt and calls LLM completion with guards to produce a summary.  
- _limit_description_sentences(text, max_sentences) — sentence-capping utility for descriptions.  
- sanitize_session_description(text, max_sentences) — public wrapper for description normalization.  
- _fallback_session_description(session) — deterministic fallback session description builder.  
- generate_session_description(target_session=None, max_sentences) (async) — LLM-backed session description generator with fallback.  
- compact_session(force=False, trigger="manual") (async) — main destructive compaction routine that updates session, metadata and persists.  
- _compact_messages_snapshot(messages, trigger) (async) — non-destructive compaction returning new message list and stats.  
- is_session_memory_protected() — checks session metadata for memory protection.  
- set_session_memory_protection(enabled, persist) (async) — toggles protection metadata and persists.  
- procreate_sessions(parent_one, parent_two, new_name, persist) (async) — merges compacted memories to create a child session and persists.  
- ensure_pipeline_subagent_contexts(pipeline, task_ids) (async) — provisions per-task subagent sessions and execution_context defaults, may call session_manager.create_session.  
- _auto_compact_if_needed() (async) — convenience to trigger auto compaction when threshold exceeded.  
- _sync_runtime_flags_from_session() — loads pipeline and monitor runtime flags from session metadata and applies model selection.  
- refresh_session_runtime_flags() — public helper wrapper for runtime flag sync.  
- set_pipeline_mode(mode, persist) (async), set_planning_mode(enabled, persist) (async) — control pipeline execution mode.  
- set_monitor_trace_llm(enabled, persist) (async), set_monitor_trace_pipeline(enabled, persist) (async) — toggle monitoring trace options.  
- _add_session_message(...) — append a message to the session with token metadata and record it in memory.  
- External/dependent calls: get_config(), Message (captain_claw.llm), get_logger(), Session type hints, self.instructions.load/render, self._complete_with_guards, self.session_manager.create_session/save_session, self._emit_tool_output, self.memory, and model selection helpers (_session_model_selection, _apply_model_option, _apply_default_config_model_if_needed).

Key logic:
1. Token counting first attempts to use an injected provider's count_tokens method and falls back to a conservative length-based heuristic (len(text)//4) to ensure nonzero token estimates.  
2. Message-level token metadata is lazily populated by _ensure_message_token_count, which writes a token_count back into message dictionaries for later reuse.  
3. Formatting for compaction builds numbered, role-prefixed lines, trims internal whitespace, truncates individual items to a per-item char limit, and stops when a global max total character budget would be exceeded.  
4. Summarization uses instruction templates to construct system and user messages and invokes an async guarded completion call to an LLM, with exceptions triggering a deterministic fallback summary.  
5. Descriptive text normalization splits on sentence boundaries and caps the result to a configured maximum number of sentences to keep session descriptions concise.  
6. The compaction decision compares the session's total tokens to a threshold computed from configured max_tokens and a compaction_threshold; compaction proceeds only when the threshold is exceeded or when forced.  
7. When compacting, the algorithm iterates messages in reverse, accumulating token counts and ensuring a minimum number of recent messages are kept while respecting a target recent-token budget derived from a compaction_ratio.  
8. Old messages are summarized (via the summarization path), and a synthesized assistant message containing the summary plus compaction metadata is prepended to the kept recent messages; token counts and timestamps are updated accordingly.  
9. Session metadata for compaction counters, last trigger, before/after token counts, and message counts are updated and persisted through the session manager, and human-readable monitor output is emitted for observability.  
10. The snapshot compaction variant mirrors the destructive compaction flow but operates on a deep-copied list and returns the compacted list and statistics without mutating the original session.  
11. Procreation compacts each parent snapshot, merges the compacted message lists, creates a new child session via the session manager, sets child metadata documenting parents and stats, saves the child if requested, and emits stepwise tool output.  
12. Subagent provisioning walks a pipeline task graph, populates execution_context defaults (context id, spawn metadata, allowlists, timeouts), enforces spawn depth and active-child caps, and either assigns a virtual session id or creates a real child session using session_manager.create_session, tracking spawn state and errors.  
13. Runtime flag synchronization reads session.metadata (planning and monitor sections) to set in-memory pipeline_mode, planning_enabled, and tracing flags, updates the memory subsystem with the active session id, clears skill snapshot caches, and attempts to apply any session-specific model selection falling back to configuration defaults on failure.  
14. Several public async setters change pipeline and monitoring modes by updating session metadata timestamps and persisting through the session manager when requested.  
15. Throughout, the mixin coordinates with other agent subsystems via calls to self._emit_tool_output for monitoring, self.session_manager for persistence and creation, self.instructions for prompt templates, and self._complete_with_guards for LLM interactions, while using fallbacks and error handling to maintain resilience.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/cron_dispatch.py

Description:
1. This module implements cron scheduling, job execution, and cron history management for the application.  
2. It provides functions that emit monitoring events and chat-style history entries to both the UI and the session manager.  
3. The module resolves saved files for scripts and tools, enforcing a saved-root constraint and session-scoped directory conventions.  
4. It can enqueue and run scripts or tools inside a target agent session, temporarily switching the agent's active session and persisting tool output as session messages.  
5. A parser is included to parse the arguments for adding cron jobs, interpreting schedule tokens and distinguishing prompt, script, tool, and orchestrate kinds.  
6. There is a dedicated routine to run orchestrator workflows inline, creating a temporary SessionOrchestrator, loading a workflow, substituting variables, executing it, and shutting it down.  
7. The primary execute_cron_job function handles different job kinds, dispatching prompts, invoking scripts/tools, or running orchestrations, and it updates job status and next-run times.  
8. A background cron_scheduler_loop periodically polls for due jobs and invokes the executor for each due job.  
9. Throughout its operations the module logs events, manages a set of running job ids to avoid duplicates, and reports errors back to the UI.  
10. Error handling includes recording failures to job history and computing fallback next-run times when schedule computation is not possible.

Purpose:
The file centralizes cron-related responsibilities so scheduling decisions, job dispatching, execution, and history recording are implemented in one place. It exists to bridge stored cron job definitions in the session manager with runtime execution inside agent sessions and the UI monitoring surface. By providing saved-file resolution it enforces organization and containment rules for where scripts and tool files may be executed from, preventing paths outside the configured saved root. The module supplies higher-level primitives for enqueuing execution tasks (via enqueue_agent_task) while preserving session context and runtime flags so work runs under the correct agent session. It records structured monitor and chat events so cron activity appears both in tool-output streams and persistent cron job histories. Multiple cron job kinds are supported — prompts dispatched into sessions, shell scripts or tool runs executed in session context, and orchestrator workflows coordinating multiple agents. The orchestrate path is executed inline so the orchestrator component can manage parallelism while cron handles logging and history. Error handling and next-run computation ensure failures are recorded and jobs are rescheduled per their schedule or a safe fallback. The scheduler loop implements a lightweight polling mechanism suitable for embedding in the application loop without requiring an external cron service. The module avoids global mutable state by operating on a RuntimeContext object, making behavior explicit and testable. It interfaces with agent internals (token counting, guarded tool execution) so outputs are captured and saved back to sessions. Overall, it makes cron jobs first-class within the agent environment by integrating execution, persistence, monitoring, and safe file access.

Key elements:
- cron_monitor (function) — builds a simple payload and appends tool output to the UI for cron steps.  
- append_cron_history (async function) — forwards chat/monitor events to session_manager.append_cron_job_history.  
- cron_monitor_event (async function) — timestamped monitor event creator that records to UI and job history.  
- cron_chat_event (async function) — timestamped chat/history event creator for cron job messages.  
- resolve_saved_file_for_kind (function) — resolves and validates file paths inside the saved root; enforces category/session layout.  
- run_script_or_tool_in_session (async function) — resolves a file, composes a shell command, and enqueues execution inside a target session.  
- parse_cron_add_args (function) — parses raw /cron add arguments using shlex and parse_schedule_tokens to produce a kind and payload.  
- _run_orchestrate_cron (async function) — creates SessionOrchestrator, loads a workflow, prepares variable values, executes, and captures synthesis.  
- execute_cron_job (async function) — main job executor that routes by kind (prompt, script/tool, orchestrate), updates job status, and handles errors.  
- cron_scheduler_loop (async function) — background loop that polls get_due_cron_jobs and invokes execute_cron_job.  
- External dependencies / notable calls: get_logger, parse_schedule_tokens, compute_next_run, now_utc, to_utc_iso, schedule_to_text, truncate_history_text, CommandLane, normalize_session_id, agent.session_manager methods (load_session, save_session, append_cron_job_history, update_cron_job, get_due_cron_jobs), enqueue_agent_task, dispatch_prompt_in_session, SessionOrchestrator, agent._execute_tool_with_guard, agent._build_script_runner_command, ctx.ui methods (append_tool_output, print_message, set_runtime_status, append_tool_output, print_error).

Key logic:
Monitoring helpers build small payloads and route human-readable lines to the UI while also assembling structured events that are appended to per-job history via the session manager. Saved-file resolution first normalizes the session id, then canonicalizes the requested path; absolute paths are accepted as candidates but relative requests that begin with known categories are mapped into saved/<category>/<session>/..., while other relative requests are placed into default categories based on the requested kind. resolve_saved_file_for_kind computes candidate.resolve(), ensures the candidate is inside the saved base path, validates the category/session prefix, and rejects missing or non-file targets. Running a script/tool loads the target session, resolves the file path, attempts to derive a platform-aware runner command (falling back to a cd && ./name pattern), and defines an asynchronous inner _execute closure that performs the actual execution. The _execute closure may switch the global agent.session to the target session and refresh runtime flags, writes start messages to the session (including token counts), invokes the guarded shell tool via agent._execute_tool_with_guard, collects output or error, appends the output to the session and UI, and writes completion or failure messages back to session history. Script/tool runs are scheduled using enqueue_agent_task with a CRON lane so execution ordering and concurrency are controlled by the agent queue. Argument parsing for /cron add uses shlex.split, delegates schedule parsing to parse_schedule_tokens, converts schedule to textual form, then branches on the following token to produce structured payloads for prompt text, script/tool paths, or orchestrate workflow names. The orchestrate runner instantiates a temporary SessionOrchestrator configured from runtime config and the main agent, loads the named workflow, computes effective variable values by taking workflow defaults and overlaying provided cron variable values, executes the orchestrator to obtain a synthesis preview, records monitor/chat events, and ensures orchestrator.shutdown() is invoked. execute_cron_job guards against concurrent duplicates via ctx.cron_running_job_ids, determines the job kind, dispatches to the appropriate handler (dispatch_prompt_in_session, run_script_or_tool_in_session, or _run_orchestrate_cron), and sets success/queued flags accordingly. On success it logs and updates the job's last_run_at, next_run_at (via compute_next_run), last_status, and last_error; on failure it logs the error, records failure events, computes a fallback next-run time when necessary, and updates the job record as failed. The scheduler loop periodically sleeps for ctx.cron_poll_seconds, queries session_manager.get_due_cron_jobs with a limit, iterates over due jobs and calls execute_cron_job, and catches exceptions while supporting asyncio cancellation to stop cleanly.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_context_mixin.py

Description:
1. This module defines AgentContextMixin, a collection of helper methods that assemble prompt and message context for model calls and manage related session-scoped context.  
2. It provides utilities to extract and merge URLs and domains from message text and tool outputs.  
3. The mixin normalizes and loads tool policy payloads from session and task metadata to control tool access.  
4. It maintains and initializes layered semantic memory and an optional deep (Typesense) index for long-term retrieval.  
5. Several "auto-capture" routines scan user and assistant text and certain tool calls to persist todos, contacts, scripts, and APIs into session-managed memory.  
6. The class discovers and registers built-in and plugin tools based on configuration and available plugin files.  
7. It constructs the system prompt and various injected context notes including memory continuity, semantic/deep memory, planning, todo, contacts, scripts, apis, and scale-progress notes.  
8. The mixin includes logic to normalize persisted tool call shapes for provider compatibility and to serialize tool calls for persistence.  
9. It contains provider-specific normalization that enforces strict assistant-tool message ordering required by some providers (notably OpenAI).  
10. The central build_messages method composes the final list of Message objects, performing token-budgeted selection, normalization, and bookkeeping of the last context window.

Purpose:
1. AgentContextMixin exists to centralize and encapsulate all logic required to assemble LLM input context for an agent, keeping message construction consistent across the codebase.  
2. It ensures that contextual signals—session history, tool outputs, semantic memory, and task planning—are combined and presented to the model in a controlled, token-budget-aware manner.  
3. The mixin prevents noisy or irrelevant data from polluting the prompt by filtering historical tool outputs, applying domain-aware URL selection, and shrinking the scan window when domain signals are absent.  
4. It supports session continuity by building compact memory continuity notes and optionally emitting debug telemetry about memory selection to external listeners.  
5. The auto-capture features reduce user friction by persistently saving salient items (todos, contacts, scripts, APIs) discovered in conversation or produced by tools, enabling later retrieval and injection.  
6. Provider compatibility code (normalizing tool call shapes and enforcing message ordering) allows the same session history and tool usage model to work across different LLM backends with differing protocol constraints.  
7. The layered memory initialization ties runtime configuration to concrete memory backends and gracefully degrades if memory services are unavailable, keeping agent initialization robust.  
8. Plugin discovery and registration enable extensibility by loading third-party tool implementations from configured directories, integrating them into the tools registry with metadata.  
9. The mixin also centralizes system prompt composition and skill injection, letting other components update or contribute skills without duplicating prompt-building logic.  
10. By performing token accounting and selective inclusion of messages, the mixin protects against exceeding model context limits while prioritizing critical content (latest user turn and scale-progress notes).  
11. The module records context window statistics back into session metadata so that downstream UI or telemetry can surface how context was constructed and pruned.  
12. Overall, AgentContextMixin exists to make the agent's LLM calls reproducible, efficient, and extensible while bridging between session storage, memory systems, tools, and LLM provider idiosyncrasies.

Key elements:
- AgentContextMixin (class): container for all context assembly and auto-capture methods.  
- _extract_urls(text) (static): finds unique URLs in appearance order.  
- _merge_unique_urls(*url_lists) (static): merges lists preserving first-seen order.  
- _normalize_tool_policy_payload(raw) (static): normalizes tool-policy dict shapes.  
- _session_tool_policy_payload(), _active_task_tool_policy_payload(planning_pipeline): load tool policy from session or task graph.  
- _extract_source_links(msg, content): extracts URLs from tool arguments and content with web-fetch exceptions.  
- _extract_mentioned_domains(text), _url_matches_domains(url, domains): domain extraction and matching helpers.  
- _collect_recent_source_urls(turn_start_idx, ...): collects recent source URLs with optional domain filtering.  
- _initialize_layered_memory(): initializes semantic memory and optional deep memory.  
- _build_todo_context_note(), _refresh_todo_context_cache(), _auto_capture_todos(...): todo injection and auto-capture.  
- _refresh_contacts_context_cache(), _build_contacts_context_note(), _auto_capture_contacts(...), _auto_capture_contacts_from_tool_call(...): contacts handling.  
- _refresh_scripts_context_cache(), _build_scripts_context_note(), _auto_capture_scripts(...), _auto_capture_scripts_from_tool_call(...): scripts memory handling.  
- _refresh_apis_context_cache(), _build_apis_context_note(), _auto_capture_apis(...), _auto_capture_apis_from_tool_call(...): APIs memory handling.  
- _build_semantic_memory_note(), _build_deep_memory_note(): integrate semantic and deep memory notes.  
- initialize(): agent initialization orchestration (provider, session, memory, tools, caches).  
- _register_default_tools(), _discover_plugin_tool_files(), _register_plugin_tools(): tool registration and plugin loading.  
- _build_system_prompt(): constructs base system prompt and optional skills section.  
- _build_tool_memory_note(): selects and formats compact memory continuity note.  
- _requires_strict_tool_message_order(), _normalize_session_tool_calls(), _serialize_tool_calls_for_session(), _normalize_selected_messages_for_provider(): tool call normalization and provider-specific ordering.  
- _build_messages(...): main routine to assemble and token-budget messages into final Message objects.  
- External dependencies referenced: get_config, get_provider, set_provider, Message, ToolCall, get_logger, Tool, create_layered_memory, DeepMemoryIndex, session_manager interface methods (load_last_active_session, get_or_create_session, list_contacts, create_todo, etc.), instructions.render/load.

Key logic:
1. URL and domain utilities extract candidates from message text and tool argument dictionaries, merge them without duplication, and optionally filter by domain to keep prefetching and planner context focused.  
2. Tool policy normalization inspects arbitrary payload shapes and returns a canonical dict with allow/deny/also_allow lists or None when absent; this is used for both session- and task-scoped policies.  
3. Layered memory initialization checks configuration and session-manager paths, then attempts to construct a semantic memory object and, conditionally, a Typesense-backed deep memory index, logging and degrading to None on failures.  
4. Auto-capture routines use conservative regular expressions to detect todos, contact declarations, script mentions, and API mentions in user and assistant text; matches lead to session-manager calls to create or update records.  
5. Tool-call-driven auto-capture inspects tool arguments for write/send_mail/web_fetch usages to discover scripts, contact emails, or API endpoints and avoid duplicates by searching existing records and incrementing usage counters when appropriate.  
6. Default tool registration consults configuration to instantiate and register a curated set of tool classes; plugin discovery loads Python files from configured directories and either calls a register_tools(module) hook or instantiates Tool subclasses found in the module.  
7. System prompt construction uses a templating instructions object to render a base prompt and optionally appends skill-provided sections when present.  
8. Tool memory note selection ranks skipped historical tool messages by tokenized term overlap with the query and by recency, truncates long snippets, and emits a debug signature to the UI when selection changes.  
9. Message composition begins with a system message and then assembles candidate messages from session history and generated context notes (memory, semantic, deep, planning, list tasks, scale progress, todo, contacts, scripts, apis).  
10. A token-budgeting loop iterates over candidates in reverse chronological order, measuring token counts via internal token-count helpers and always ensuring inclusion of the latest user turn and critical scale-progress notes while dropping lower-priority items when over budget.  
11. Historical tool messages can be filtered by index; filtered tool responses are collected into a skipped list used for the memory continuity note and their tool_call ids are tracked so corresponding assistant tool_calls can be stripped to avoid orphan references.  
12. Provider compatibility normalization enforces an assistant/tool message pairing model required by some providers: it consolidates tool_calls on assistant messages, keeps tool messages that match pending tool_call ids, converts orphaned tool messages into assistant content prefixed with a tool context tag, and clears incomplete tool chains.  
13. Tool call normalization converts persisted or in-memory ToolCall objects into a consistent JSON-friendly shape expected by providers and for session persistence, serializing argument dicts into JSON strings when needed.  
14. After selection and normalization, candidate messages become Message objects with appropriate role, content, and tool metadata; the mixin records a last_context_window summary including token budgets, included/dropped counts, and whether various context notes were used.  
15. Throughout, the mixin emits structured logs and tool output debug events for memory selection and deep memory usage, and it gracefully handles exceptions from optional subsystems so agent initialization and message building remain resilient.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/cli.py

Description:
