1. This module implements a TerminalUI class that provides a command-line interface framework for the Captain Claw application.  
2. It initializes terminal behavior, readline-based history and completion, and stores UI-related runtime state and buffers.  
3. The class supports a sticky footer with a fixed system/status area and an optional split monitor view showing chat and raw tool output.  
4. Multiple print_* methods handle rendering of user, assistant, system, tool messages, token usage, errors, warnings, and other informational views.  
5. Monitor rendering logic computes layout, wraps text to pane widths, slices scrolled views, and writes directly to the terminal using ANSI cursor controls.  
6. The file contains logic to append and format tool outputs, including special summarization for web fetch results and size-limited buffering.  
7. Input handling includes a prompt method, support for streaming assistant output (begin/end stream), and ESC key capture using termios/asyncio on POSIX.  
8. A comprehensive handle_special_command method parses slash-commands (/session, /cron, /todo, /contacts, etc.) into structured return tokens or triggers printed help/errors.  
9. Footer rendering is rate-limited with FPS constraints and composes contextual status lines showing token usage, timing, session, and model details.  
10. Utility helpers manage scroll offsets, persistence of history to a file, and some provider/tool-specific behaviors through configuration access.

Purpose:
1. The primary role of this file is to provide a terminal-based user interface layer for interacting with the Captain Claw runtime.  
2. It exists to centralize all terminal formatting, input prompting, and user-visible status presentation so higher-level runtime logic can remain UI-agnostic.  
3. By encapsulating monitor and footer rendering, it enables a consistent split-screen experience with live tool trace output alongside conversational text.  
4. The TerminalUI maps many user-facing slash commands into machine-readable action tokens, simplifying how the command dispatcher interprets interactive input.  
5. Readline integration and history persistence improve the interactive experience by enabling tab completion, history recall, and durable session command logs.  
6. Streaming helpers and assistant output state management ensure the UI can render partial LLM outputs while preserving footer/system updates without visual corruption.  
7. Layout and wrapping helpers compute pane sizes from terminal dimensions and handle narrow-terminal fallbacks so the UI degrades gracefully.  
8. The file includes utility logic to truncate, summarize, and bound tool output buffers to prevent runaway memory usage in long-lived monitor mode.  
9. It also provides small user-facing conveniences like confirmation prompts, error/warning/success formatting, and compact session/model/cron printing utilities.  
10. Footer and system panel composition conveys runtime telemetry (tokens, durations, model selection) to users for transparency and debugging.  
11. Integration points (configuration access and occasional imports of agent tool mixins) connect the UI to other runtime components without embedding business logic.  
12. Overall, the module exists to offer a robust, interactive terminal front end that supports both conversational flows and developer-focused monitoring/tracing needs.

Key elements:
- TerminalUI class (primary UI implementation and state container).  
- __init__ (initializes config, buffers, layout flags, and calls _setup_readline).  
- _setup_readline (attempts to configure readline, history file, and completion).  
- _special_commands (list of slash-commands for completion).  
- print_welcome, print_help (welcome and command help rendering).  
- print_message, print_error, print_warning, print_success (role-aware printing helpers).  
- print_tool_call, print_tool_result, append_tool_output (tool output formatting and monitor integration).  
- _format_monitor_tool_body, _summarize_text, _split_web_fetch_payload (web-fetch specific summarization helpers).  
- Monitor rendering: _layout_metrics, _monitor_pane_layout, _wrap_plain_text, _slice_scrolled_lines, _render_monitor_view.  
- Scroll management: scroll_monitor_pane, _monitor_scroll_limits, _clamp_monitor_scroll_offsets, get_monitor_scroll_state.  
- Footer and status: _render_system_panel, _render_footer, print_status_line, set_runtime_status, set_thinking.  
- Streaming and prompt: begin_assistant_stream, end_assistant_stream, complete_stream_line, prompt.  
- History persistence: _history_file path and _save_history (registered via atexit).  
- Input parsing: handle_special_command (parses and validates many slash-commands, returns encoded actions).  
- ESC capture: can_capture_escape and wait_for_escape (termios/tty + asyncio reader).  
- Configuration and logging dependencies: get_config and get_logger usage, plus dynamic import of AgentToolLoopMixin inside append_tool_output.

Key logic:
1. Initialization establishes UI behavior by loading configuration, setting flags for sticky footer/ANSI, and creating buffers and scroll offsets.  
2. _setup_readline tries to import and configure readline, register a completer based on _special_commands, and persist history to a file on exit.  
3. Printing functions branch on monitor mode and sticky footer: when monitor mode is active they append to internal buffers and call _render_monitor_view, otherwise they print directly to stdout.  
4. The monitor renderer computes layout metrics from terminal size, determines left/right pane widths, wraps buffered text to pane widths, extracts the visible slice given scroll offsets, and writes rows with ANSI cursor positioning.  
5. Text wrapping uses textwrap.wrap with controlled options to avoid dropping whitespace and to break long words when necessary; trailing newline behavior is preserved.  
6. append_tool_output formats a header and body for each tool invocation, optionally summarizes web fetch outputs, clips long outputs, appends to the tool buffer, and triggers a thinking indicator for non-silent tools.  
7. The thinking indicator and runtime status are shown in the system panel; set_thinking updates inline text and forces rendering of the system panel immediately to provide real-time feedback.  
8. Footer rendering composes two status lines with left/right pieces, using _compose_footer_line to right-align metadata, and enforces a minimum interval between renders to throttle updates.  
9. handle_special_command parses slash-prefixed strings into normalized commands, validates arguments, constructs JSON payloads when needed, and returns uniform action tokens that the caller can interpret; invalid usage triggers printed errors and returns None.  
10. Scrolling operations compute page steps relative to content rows, clamp offsets within computed maxima, update internal offsets, and re-render the monitor view when running in sticky footer mode.  
11. Assistant streaming mode toggles an internal flag so output can be streamed into the chat pane without immediate footer refreshes; end_assistant_stream flushes and triggers a final footer render.  
12. POSIX ESC capture installs an asyncio reader on stdin in cbreak mode to resolve an ESC key press into a Future result, and restores terminal settings on completion or cancellation.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/google_oauth_manager.py

Description:
1. This module defines a GoogleOAuthManager class that manages Google OAuth token storage and refresh.  
2. It interacts with a SessionManager to persist tokens and Google user profile data into an app_state SQLite table.  
3. The manager caches tokens in memory and will return the cached copy when it is still valid.  
4. When stored tokens are expired, it attempts to refresh the access token using stored refresh credentials.  
5. The module exposes methods to load, store, and revoke tokens, as well as to store and retrieve user profile information.  
6. It can build an authorized_user credentials dict suitable for Vertex/LiteLLM when client credentials are available in configuration.  
7. Revocation logic tries the refresh token first and falls back to the access token where appropriate.  
8. JSON serialization/deserialization is used for persistent storage of tokens and user info, with defensive error handling on failure.  
9. External helper functions (refresh_access_token, revoke_token, fetch_user_info) are invoked for network operations.  
10. Logging is used to emit warnings and informational messages for refresh, failure, and disconnect events.

Purpose:
This file centralizes the lifecycle management of Google OAuth tokens for the application so other components can obtain valid credentials without duplicating refresh and storage logic. It exists to provide a single asynchronous interface that handles caching, persistence, refresh, and revocation of OAuth tokens while integrating with the application's SessionManager-backed app_state. By persisting tokens and user info to app_state, the manager enables tokens to survive process restarts and be shared across sessions. It also packages tokens into the specific credentials format required by Vertex/LiteLLM, bridging the gap between raw OAuth tokens and provider-specific credential expectations. The class encapsulates error-handling policies, such as returning None on deserialization or refresh failures and logging warnings rather than raising in most cases, which keeps callers simple and robust. The manager avoids unnecessary network calls by using an in-memory cache when possible, reducing latency for credential retrieval. It updates cached user profile data opportunistically after successful refreshes so downstream UI or logic can present fresh account information. Revocation behavior is implemented as best-effort to clear server-side access when disconnecting, while also ensuring local state is cleared. The file enforces dependency on application configuration for client_id and client_secret to produce Vertex credentials, preventing misuse when those values are absent. Being written with async methods, it integrates cleanly into asynchronous application flows. Overall, it provides a focused, reusable component that implements the OAuth token lifecycle concerns needed by the rest of the project.

Key elements:
- GoogleOAuthManager (class; orchestrates token lifecycle and storage)  
- __init__ (constructor; accepts SessionManager and initializes cache)  
- get_tokens (async; loads tokens from session storage, deserializes, refreshes if expired)  
- store_tokens (async; persists tokens JSON to app_state and updates in-memory cache)  
- store_user_info (async; persists Google user profile JSON to app_state)  
- get_vertex_credentials (async; returns authorized_user credentials dict using config client_id/client_secret)  
- get_user_info (async; returns cached user profile by reading app_state)  
- is_connected (async; reports whether valid or refreshable tokens exist)  
- disconnect (async; revokes tokens and clears stored OAuth state)  
- _try_refresh (async; attempts refresh via refresh_access_token, stores fresh tokens, updates user info)  
- External calls/dependencies: get_config (config access), refresh_access_token, revoke_token, fetch_user_info (network helpers), GoogleOAuthTokens (type with from_dict/to_dict/is_expired/to_vertex_credentials_json), SessionManager methods get_app_state/set_app_state/delete_app_state, logging via get_logger

Key logic:
1. Token retrieval first checks an in-memory cached GoogleOAuthTokens instance; if present and not expired it is returned immediately to avoid I/O.  
2. If no valid cache exists, get_tokens reads a JSON blob from session app_state using a predefined STATE_KEY_TOKENS key and attempts to deserialize into GoogleOAuthTokens.  
3. Deserialization failures are caught, logged as warnings, and result in returning None to indicate no usable tokens.  
4. When deserialized tokens report as expired, get_tokens delegates to _try_refresh to obtain fresh access credentials; failures in refresh return None.  
5. _try_refresh requires a refresh_token and application client credentials from config; if either is missing it logs and aborts the refresh attempt.  
6. On successful refresh, _try_refresh persistently stores the fresh tokens via store_tokens and tries to fetch and persist updated user profile info, treating user-info fetch failures as non-critical.  
7. store_tokens serializes the GoogleOAuthTokens to JSON, writes it to app_state with set_app_state, and updates the in-memory cache.  
8. get_vertex_credentials uses the tokens returned by get_tokens and the configured client_id/client_secret to build a Vertex-compatible authorized_user credentials JSON via GoogleOAuthTokens.to_vertex_credentials_json; it returns None when tokens or config are missing.  
9. disconnect performs best-effort token revocation by calling revoke_token on the refresh token if available, otherwise on the access token, then clears the cache and deletes both token and user app_state entries.  
10. is_connected is a lightweight convenience that treats presence of tokens and a refresh_token as an indicator of a connected state.  
11. get_user_info simply reads the stored user JSON from app_state and returns a parsed dict or None on error.  
12. Throughout the flow, the module uses logging to record important events (successful refresh, failed refresh, disconnection) and avoids raising exceptions for recoverable OAuth lifecycle issues, preferring to return None so callers can handle absent credentials.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/remote_command_handler.py

Description:
1. This module provides unified remote command and message handling for chat platforms like Telegram, Slack, and Discord.  
2. It defines helper functions to format recent session history and active configuration text for remote responses.  
3. A remote_help_text helper composes a platform-specific help listing from command specs on the runtime context.  
4. The core function handle_remote_command parses incoming command text, routes many application-specific commands, and sends text replies via a provided send_text callback.  
5. handle_remote_command supports commands for session management, pipeline mode, skills, scripts, to-dos, contacts, APIs, orchestration, and configuration inspection.  
6. It interacts extensively with the agent and its session_manager to query, create, update, and delete domain objects.  
7. Per-platform dispatch is implemented in handle_platform_message which adapts raw platform messages using PlatformAdapter and mediates monitoring and permission checks.  
8. handle_platform_message strips bot mentions from slash commands, enforces approved user pairing, and distinguishes slash commands from normal chat messages.  
9. Slash commands are executed through handle_remote_command wrapped in adapter.run_with_typing to show typing status and to forward assistant output back to the platform.  
10. The module includes robust error handling that logs errors, reports handler failures to the monitoring system, and sends error messages back to the chat when possible.  

Purpose:
This file centralizes the logic for interpreting and executing remote chat commands so platform-specific adapters do not need to implement command semantics.  
It exists to map textual slash commands and normal chat messages into operations on the agent, its session manager, and other core services.  
By providing format helpers, it standardizes how session history and configuration are presented to remote users.  
It delegates execution of prompts and long-running tasks to prompt_execution utilities while handling immediate command responses itself.  
The handler also enforces platform-level constraints such as guild mention requirements for Discord and pairing/approval for unknown users.  
It integrates monitoring hooks via PlatformAdapter.monitor_event to record incoming messages and handler errors.  
Command parsing is centralized so new commands or command translations can be added in one module.  
The module coordinates skill installation, invocation, and searching by calling agent methods and returning human-readable summaries.  
It manipulates persistent artifacts (sessions, scripts, todos, contacts, APIs) through the agent.session_manager and surfaces results to the user.  
For chat flows it orchestrates typing indicators, assistant text streaming, and optional audio delivery via adapter callbacks.  
Error handling and monitoring in this layer minimize exposure of internal errors to platform clients and ensure operator visibility.  
Overall, it provides a stable translation layer between external chat protocols and the application's agent-centric runtime operations.  

Key elements:
- format_recent_history (formats a compact text summary of recent session messages).  
- format_active_configuration_text (renders active model, workspace, pipeline and guard settings).  
- remote_help_text (builds help text from ctx.telegram_command_specs for a given platform label).  
- handle_remote_command (async function that parses and executes many slash commands; primary command dispatcher).  
- handle_platform_message (async function that adapts platform messages, enforces pairing, and routes slash vs normal chat).  
- PlatformAdapter (external adapter used for sending, monitoring, marking read, pairing, typing, and audio delivery).  
- truncate_chat_text (helper imported from platform_adapter to truncate previews used in monitoring).  
- get_config (configuration accessor used by formatting helpers).  
- log (logging facility used in exception handling).  
- enqueue_agent_task and run_prompt_in_active_session (prompt_execution utilities used to run orchestrations and dialogue tasks).  
- SessionOrchestrator (instantiated for orchestration requests within handle_remote_command).  
- agent and agent.session_manager (used extensively for session, skills, scripts, todos, contacts, and APIs operations).  
- JSON parsing (json.loads used to accept structured payloads for several commands).  
- adapter.run_with_typing, adapter.send, adapter.monitor_event, adapter.mark_read, adapter.pair_unknown_user, adapter.maybe_send_audio_for_turn (adapter methods used to interact with platforms and report status).  

Key logic:
The module first defines small formatters that produce human-readable summaries of session history and active configuration for remote replies.  
handle_remote_command lowercases and trims incoming raw_text, handles built-in short commands like /start and /help, and delegates many structured commands through a ui.handle_special_command hook.  
When ui.handle_special_command returns special tokens, the dispatcher interprets them to perform actions such as toggling pipeline modes, orchestrating tasks, or mapping to internal verbs for skills and resource management.  
For orchestrate requests it builds a SessionOrchestrator and enqueues its orchestration call via enqueue_agent_task, then sends the orchestrator's response back to the user and shuts it down.  
Skill-related flows parse JSON payloads or argument strings, support search/install/invoke flows, and either return immediate text results or transform invocation responses into prompts executed in the active session.  
Session management commands create, select, rename, clear, compact, and inspect sessions by calling agent.session_manager methods and then informing the requesting user of outcomes.  
To-do, contacts, scripts, and APIs are each handled by a group of commands that parse payloads or inline arguments, call the appropriate session_manager CRUD methods, and render summary lines describing the resulting data.  
Input that requires updating records often uses shlex splitting to parse key=value pairs, filters them against valid field names, and passes the resulting kwargs to update_* methods on the session manager.  
When a slash command is unhandled for remote platforms the function explicitly responds that the command requires the local console, preventing accidental exposure of local-only operations.  
handle_platform_message creates a PlatformAdapter for the incoming message, performs platform-specific checks (e.g., Discord guild mention requirement), marks the message as read, and emits monitoring events with a truncated preview.  
It enforces user approval by checking state.approved_users and triggers pairing for unknown users; it also strips @BotName suffixes from slash commands to normalize command tokens.  
Depending on whether the message is a slash command or normal chat, the handler either runs handle_remote_command (wrapped in adapter.run_with_typing) or starts a prompt run via run_prompt_in_active_session, wiring adapter callbacks to stream assistant text and optionally send audio; all of this is guarded by try/except logic that logs errors, reports handler_error events, and attempts to notify the user of failures.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent.py

Description:
1. This module defines the Agent class which orchestrates runtime behavior for Captain Claw.  
2. Agent composes many mixins to provide features like orchestration, file operations, context management, guarding, model interfacing, pipeline control, reasoning, session handling, skills, and tool loops.  
3. The constructor accepts optional LLM provider and several callback hooks and then configures the tool registry, runtime and workspace paths, and a session manager.  
4. The agent initializes usage tracking buckets, monitoring flags, instruction loading, and other runtime bookkeeping such as provider override and model detail caches.  
5. Utility methods create empty usage containers and accumulate token usage from provider responses.  
6. Helper methods forward runtime status and inline "thinking" messages to configured callbacks while protecting against callback exceptions.  
7. A small helper determines monitor-only tool names that should not be added to model context.  
8. Tool output handling can record tool outputs into the active session, emit pipeline trace payloads when configured, and call an external tool output callback.  
9. The agent exposes an asyncio cancellation event intended for external UI layers to cancel long-running orchestrations.  
10. Overall, the file focuses on wiring runtime components, tracking resource usage, and mediating interactions among tools, sessions, and UI callbacks.

Purpose:
This file exists to centralize and encapsulate the top-level orchestration responsibilities of an Agent instance within the Captain Claw project. It provides a single class that wires together many orthogonal capabilities through mixins so that higher-level flows (planning, tool execution, session management) can rely on a consistent runtime surface. The constructor sets up dependencies such as the LLM provider, tool registry, session manager, and resolved workspace paths so other components do not need to duplicate that configuration logic. Usage accounting helpers are included so token consumption can be tracked per-turn and aggregated globally for reporting or limits. Callback forwarders (status, thinking, tool output, approval) let UI or integration layers receive incremental updates without coupling the orchestration logic to specific presentation code. The monitor-only tool name filter prevents certain tools from polluting model context, supporting observable tracing without affecting reasoning. The file registry and instruction loader initialization enable consistent cross-task file handling and instruction resolution for multi-step workflows. Cancellation support via an asyncio.Event gives the UI a mechanism to interrupt loops gracefully. The module also stores runtime flags and caches (e.g., pipeline mode, planning toggle, provider override, model details) that influence orchestration behavior across different runs. By composing behavior through mixins, this Agent class remains extensible and focused on coordination while delegating specialized behaviors to their respective mixins.

Key elements:
- Agent class (main orchestrator composed from multiple mixins).  
- __init__ (constructor) (initializes provider, callbacks, tools, paths, session manager, flags, and caches).  
- _empty_usage (static method) (creates a token usage bucket).  
- _is_monitor_only_tool_name (static method) (normalizes and checks if a tool is monitor-only).  
- _accumulate_usage (static method) (adds prompt/completion/total token counts into a target).  
- _finalize_turn_usage (method) (persists last turn usage and aggregates totals).  
- _set_runtime_status (method) (forwards status strings to status_callback safely).  
- _emit_thinking (method) (forwards inline reasoning/thinking updates to thinking_callback safely).  
- _emit_tool_output (method) (records certain tool outputs into session and calls tool_output_callback; emits pipeline trace messages when enabled).  
- tools (ToolRegistry instance obtained via get_tool_registry).  
- session_manager (Session manager obtained via get_session_manager).  
- cancel_event (asyncio.Event used to cancel orchestrations).  
- instructions (InstructionLoader instance).  
- External dependencies (get_config, FileRegistry, InstructionLoader, LLMProvider, get_session_manager, get_tool_registry, Session, Path, asyncio).

Key logic:
1. During initialization the Agent sets provided callbacks and the LLM provider reference, then acquires the global tool registry and applies the approval callback to it.  
2. The runtime base path is resolved from the current working directory and the workspace path is derived via configuration to determine where file operations should execute.  
3. The tools registry is informed of the runtime workspace so tools that operate on files can resolve paths consistently.  
4. A session manager is fetched and stored; the active session begins as None until session lifecycle methods (in mixins) create or attach one.  
5. The agent sets up token usage tracking with empty buckets for last and total usage and holds a dictionary for context window measurements and other debug signatures.  
6. Monitoring flags and pipeline mode settings are configured from provided configuration values so tracing and pipeline behavior can be toggled at runtime.  
7. _empty_usage returns a zeroed token count map; _accumulate_usage reads numeric prompt/completion values, computes totals, and safely accumulates them into target totals.  
8. _finalize_turn_usage assigns the provided turn usage to last_usage and invokes _accumulate_usage to update the persistent total_usage.  
9. _set_runtime_status and _emit_thinking simply invoke the configured callbacks with try/except around the calls to prevent callback exceptions from bubbling into orchestration logic.  
10. _is_monitor_only_tool_name normalizes a tool name string and checks membership in a fixed set of tool identifiers that are treated as trace/monitor-only.  
11. _emit_tool_output first checks for special tool names (planning, task_contract, task_rephrase, completion_gate) and if present, appends the raw output to the session as a tool message and optionally creates a pipeline_trace payload when pipeline tracing is enabled.  
12. After session recording, _emit_tool_output will call the external tool_output_callback with the tool name, arguments, and output, again guarding the call in a try/except to avoid propagation of errors to the orchestrator.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/slack_bridge.py

Description:
1. This module implements a minimal Slack Web API bridge focused on direct message polling and message sending.  
2. It defines a SlackMessage dataclass that normalizes incoming Slack payloads with fields for channel id, message timestamp, user id, username, text, and optional thread timestamp.  
3. The SlackBridge class wraps an httpx.AsyncClient and the Slack API base URL and token to perform authenticated asynchronous HTTP requests.  
4. It centralizes low-level request logic in helper methods that build URLs, headers, and perform GET/POST requests while validating Slack's "ok" response field.  
5. The bridge maintains an in-memory user ID → display name cache to reduce repeated users.info calls.  
6. A paginated listing of IM channels is implemented to discover direct-message conversations via conversations.list.  
7. The get_updates method retrieves conversation history per DM, filters out non-user and bot messages, sorts by timestamp, and returns normalized SlackMessage objects plus updated per-channel offsets.  
8. Sending messages is handled by splitting large texts into safe-sized chunks and posting each chunk to chat.postMessage, optionally in a thread.  
9. The module implements best-effort helpers for signaling typing/read state using conversations.mark and a method for uploading audio files to Slack via files.upload.  
10. Error handling propagates API errors for GET/POST helper calls while some higher-level interactions swallow exceptions to provide best-effort behavior.

Purpose:
This file exists to encapsulate all direct interactions with the Slack Web API required by a DM-first bot workflow. It centralizes connection configuration (token and base URL) and the httpx.AsyncClient lifecycle so higher-level components do not need to manage HTTP details. The SlackMessage dataclass provides a simple normalized structure that other parts of the application can consume consistently. Username resolution and caching reduce redundant network calls and present human-friendly names to the rest of the system. The paginated conversation listing and history retrieval implement the polling semantics needed to detect new direct messages across multiple IM channels. get_updates returns both new messages and updated offsets so callers can persist and resume polling state. The send_message chunking logic exists to avoid hitting Slack message size limits and to preserve message structure by preferring splits at newlines. Best-effort methods like send_chat_action and mark_read provide UX-friendly behavior while avoiding hard failures when the Slack API lacks stable endpoints for typing. The send_audio_file method enables sending local MP3 files as Slack uploads and performs basic file validation before attempting to upload. Centralizing Slack API error checking in _api_get and _api_post ensures consistent error semantics across all high-level operations. Overall, the module is designed to be a small, dependable adapter that exposes a simple async interface for polling, sending, and basic channel operations without embedding business logic or state management beyond username caching and per-channel offsets.

Key elements:
- SlackMessage (dataclass) — normalized incoming message payload structure.  
- SlackBridge (class) — main adapter encapsulating Slack interactions.  
- __init__ (SlackBridge) — initializes token, api_base_url, httpx.AsyncClient, and user cache.  
- enabled (property) — boolean indicating presence of a token.  
- close (async method) — closes the underlying httpx client.  
- _url, _headers (helpers) — construct endpoint URL and Authorization header.  
- _api_get, _api_post (async helpers) — perform HTTP GET/POST, validate response JSON and Slack "ok" field.  
- _resolve_username (async method) — resolves user display name via users.info and caches results.  
- _list_dm_channels (async method) — paginates conversations.list to enumerate direct-message channels.  
- _ts_to_float (static) — safe conversion of Slack timestamp strings to float.  
- get_updates (async method) — polls conversations.history, filters and sorts messages, returns SlackMessage list and offsets.  
- send_message (async method) — chunks large text and posts via chat.postMessage, supports thread replies.  
- send_chat_action (async method) — best-effort typing signal implemented via conversations.mark.  
- mark_read (async method) — best-effort mark read via conversations.mark.  
- send_audio_file (async method) — validates Path and uploads file via files.upload.  
- External dependency: httpx.AsyncClient (for async HTTP).  
- Slack endpoints used: conversations.list, conversations.history, users.info, chat.postMessage, conversations.mark, files.upload.

Key logic:
1. Initialization records the token and API base URL, constructs an AsyncClient with a 40-second timeout, and prepares an empty username cache.  
2. The enabled property is a simple truth test on the configured token to allow callers to skip Slack operations when no token is present.  
3. Low-level request methods _api_get and _api_post centralize HTTP calls, call response.raise_for_status(), parse JSON, ensure the payload is a dict, and require payload["ok"] to be True; otherwise they raise RuntimeError.  
4. URL and header construction helpers ensure consistent Authorization headers and normalized endpoint paths for all requests.  
5. Username resolution checks the cache first, then calls users.info; it extracts display_name, real_name, or name in that order and caches empty strings on failure to avoid repeated lookups.  
6. The DM channel enumerator _list_dm_channels loops with a cursor to call conversations.list repeatedly, collects channel dicts, and respects Slack pagination via response_metadata.next_cursor.  
7. get_updates takes an offsets map and an optional per-channel limit, lists DM channels, and for each channel requests conversation history with optional oldest param to limit returned messages.  
8. Messages from history are normalized by ensuring dict shape, filtered to skip empty text, missing user, and subtypes like bot_message, message_changed, and message_deleted, and are converted into SlackMessage objects with resolved usernames.  
9. Timestamps are handled by _ts_to_float to allow sorting and comparison; get_updates computes last_seen_ts per channel and returns next_offsets to let callers persist polling state.  
10. send_message implements a chunking algorithm with a max_len of 3500 characters: it prefers to split at the last newline before the limit but falls back to a hard split if that newline is too early, then posts each chunk and attaches thread_ts only for the first chunk when replying.  
11. send_chat_action and mark_read are implemented as best-effort operations that call conversations.mark and swallow exceptions to avoid failing the caller when Slack lacks stable typing endpoints.  
12. send_audio_file validates the provided file path (exists and is a file), opens it in binary mode, and uploads it as "audio/mpeg" using files.upload with appropriate metadata fields; it raises FileNotFoundError if validation fails.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/deep_memory.py

Description:
1. This module provides a Typesense-backed deep memory implementation for long-term searchable content.  
2. It defines a DeepMemoryResult dataclass that represents a single search hit with metadata like doc_id, source, path, snippet, scores, and timestamps.  
3. A collection schema template for Typesense is declared to specify fields, facets, token separators, and default sorting.  
4. Helper functions include a deterministic short-hash generator for IDs and a line-based overlapping text chunker used to split documents.  
5. The DeepMemoryIndex class encapsulates configuration, a lazy httpx.Client, and methods to manage a Typesense collection.  
6. Indexing methods include index_document for auto-chunking and embedding text, index_batch for bulk upserts, and an internal _upsert_batch that sends JSONL to Typesense.  
7. An embedding helper _embed invokes a provided embedding_chain when enabled to compute vector representations.  
8. Search supports hybrid BM25 and optional vector queries, converting Typesense hits into DeepMemoryResult objects.  
9. A build_context_note method formats search results into a text block suitable for LLM prompt injection along with a debug block.  
10. Deletion helpers and a close method complete the lifecycle by allowing document removal and HTTP client shutdown.  

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a persistent, long-term archive layer for searchable content that complements an in-memory or SQLite-backed semantic memory.  
2. It centralizes Typesense collection management so the rest of the application can index, search, and delete long-term documents without dealing with HTTP details.  
3. By handling chunking and optional embedding, it ensures large documents are split into consistent chunks that align with other memory layers.  
4. The auto-embedding integration lets the index store vector representations when an embedding chain is available, enabling hybrid text + vector search.  
5. Its upsert and batch indexing logic provide efficient ingestion paths for both programmatic calls and manual tool-based indexing.  
6. Search results are normalized to a consistent dataclass so callers receive typed results with combined scoring and metadata.  
7. The build_context_note method exists to produce concise context snippets that can be injected into LLM prompts without callers needing to format the results.  
8. Ensure_collection abstracts collection creation and schema management, including adding an embedding field if dimensions are configured.  
9. Error handling around HTTP calls and embeddings is conservative: failures in embedding or remote requests are logged and often result in empty fallbacks.  
10. Delete helpers let higher-level components purge documents either by a doc_id or arbitrary Typesense filters.  
11. A lazy HTTP client and a close method manage network resources so the index can be long-lived without leaking connections.  
12. Overall, the module exists to offer a reusable, testable interface for long-term searchable memory backed by Typesense for the agent or application.  

Key elements:
- DeepMemoryResult (dataclass for search hit metadata).  
- _COLLECTION_SCHEMA_TEMPLATE (Typesense collection schema template dict).  
- _hash_id(text) (short deterministic SHA1-based ID generator).  
- _chunk_text(text, chunk_chars, chunk_overlap_chars) (line-based overlapping chunker).  
- DeepMemoryIndex (main class encapsulating Typesense interactions and memory logic).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.__init__ (stores config: host, port, api_key, collection_name, embedding dims, chunk sizes, embedding_chain).  
- DeepMemoryIndex._get_client (lazy httpx.Client creator with Typesense headers).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.ensure_collection (checks/creates Typesense collection and schema).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.index_document (auto-chunks text, builds docs, optionally embeds, upserts).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.index_batch (accepts prebuilt documents, optionally embeds missing vectors, upserts).  
- DeepMemoryIndex._upsert_batch (JSONL upsert to Typesense import endpoint and success counting).  
- DeepMemoryIndex._embed (uses provided embedding_chain.embed_batch when enabled; returns vectors or empty on failure).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.search (hybrid BM25 + optional vector search, converts hits to DeepMemoryResult).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.build_context_note (formats top search hits into a note and a debug block for LLM prompts).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.delete_document / delete_by_filter (delete via Typesense documents endpoint using filter_by).  
- DeepMemoryIndex.close (closes the httpx client).  
- Dependencies: httpx (HTTP client), time, hashlib, json, and a pluggable embedding_chain interface.  

Key logic:
1. Initialization captures all configuration parameters (Typesense host/port/protocol, API key, collection name, embedding dimensions, chunk sizing, and an optional embedding_chain) and defers network setup by keeping _client None until needed.  
2. A lazy HTTP client is created by _get_client, which constructs an httpx.Client with a 30s timeout and Typesense API key header to reuse connections across operations.  
3. ensure_collection first probes the collection via a GET and only constructs and POSTs a schema when the collection is not present; the schema conditionally includes a float[] embedding field when embedding_dims is set.  
4. _chunk_text implements a consistent, line-aware chunking algorithm with overlap: it accumulates lines until a character budget is reached, emits a chunk, and computes an overlap region to preserve context between adjacent chunks.  
5. index_document calls _chunk_text to split text, builds per-chunk document dicts with metadata (id, doc_id, source, path, lines, timestamps), and collects texts for embedding when enabled.  
6. The embedding step (_embed) checks auto_embed and the presence and enabled flag on embedding_chain, then calls embed_batch(texts) and returns vectors, swallowing exceptions and logging failures to avoid breaking indexing.  
7. _upsert_batch serializes the list of document dicts into JSONL and posts it to the Typesense import endpoint with action=upsert, then parses each response line to count successes and logs a warning if some documents failed.  
8. index_batch handles preformed documents by embedding only those with text but missing an embedding field, then calls the same _upsert_batch path to persist them.  
9. search builds query parameters for Typesense (q/query_by/per_page and optional filter_by), auto-generates a vector_query by embedding the query text when possible, and issues a GET to the documents/search endpoint.  
10. Search post-processes Typesense hits by extracting document fields and metrics (text_match and vector_distance), computing a combined score that favors text matches but inverts vector distance, and returning DeepMemoryResult instances.  
11. build_context_note invokes search, truncates long snippets to max_snippet_chars, composes a human-readable note listing source, location, and score for each hit, and also produces a debug block with per-hit diagnostics for developer use.  
12. Deletion methods call the Typesense documents delete endpoint with filter expressions to remove documents by doc_id or arbitrary filters, return the number deleted, and close cleans up the HTTP client to release network resources.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/exceptions.py

Description:
1. This module defines custom exception types used across the Captain Claw project.  
2. It declares a single base exception CaptainClawError that all other custom errors inherit from.  
3. Specialized subclasses cover configuration, LLM interactions, tool execution, sessions, context management, validation, and guard-related failures.  
4. LLMAPIError extends LLMError and stores an optional HTTP-like status_code alongside the error message.  
5. Tool-related exceptions include ToolError and more specific ToolExecutionError, ToolNotFoundError, and ToolBlockedError that attach tool_name and reason metadata.  
6. SessionNotFoundError extends SessionError and records a missing session_id in its instance.  
7. ContextOverflowError captures current and maximum token counts when a context window is exceeded.  
8. GuardBlockedError represents policy or guard rejections and preserves a guard_type to indicate the blocking mechanism.  
9. Several classes use simple __init__ methods to format human-readable messages while storing additional attributes for programmatic inspection.  
10. The module contains no external dependencies and focuses solely on exception definitions and lightweight attribute assignment.  

Purpose:
1. The file exists to centralize and standardize error handling across the codebase by providing a clear hierarchy of exception types.  
2. By grouping errors into semantic categories (configuration, LLM, tools, sessions, context, validation, guard), other modules can catch and respond to classes of failures rather than relying on generic exceptions.  
3. Several exception classes carry structured metadata (for example status_code, tool_name, reason, session_id, token counts, guard_type) to enable richer logging, diagnostics, and programmatic decision making.  
4. Formatting descriptive messages in constructors ensures that raised exceptions produce consistent human-readable output for observability and debugging.  
5. The presence of fine-grained tool exceptions allows tool orchestration layers to differentiate between missing tools, execution failures, and policy-blocked attempts.  
6. LLM-specific exceptions provide a pathway to convey API-level failures such as rate limits or authorization issues by surfacing an optional numeric status code.  
7. Session and context-related exceptions help session management components detect and react to missing state or token budget violations.  
8. GuardBlockedError encapsulates guard decisions so higher-level logic can treat guarded actions distinctly from functional errors.  
9. The exception types facilitate mapping internal failures to external responses or retry policies in integration layers without inspecting message strings.  
10. Because the module is dependency-free and lightweight, it can be imported widely without risking circular imports or heavy coupling.  
11. Overall, the file exists to improve code clarity, error handling robustness, and maintainability by providing a single source of truth for the project's error taxonomy.  
12. The design anticipates common operational needs such as logging, monitoring, and conditional handling based on error attributes rather than raw messages.  

Key elements:
- CaptainClawError (base exception class).  
- ConfigurationError (configuration-related subclass).  
- LLMError (base class for LLM-related errors).  
- LLMAPIError (stores message and optional status_code).  
- ToolError (base class for tool-related errors).  
- ToolExecutionError (formats message and stores tool_name).  
- ToolNotFoundError (indicates missing tool and stores tool_name).  
- ToolBlockedError (indicates blocked tool execution and stores tool_name and reason).  
- SessionError (base class for session-related errors).  
- SessionNotFoundError (stores session_id of missing session).  
- ContextError (base class for context/window errors).  
- ContextOverflowError (stores current_tokens and max_tokens).  
- ValidationError (generic validation failure).  
- GuardBlockedError (stores guard_type and message indicating a guard blocked an action).  

Key logic:
1. The module establishes a simple inheritance hierarchy with CaptainClawError at the root so that catch-all and specific catches are both supported.  
2. Most subclasses are declarative and contain no additional logic beyond inheritance and optional attribute initialization.  
3. LLMAPIError defines an __init__ that calls the base Exception initializer with the provided message and then stores status_code as an instance attribute.  
4. ToolExecutionError formats a message that includes the tool name and failure message and retains the tool_name for programmatic access.  
5. ToolNotFoundError and ToolBlockedError both set human-readable messages and preserve identifying attributes such as tool_name and reason to guide handling.  
6. SessionNotFoundError constructs a message indicating the missing session and stores the session_id for downstream logic to reference.  
7. ContextOverflowError computes and stores current_tokens and max_tokens and formats an informative message reflecting the overflow condition.  
8. GuardBlockedError stores a guard_type along with the provided message so callers can distinguish between different guard mechanisms.  
9. The module relies entirely on attribute assignment and string formatting inside constructors rather than complex control flow or external I/O.  
10. Because exceptions are simple objects, they are intended to be raised and caught in other components where the contained attributes inform response behavior.  
11. There are no helper functions or side effects; the file's runtime behavior is limited to class definitions and their initialization semantics when instances are created.  
12. This minimal, explicit approach ensures exceptions are lightweight, serializable by standard mechanisms if needed, and easy to inspect during error handling and logging.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/google_oauth.py

Description:
1. This module implements Google OAuth2 helpers targeted at obtaining credentials usable with Vertex AI and LiteLLM.  
2. It defines constants for Google OAuth2 endpoints and a set of default scopes used for authorization.  
3. The GoogleOAuthTokens dataclass encapsulates access, refresh, id token, expiry, and scope information with helper methods.  
4. A PKCE helper generate_pkce_pair produces a code verifier and an S256 code challenge suitable for the Authorization Code flow.  
5. build_authorization_url constructs the authorization endpoint URL including optional state and PKCE code challenge parameters.  
6. exchange_code_for_tokens performs an async POST to the token endpoint to exchange an authorization code for tokens and computes an expires_at timestamp.  
7. refresh_access_token performs an async refresh-token grant and returns a GoogleOAuthTokens instance, preserving the original refresh token.  
8. fetch_user_info performs an authenticated async GET to Google’s userinfo endpoint and returns the parsed JSON profile.  
9. revoke_token tries to revoke an access or refresh token with Google, returning True on HTTP 200 and logging warnings on exceptions.  
10. The module uses httpx.AsyncClient for HTTP requests, standard library crypto utilities for PKCE, and a module-level logger for warnings.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to centralize and encapsulate Google OAuth2 logic required to authenticate against Google APIs and to produce credentials consumable by Vertex AI/LiteLLM.  
2. It provides a small, focused API for the common OAuth flows required by the application: building authorization URLs, exchanging codes, refreshing tokens, fetching user info, and revoking tokens.  
3. By packaging token data in GoogleOAuthTokens it standardizes token handling, expiry checks, serialization, and conversion to the "authorized_user" format expected by downstream libraries.  
4. The PKCE utilities support a secure Authorization Code flow with S256 code challenges to avoid exposing client secrets in insecure contexts.  
5. The authorization URL builder abstracts away parameter encoding details and ensures scopes, access_type, and prompt settings are consistently applied.  
6. Async token exchange and refresh functions centralize HTTP interaction details (timeouts, POST payload shape, response parsing) so callers don’t duplicate that behavior.  
7. fetch_user_info and revoke_token encapsulate specific Google endpoints and headers, keeping higher-level code free of hard-coded URLs and HTTP plumbing.  
8. Constants for app-state keys (STATE_KEY_TOKENS, STATE_KEY_USER) are provided to allow persistent storage managers (e.g., GoogleOAuthManager referenced in comments) to store and retrieve OAuth state consistently.  
9. The module intentionally delegates HTTP error propagation (via resp.raise_for_status) for most operations so calling code can handle failures, while best-effort revocation logs and returns False rather than raising.  
10. Conversion to a Vertex/LiteLLM-friendly credentials dict is provided to bridge this module with authentication consumers that expect the "authorized_user" format.  
11. Use of typed dataclasses, small helpers, and clear function boundaries makes the module suitable for reuse in different parts of the application that require Google authentication.  
12. Overall, the file exists to hide protocol specifics and provide reliable, testable primitives for integrating Google OAuth2 into the project.

Key elements:
- GOOGLE_AUTH_URL, GOOGLE_TOKEN_URL, GOOGLE_USERINFO_URL, GOOGLE_REVOKE_URL (endpoint constants).  
- DEFAULT_SCOPES (default OAuth scopes list).  
- STATE_KEY_TOKENS, STATE_KEY_USER (app-state keys for persistent storage).  
- GoogleOAuthTokens (dataclass holding access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_at, scope, id_token).  
- GoogleOAuthTokens.is_expired (checks expiry with buffer_seconds).  
- GoogleOAuthTokens.to_dict and .from_dict (serialization helpers).  
- GoogleOAuthTokens.to_vertex_credentials_json (builds authorized_user dict for LiteLLM/Vertex).  
- generate_pkce_pair (creates code_verifier and S256 code_challenge).  
- build_authorization_url (constructs OAuth2 authorization URL with query params).  
- exchange_code_for_tokens (async; exchanges code for tokens using httpx.AsyncClient).  
- refresh_access_token (async; obtains fresh access token with refresh_token).  
- fetch_user_info (async; GET userinfo with Bearer token).  
- revoke_token (async; POST to revoke endpoint, returns boolean).  
- httpx.AsyncClient (external HTTP dependency used for async requests).  
- get_logger / log (module-level logger for warnings).

Key logic:
1. The module centralizes OAuth endpoint configuration as constants so all request builders and HTTP calls reference the same URLs.  
2. PKCE generation uses secrets.token_urlsafe(64) to create a high-entropy verifier, computes its SHA-256 digest, and produces a URL-safe base64-encoded challenge with padding removed for S256.  
3. build_authorization_url assembles a parameter dictionary including client_id, redirect_uri, response_type, joined scopes, access_type, and prompt, then conditionally includes state and PKCE code_challenge parameters before URL-encoding.  
4. exchange_code_for_tokens composes a token request payload with grant_type "authorization_code" and includes code_verifier when provided, then performs an HTTP POST to GOOGLE_TOKEN_URL using httpx.AsyncClient with a 30s timeout.  
5. After posting the token exchange request, exchange_code_for_tokens calls resp.raise_for_status() to propagate HTTP errors and reads resp.json() to extract access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_in, scope, and id_token; it computes expires_at by adding expires_in to the current time.  
6. refresh_access_token builds a payload for the refresh_token grant and POSTs to the token endpoint; it expects the response to contain a new access_token and possibly other fields, but preserves the original refresh_token because Google typically does not return a new refresh token.  
7. Both token-issuing functions return a GoogleOAuthTokens instance populated from the JSON response and computed expiry, providing a single object for callers to inspect and persist.  
8. fetch_user_info issues a GET to GOOGLE_USERINFO_URL with an Authorization: Bearer header, raises for non-2xx responses, and returns the parsed JSON profile to the caller.  
9. revoke_token sends a POST to the revoke endpoint with the token as a URL parameter and a form content-type header, interprets an HTTP 200 as success, and catches exceptions to log a warning and return False as a best-effort behavior.  
10. GoogleOAuthTokens provides helper logic: is_expired compares current time against expires_at minus a buffer to indicate near-term expiry; from_dict filters unknown keys when reconstructing an instance.  
11. to_vertex_credentials_json constructs the "authorized_user" dictionary expected by LiteLLM/VertexBase.load_auth() containing client_id, client_secret, refresh_token, token, and token_uri to enable downstream libraries to create refreshable Google credentials.  
12. The module relies on httpx.AsyncClient context managers to manage connection lifetimes and sets explicit timeouts for each kind of request (30s for token endpoints, 15s for userinfo and revoke) to limit blocking durations.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/main.py

Description:
1. This module is the main entry point for the Captain Claw application and coordinates startup for interactive and web-based modes.  
2. It provides a CLI argument parser builder for runtime overrides and a helper to decide whether to parse argv implicitly.  
3. The main() function orchestrates initial setup including logging configuration, onboarding, loading and applying configuration, and branching into TUI or web server modes.  
4. A special "orchestrate" subcommand is handled early to support headless workflow execution, including listing and running saved workflows.  
5. The module sets up session and workspace directories and exposes a version() helper to print package version information.  
6. An async run_interactive() function implements the terminal interactive loop, including signal handling, UI integration, agent initialization, and platform lifecycle management.  
7. run_interactive starts a background cron scheduler, races a threaded prompt against a stop event, and dispatches user input to local commands or the agent execution flow.  
8. Cleanup logic ensures platforms are torn down, background tasks are cancelled, terminal state is restored, and the process is force-exited to avoid thread-hang issues.  
9. When executed as a script it registers a small Typer-based CLI with run and ver commands that delegate to main() and version().  
10. The module relies on other project components such as Agent, UI, configuration, logging, onboarding, orchestrator, and web server modules to perform its responsibilities.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to centralize application bootstrap and provide a single, well-defined entrypoint for users and scripts to start Captain Claw.  
2. It encapsulates runtime argument parsing so callers and package entrypoints can flexibly override configuration, model, provider, and UI mode without duplicating logic.  
3. By handling an "orchestrate" subcommand early and separately, it supports headless automation and workflow execution suitable for cron jobs and non-interactive use.  
4. The onboarding integration allows initial configuration to be run interactively before normal startup, ensuring first-time users can be guided into a usable configuration.  
5. The main function unifies configuration loading, CLI overrides, and global configuration registration so the rest of the application can access a consistent Config instance.  
6. It chooses between terminal UI (TUI) and web UI modes based on flags and configuration, providing both interactive and server-based usage models from the same codepath.  
7. run_interactive implements a resilient event-driven REPL-style loop that coexists with asynchronous platform bridges and scheduled cron work.  
8. Signal handling and a cancellable agent cancel_event provide a controlled shutdown and per-turn cancellation behavior that is important for a responsive CLI.  
9. The module ensures workspace and session directories are created proactively to avoid runtime file-system errors when sessions are started or logs are written.  
10. Centralized logging configuration and a mechanism to redirect system log sink to the UI keep runtime status and diagnostics visible to the user.  
11. The forced os._exit() at the end of interactive shutdown is included to avoid deadlocks caused by non-interruptible input threads, trading a normal atexit sequence for guaranteed process termination.  
12. Providing a lightweight Typer CLI wrapper lets the module behave nicely when invoked as a script or installed CLI entrypoint without duplicating CLI definitions elsewhere.

Key elements:
- _build_runtime_arg_parser (function) — constructs argparse.ArgumentParser with runtime options and an "orchestrate" subparser.  
- _should_parse_runtime_cli_from_argv (function) — heuristic to decide whether to parse sys.argv for runtime flags.  
- main (function) — primary synchronous startup routine that handles CLI integration, onboarding, config loading, mode selection, and launching UI or web server.  
- run_interactive (async function) — implements the asynchronous terminal interactive loop, signal handlers, agent initialization, and cleanup.  
- version (function) — prints the package version using captain_claw.__version__.  
- Typer CLI (if __name__ == "__main__") — registers run and ver commands that delegate to main() and version().  
- Agent (imported class) — used to create the agent instance and access cancel_event, session, and usage metrics.  
- get_ui (imported function) — obtains UI instance used for prompt, status, and output callbacks.  
- Config (imported class) and set_config/get_config (functions) — configuration loading, instantiation, and global registration.  
- configure_logging, log, set_system_log_sink (imports) — logging setup and runtime log sinking into the UI.  
- run_onboarding_wizard and should_run_onboarding (imports) — interactive onboarding flow control.  
- orchestrator_cli.run_orchestrator_headless and _list_workflows_cli (imports used in orchestrate mode).  
- run_web_server (imported function) — starts the web server when web UI mode is selected.  
- asyncio, signal, os._exit, asyncio.Event, asyncio.to_thread, and asyncio.create_task (standard concurrency primitives used extensively).

Key logic:
1. On entry, the module may parse runtime CLI arguments sourced from sys.argv only if no explicit parameters were passed to main() and the invoking program name indicates a direct run.  
2. The _build_runtime_arg_parser defines global overrides such as config, model, provider, streaming, verbosity, onboarding, version, and a "tui" flag, plus an "orchestrate" subcommand with its own options.  
3. If parsing detects the "orchestrate" subcommand the module configures logging, imports orchestrator helpers, handles listing saved workflows, validates inputs, and invokes run_orchestrator_headless synchronously via asyncio.run().  
4. After orchestrator handling or normal CLI parsing, main sets up logging, possibly toggling DEBUG via environment variables when verbose is requested.  
5. Onboarding is conditionally run based on configuration and flags; failures or cancellations are caught, logged, and may cause process exit with appropriate messages.  
6. Configuration is loaded from a provided path or via Config.load(); CLI model/provider/no_stream overrides are applied and the resulting Config instance is stored globally via set_config.  
7. Filesystem preparation ensures session and workspace directories exist by expanding paths and creating parent directories as needed.  
8. The choice of TUI vs web mode is made from flags and cfg.web.enabled; TUI mode obtains the UI, sets system log sink, and executes the async run_interactive loop via asyncio.run().  
9. run_interactive sets up signal handlers that map first Ctrl+C to canceling the current agent turn and a second to a full stop, using a shared asyncio.Event and the agent's cancel_event.  
10. The interactive loop initializes the Agent, loads previous session outputs into the UI if present, starts platform bridges, and starts a cron scheduler task as a background worker.  
11. For each iteration it prints a status line, then races a threaded blocking prompt (via asyncio.to_thread) against the stop_event to remain responsive to signals while waiting for user input.  
12. After receiving input, special UI commands are handled first, then local commands are dispatched (which may break or continue the loop), and non-empty user prompts are passed to run_prompt_in_active_session for execution.  
13. Exceptions like KeyboardInterrupt, EOFError, and generic errors are logged and surfaced to the UI as appropriate, with the loop breaking on termination signals.  
14. During shutdown the module awaits teardown of platform bridges, cancels the cron worker and awaits its cancellation, resets terminal scroll regions, moves the cursor to a clean line, flushes stdout, and calls os._exit(0) to avoid hanging on thread joins.  
15. In web mode the module defers to run_web_server(cfg) and implements similar KeyboardInterrupt and exception handling to exit cleanly or log fatal errors.  
16. The included version() helper and Typer CLI provide convenience entrypoints for printing version information and running the main startup flow from the command line.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/prompt_execution.py

Description:
1. This module provides helpers to execute user prompts and to dispatch those prompts into the project's queuing and followup systems.  
2. It implements utilities for enqueuing tasks into layered command lanes, resolving per-session queue settings, and waiting for session idle states.  
3. The module can update and validate session queue metadata, persisting changes through the agent's session manager.  
4. It exposes a cancellable runner that races an awaitable against an ESC key capture from the UI to allow user-initiated cancellation.  
5. The core prompt execution path handles printing user prompts, streaming or non-streaming assistant responses, and integrating with cron events.  
6. It records timing and completion metadata on the runtime context and writes tool-style messages into session history for cron-triggered runs.  
7. Followup and scheduled prompts are enqueued into a followup queue when sessions are busy, with deduplication and drop-policy handling.  
8. An interrupt mode can clear a session's command lane and followup backlog before scheduling a new followup prompt.  
9. The module carefully switches agent.session when executing prompts in arbitrary sessions and restores the previous session afterward.  
10. Errors during prompt handling are logged, propagated to cron monitoring events, and optionally re-raised depending on context.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to centralize and standardize how prompts are executed in both interactive and scheduled (cron) contexts within the application.  
2. It abstracts queue lane resolution and multilayer enqueuing so callers can request prompt execution without managing low-level queue details.  
3. By resolving session-specific queue settings it ensures session metadata can influence runtime behavior like debounce, cap, mode, and drop policy.  
4. It provides a clean cancellation mechanism tied to the UI so long-running completions or streams can be interrupted by the user.  
5. The module integrates with cron_dispatch to emit structured events for monitoring and to log assistant and system activities related to scheduled runs.  
6. It supports streaming assistant output and non-streaming completion paths, allowing the UI to present partial output during generation.  
7. Followup queuing and dispatch logic decouples scheduled followups from immediate execution and implements deduplication and scheduling semantics.  
8. The interrupt capability exists to allow critical followups to preempt queued work and clear backlogs when required by policy.  
9. Updating session queue metadata via a dedicated function ensures validation and consistent persistence through the session manager.  
10. The file ensures that when a prompt is run in a session other than the current one, the agent's session is temporarily switched and then restored to avoid side effects.  
11. It also collects execution timing and state into the runtime context so higher-level components can report or react to recent execution metrics.  
12. Overall, the module ties together configuration, queueing, UI behavior, session management, and cron instrumentation to make prompt execution robust and observable.

Key elements:
- enqueue_agent_task (nested enqueuing into session, global, and AGENT_RUNTIME lanes).  
- _safe_int (parses and bounds integers with a minimum).  
- resolve_queue_settings_for_session (builds QueueSettings from config and session metadata).  
- wait_until_session_idle (polls command queue size for a session lane).  
- queue_meta (extracts queue metadata from a session-like object).  
- update_active_session_queue_settings (validates and writes queue metadata to the active session).  
- run_cancellable (runs an awaitable and cancels it if UI ESC is detected).  
- run_prompt_in_active_session (prints user message, runs agent stream/complete, handles streaming, calls cron events, and invokes callbacks).  
- run_queued_followup_prompt (adapter to run a FollowupRun from the followup queue).  
- dispatch_prompt_in_session (decides execute vs queue for followups, handles interrupt mode, schedules followup drains).  
- run_prompt_in_session (loads target session, switches agent.session, records tool messages, and enqueues the prompt run).  
- External dependencies: get_config (config access), CommandLane/FollowupRun/QueueSettings and normalize_* helpers from execution_queue, cron_chat_event/cron_monitor_event from cron_dispatch, ctx.command_queue and ctx.followup_queue, and agent.session_manager.

Key logic:
1. enqueue_agent_task composes three nested enqueue_in_lane calls so a task is first enqueued in a session-specific lane, then a resolved global lane, and finally the AGENT_RUNTIME lane to control execution ordering across scopes.  
2. _safe_int attempts integer conversion and enforces a minimum value, returning a provided default on failure.  
3. resolve_queue_settings_for_session fetches global config, loads the session if necessary, merges session-level queue metadata with config defaults, normalizes mode and drop_policy, and returns a QueueSettings object with computed debounce and cap values.  
4. wait_until_session_idle polls the command queue size for the resolved session lane with a short sleep loop until the queue is empty.  
5. queue_meta defensively extracts a "queue" dict from a session-like object's metadata only if present and valid.  
6. update_active_session_queue_settings validates incoming mode and drop_policy values using normalization helpers, updates the session metadata, timestamps the change, persists the session via session_manager, and returns a summary message along with success status.  
7. run_cancellable creates tasks for the work awaitable and optionally an ESC waiter from the UI, waits for the first to complete, cancels the other, and reports whether cancellation occurred while ensuring cleanup of tasks.  
8. run_prompt_in_active_session is the principal path for executing a single prompt in the currently active session: it prints the user prompt, emits cron start events if applicable, sets UI thinking/streaming states, and either streams assistant chunks via agent.stream or collects a single completion via agent.complete.  
9. During streaming, chunks are appended and printed via UI stream methods; non-streaming completions are printed as a single assistant message; both paths use run_cancellable to allow ESC-driven cancellation and handle cron bookkeeping for cancellations.  
10. After assistant output, optional callbacks on_assistant_text and after_turn are invoked with derived outbound text and turn indices; execution timing and last-completed timestamps are stored on the runtime context and the UI status is reset to waiting.  
11. Error handling logs the exception, emits cron failure events and messages into the session history, attempts to notify on_assistant_text of the error, and conditionally re-raises based on raise_on_error.  
12. Followup dispatch logic checks whether the session is busy or has a followup backlog, decides immediate execution or queuing based on resolved QueueSettings, supports an "interrupt" mode that clears lanes and followups, enqueues FollowupRun entries with deduplication, schedules drain callbacks, and emits monitoring/chat events for queued/skipped actions.  
13. run_prompt_in_session loads the target session object, raises if not found, and defines an _execute closure that switches agent.session to the target session, records start/done/fail tool messages into session history with token counts, invokes run_prompt_in_active_session directly (queue=False) under the CRON lane, persists session changes, and restores the previous session afterward.  
14. The module consistently uses ctx.command_queue and ctx.followup_queue for concurrency control and scheduling, and leverages agent.session_manager for durable session operations.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/telegram_bridge.py

Description:
1. This module implements a minimal asynchronous Telegram Bot API bridge using httpx.AsyncClient.  
2. It defines a dataclass TelegramMessage that normalizes incoming update payloads into a consistent structure.  
3. The TelegramBridge class wraps API URL construction, polling for updates, sending text messages, and other helper endpoints.  
4. get_updates performs long-polling, validates the API response, and extracts only text messages into TelegramMessage instances.  
5. send_message splits long text into manageable chunks and posts each chunk to Telegram using the sendMessage endpoint.  
6. send_chat_action posts transient chat status (for example, typing) to inform users of activity.  
7. send_audio_file uploads an audio file as multipart form data to the sendAudio endpoint after verifying the file exists.  
8. read_business_message posts a read receipt for business API messages when a business_connection_id is present.  
9. The bridge also exposes methods to register bot commands and configure the chat menu button via set_my_commands and set_chat_menu_button_commands.  
10. All network calls raise for HTTP errors through response.raise_for_status and the class manages an underlying AsyncClient lifecycle.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to centralize Telegram API interactions so other parts of the project can poll messages and send responses without duplicating HTTP logic.  
2. It provides a small, focused abstraction over the Telegram Bot API operations the application needs: fetching updates, sending messages and actions, uploading audio, and managing command metadata.  
3. By normalizing incoming updates into TelegramMessage objects, it simplifies downstream code that consumes user messages by guaranteeing a consistent set of fields.  
4. Long-polling logic and timeout handling are encapsulated so the rest of the system can rely on a single async call to receive new messages.  
5. The message chunking behavior ensures very long messages are safely split to respect Telegram payload limits and reduces the need for callers to handle splitting.  
6. File upload support is provided with local file validation to avoid sending invalid requests and to centralize the multipart upload pattern.  
7. Business-message read receipts are handled only when a business_connection_id is present, keeping consumer code free of API details.  
8. Command registration helpers let the application configure slash commands and menu button behavior in one place, improving maintainability when command sets change.  
9. The AsyncClient is owned by the bridge so connection pooling, timeouts, and graceful closure are managed consistently.  
10. Exposing an enabled property makes it trivial for the application to disable Telegram integration by omitting a token.  
11. The module keeps API base URL configurable to support alternate Telegram-compatible endpoints if needed.  
12. Overall, it exists to provide dependable, reusable Telegram integration primitives that other modules can call asynchronously without handling HTTP or payload normalization themselves.

Key elements:
- TelegramMessage (dataclass: normalized fields for update_id, message_id, chat_id, user_id, username, first_name, text, business_connection_id)  
- TelegramBridge.__init__ (constructor: stores token, api_base_url, creates httpx.AsyncClient)  
- TelegramBridge.enabled (property: boolean indicating token presence)  
- TelegramBridge._url (helper: constructs endpoint URL for given method)  
- TelegramBridge.close (async: closes AsyncClient)  
- TelegramBridge.get_updates (async: long-poll getUpdates and normalize messages)  
- TelegramBridge.send_message (async: chunk and post sendMessage)  
- TelegramBridge.send_chat_action (async: post sendChatAction)  
- TelegramBridge.send_audio_file (async: validate file and post sendAudio with multipart files)  
- TelegramBridge.read_business_message (async: post readBusinessMessage for business API)  
- TelegramBridge.set_my_commands (async: sanitize and post setMyCommands payload)  
- TelegramBridge.set_chat_menu_button_commands (async: post setChatMenuButton payload)  
- httpx.AsyncClient (external dependency used for all HTTP calls)  
- pathlib.Path (used for file resolution/validation in send_audio_file)

Key logic:
1. Initialization stores a stripped token and a normalized API base URL, then creates an AsyncClient with a 40-second timeout for reuse across calls.  
2. The enabled property simply returns whether a non-empty token is configured, enabling callers to gate Telegram usage.  
3. _url concatenates the base URL, bot token, and a method name to produce endpoint URLs used by all request methods.  
4. get_updates builds query parameters including an optional offset and a timeout for long-polling, then performs a GET against getUpdates.  
5. The response JSON is validated to be a dict with ok=True and a list result; nonconforming responses result in an empty list.  
6. For each result item, get_updates prefers the "message" key and falls back to "business_message", then skips non-dict or non-text entries.  
7. It extracts user and chat info, coerces numeric fields to int, filters out zero ids, and creates TelegramMessage objects only for valid text messages.  
8. send_message accepts text, trims it, and splits it into chunks with a practical max length (3800 chars), trying to break on newlines but falling back to a hard split when necessary.  
9. Each chunk is posted to sendMessage as JSON, with reply_to_message_id included only for the first chunk if provided, and each call raises on HTTP error.  
10. send_chat_action simply posts a chat_id and action (default typing) to the sendChatAction endpoint and raises on error.  
11. send_audio_file resolves and validates the file path, constructs a payload and multipart files mapping, then posts data/files to sendAudio and raises on failure.  
12. read_business_message composes a payload with business_connection_id, chat_id, and message_id but returns early if the business_connection_id is empty to avoid unnecessary calls.  
13. set_my_commands iterates provided (name, description) tuples, sanitizes and lowercases command names, builds a list of command dicts, skips if empty, and posts to setMyCommands.  
14. set_chat_menu_button_commands posts a fixed payload to set the menu button to open commands.  
15. All methods rely on response.raise_for_status to surface HTTP error conditions rather than returning partial or silent failures.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/pocket_tts.py

Description:
1. This module implements a local text-to-speech tool that synthesizes MP3 audio from text using the pocket-tts package.  
2. It provides helper functions to normalize and convert model-produced audio samples into signed 16-bit PCM and then encode those bytes to MP3.  
3. The module attempts MP3 encoding first via the Python lameenc package and falls back to invoking system ffmpeg if lameenc is not available.  
4. A PocketTTSTool class is defined that extends the project Tool abstraction and exposes an async execute method to run the synthesis pipeline.  
5. The tool lazily loads and caches a pocket-tts model, capturing a load error message to avoid repeated failed import attempts.  
6. The code supports selecting a voice preset, obtaining a corresponding model "state", and handling multiple generate_audio method signatures for compatibility.  
7. Input text length is validated against a configurable max_chars setting from project configuration before synthesis proceeds.  
8. Generated audio samples are coerced from nested or tensor-like structures into a flat list of floats, then converted into PCM, encoded, and saved to a normalized path under the saved/media area.  
9. The execute method returns a ToolResult summarizing file path, voice, format, bitrate, sample rate, and approximate duration on success or an error on failure.  
10. Robust error handling and logging are used throughout to convert dependency or runtime failures into clear error messages.

Purpose:
