1. The file exists to provide a reusable, project-integrated tool for converting textual content into speech that can be stored and referenced by other components.  
2. It centralizes pocket-tts integration so callers need not manage model loading, signature compatibility, sample conversion, or encoding details.  
3. The PocketTTSTool wraps configuration-driven defaults (voice, sample rate, mp3 bitrate, and timeouts) and enforces length limits to keep synthesis predictable.  
4. By encoding to MP3 and writing into the project's saved/media area, the tool matches the repository's file organization and ensures outputs are accessible to downstream features.  
5. The lazy model loading and cached error behavior reduce startup overhead and avoid redundant import failures in long-running processes.  
6. The module provides compatibility handling for different pocket-tts method signatures and for different audio sample containers (lists, tensors, numpy-like objects).  
7. The lameenc/ffmpeg dual-encoding strategy makes the feature usable in environments with either a pure-Python encoder or a system ffmpeg binary.  
8. Helper conversion functions isolate concerns: iterating nested audio values, coercing to floats, PCM conversion, and MP3 encoding are each testable and replaceable.  
9. The tool's execute method exposes a simple, documented parameter set so orchestration layers can request synthesis without duplicating audio processing logic.  
10. Centralized logging and error propagation via ToolResult allow orchestration code to handle failures uniformly.  
11. Path resolution logic ensures untrusted or user-provided paths are normalized under the saved root and that output files always use the .mp3 suffix.  
12. Overall, the file exists to reliably turn text into persisted speech artifacts while hiding low-level audio and dependency complexity from the rest of the project.

Key elements:
- _iter_scalar_samples (function): yields float samples from arbitrarily nested list/tuple or scalar values.  
- _coerce_samples (function): normalizes tensor-like or nested model outputs into a flat list of float samples.  
- _samples_to_pcm16 (function): converts float samples into signed 16-bit PCM bytes with scaling and clipping.  
- _encode_mp3_bytes (function): encodes PCM bytes to MP3 using lameenc or falling back to ffmpeg via subprocess.  
- _write_bytes (function): simple helper to write raw bytes to a pathlib.Path.  
- PocketTTSTool (class): Tool subclass implementing pocket-tts synthesis, configuration, and file output.  
- PocketTTSTool.execute (async method): orchestrates validation, model load, generation, conversion, encoding, and file write.  
- PocketTTSTool._ensure_model (async method): lazily imports pocket_tts, validates TTSModel, and loads it in a background thread.  
- PocketTTSTool._generate_audio (staticmethod): compatibility wrapper trying multiple generate_audio call signatures including state handling.  
- PocketTTSTool._resolve_output_path (method): constructs and normalizes the output path under the project's saved root and enforces .mp3 suffix.  
- get_config (external call): used to read pocket_tts-related configuration values.  
- WriteTool (external dependency): used for saved root and session id normalization utilities.  
- importlib, asyncio.to_thread, subprocess.run, shutil.which, lameenc, ffmpeg (external modules/calls): used for dynamic imports, threading wrappers, and encoding fallbacks.  
- ToolResult (class): used to return structured success/error results from execute.

Key logic:
1. The module first provides small, focused helpers to transform arbitrary model audio outputs into a canonical float sample list by attempting tensor detachment, CPU transfer, reshape, and tolist conversions.  
2. After coercing samples, it converts floats to signed 16-bit integers by scaling values within a typical [-1,1] range to the 16-bit amplitude and clipping to the valid PCM range.  
3. MP3 encoding is attempted using the lameenc Python encoder; if that import or encoding fails, the code locates a system ffmpeg binary and runs it as a subprocess feeding raw s16le mono PCM on stdin and capturing encoded MP3 on stdout.  
4. The ffmpeg call is constructed with explicit sample rate, channel count, format, and bitrate and any subprocess errors are captured and surfaced with stderr content when available.  
5. PocketTTSTool manages a cached _model and a _model_load_error string so repeated attempts to use a missing or incompatible dependency produce a consistent runtime error rather than repeatedly failing import.  
6. _ensure_model performs a dynamic import of pocket_tts and verifies that the package exposes a TTSModel; model loading is delegated to a background thread via asyncio.to_thread.  
7. _generate_audio provides signature compatibility by trying multiple call forms when a voice state is provided and falling back to simple text-only calls when state is None, raising a TypeError for unsupported signatures.  
8. execute validates the provided text and enforces a configurable maximum character length from the project config, returning a failure ToolResult for invalid input.  
9. The output file path is resolved using WriteTool utilities to ensure the path is safely nested under the saved root and to guarantee an .mp3 suffix; directories are created as needed.  
10. Voice selection prioritizes the explicit voice parameter, then a configured default in config, then a model-provided default_voice; if a voice is selected the code requests a voice state from the model in a background thread.  
11. Audio generation, sample coercion, PCM conversion, MP3 encoding, and file writing are each executed in background threads to avoid blocking the event loop, and intermediate emptiness checks (e.g., no samples) produce clear error results.  
12. On success the tool composes a human-readable summary including the actual saved path, voice label, format, bitrate, sample rate, and estimated duration, while exceptions are logged and returned as ToolResult failures.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/contacts.py

Description:
1. This module defines a ContactsTool class for managing a persistent cross-session address book.  
2. The tool exposes actions to add, list, search, view info, update, and remove contacts.  
3. It integrates with a session manager (obtained via get_session_manager) to perform CRUD operations on stored contact records.  
4. The tool declares a JSON schema for expected parameters including fields like name, contact_id, email, tags, notes, and privacy_tier.  
5. The execute method routes incoming action requests to internal async helper methods based on the action string.  
6. The add helper validates that a name is provided, calls sm.create_contact, and returns a success ToolResult with a brief confirmation.  
7. The list and search helpers format contact summaries into line-oriented strings and return them as ToolResult content.  
8. The info helper assembles a multi-line detailed view of a single contact including metadata such as importance and last seen.  
9. The update helper builds an update dict from provided fields, appends notes instead of replacing, clamps importance into a 1–10 range, and calls sm.update_contact.  
10. The remove helper selects a contact then calls sm.delete_contact and returns success or error results accordingly.  

Purpose:
1. This file exists to provide a reusable tool abstraction that allows other parts of the application to manage contacts in a consistent programmatic way.  
2. By encapsulating contact operations behind the Tool interface, the module makes it straightforward to invoke contact actions from sessions, agents, or external integrations.  
3. The parameter schema documents available fields and expected types so callers can validate and build requests uniformly.  
4. Delegating persistence to the session manager separates storage concerns from the tool logic and enables contacts to persist across sessions.  
5. Helper methods centralize validation, formatting, and transformation logic so responses are standardized and human-readable.  
6. Returning ToolResult objects integrates with the project's tool execution framework and provides consistent success/error reporting.  
7. The module implements small business rules like defaulting importance and privacy tiers to maintain sensible defaults on creation.  
8. Appending notes instead of replacing them preserves context accumulation on contacts, which supports tracking over time.  
9. Formatting choices such as truncated IDs and inline organization/position snippets optimize lists for compact display.  
10. Centralizing contact operations reduces duplication and simplifies future changes to persistence, formatting, or validation.  
11. The top-level execute method also provides a single place to catch and log exceptions and convert them into ToolResult errors for callers.  
12. Overall, the module serves as the bridge between external commands and the session-backed contact datastore while enforcing input constraints and presentation conventions.  

Key elements:
- ContactsTool (class) — Tool subclass implementing contact management.  
- name, description (attributes) — tool metadata used by registry and user-facing help.  
- parameters (attribute) — JSON schema describing allowed action fields and types.  
- execute(action, ...) (method) — dispatcher that routes actions to internal helpers and handles errors.  
- _add(sm, ...) (async helper) — creates a contact via sm.create_contact with defaults and validation.  
- _list(sm) (async helper) — lists contacts via sm.list_contacts and formats summary lines.  
- _search(sm, query) (async helper) — searches via sm.search_contacts and formats results.  
- _info(sm, contact_id) (async helper) — builds detailed multi-line view from a selected contact.  
- _update(sm, contact_id, ...) (async helper) — constructs update kwargs, appends notes, clamps importance, calls sm.update_contact.  
- _remove(sm, contact_id) (async helper) — selects and deletes a contact via sm.delete_contact.  
- get_session_manager (external call) — obtains persistence/session manager used for contact operations.  
- ToolResult (type) — used for returning standardized success/error payloads.  
- get_logger / log (dependency) — used for error logging in execute exception handling.  
- session manager methods referenced: create_contact, list_contacts, search_contacts, select_contact, update_contact, delete_contact.  

Key logic:
1. execute begins by extracting an optional _session_id from kwargs and obtaining the shared session manager to route operations through a consistent persistence layer.  
2. The method then matches the action string against supported actions and forwards parameters to the corresponding private async helper.  
3. Unknown actions immediately return a ToolResult error, while exceptions thrown by helpers are caught, logged, and converted to ToolResult errors.  
4. The add helper enforces that a non-empty name is provided, calls sm.create_contact with defaults for importance and privacy_tier, and returns a brief success message containing the new contact's truncated id and name.  
5. The list helper requests up to 50 contacts from sm.list_contacts and builds compact summary lines including importance, name, optional position and organization, relation, and an 8-character id prefix.  
6. The search helper requires a non-empty query, calls sm.search_contacts with a limit (20), and formats matching entries similarly to the list output.  
7. The info helper requires a contact identifier, resolves it via sm.select_contact, and composes a detailed, multi-line representation including id, position, organization, emails, phones, importance and whether it was pinned, mention counts, last seen timestamp, tags, description, notes, and privacy tier.  
8. The update helper first resolves the contact by id then accumulates only provided fields into a kwargs dict; it clamps importance values to the 1–10 range and sets an importance_pinned flag when importance is provided.  
9. Notes provided in an update are appended to any existing notes with a newline separator rather than replacing them, preserving historical context.  
10. If no updatable fields are present the update helper returns an error; otherwise it calls sm.update_contact and reports success or failure based on the return value.  
11. The remove helper resolves the contact, calls sm.delete_contact, and returns success with a truncated id and name or an error if deletion failed.  
12. Throughout, methods return ToolResult objects with success booleans and textual content or error messages, enabling predictable consumption by the tool registry and callers.

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/write.py

Description:
1. This module implements a WriteTool class that provides functionality to create or overwrite files with supplied content.  
2. The tool defines metadata including a name ("write"), a short description, and a JSON schema for expected parameters such as path, content, and append.  
3. It includes helper static methods to normalize a session identifier, resolve a saved-root directory, and map requested paths into a session-scoped saved area.  
4. The write operation enforces that outputs are placed under a designated saved root and attempts to scope files by session and category names.  
5. The execute method creates parent directories as needed, chooses append or write mode, writes UTF-8 content to the resolved file path, and returns a ToolResult.  
6. The module attempts a best-effort registration of the logical requested path to the physical file path with an optional file registry passed in kwargs.  
7. Path normalization handles absolute and relative inputs, strips unsafe path parts, rejects upward traversal, and applies a fallback when a candidate path would escape the saved root.  
8. Session identifiers are sanitized to filesystem-safe strings with a default of "default" when empty.  
9. Saved-root resolution prefers explicit _saved_base_path, then derives a saved subdirectory from _runtime_base_path, and otherwise falls back to the current working directory's saved folder.  
10. Errors during writing are logged and returned as a failing ToolResult rather than raising.

Purpose:
1. This file exists to centralize and encapsulate the logic for writing tool-managed outputs into a controlled filesystem area so other components can produce files safely.  
2. It enforces consistent scoping of outputs by session and by a set of accepted categories so that multiple sessions or tasks do not collide on file names.  
3. The tool exists to provide a programmatic, schema-driven interface for agents or tasks to request file writes without needing to manipulate the repository filesystem directly.  
4. By resolving a saved root from runtime-provided paths, the tool can operate in different deployment contexts where the base output location may vary.  
5. The normalization helpers ensure session identifiers become filesystem-safe and that requested paths are mapped into the saved hierarchy, preventing accidental writes outside the intended area.  
6. Appending support is provided to allow incremental writes to existing outputs when needed by callers.  
7. The optional file registry integration allows other parts of the system to later discover files by their original requested logical path, improving interoperability.  
8. The implementation takes a defensive stance: it creates directories as needed and performs best-effort registry registration but does not fail the write if the registry call throws.  
9. Logging and ToolResult-based error reporting make the tool suitable for use in broader automated workflows where exceptions should be converted into structured results.  
10. The category-based scoping and fallback behavior exist to keep files organized into predictable directories like downloads, media, and tmp, aiding downstream consumers.  
11. The tool is designed to be lightweight and synchronous in its file I/O while fitting into an async-compatible tool execution flow (execute is async).  
12. Overall, it provides a safe, auditable, and reusable mechanism for controlled file output from programmatic tasks.

Key elements:
- WriteTool (class) (main tool class exposing name, description, parameters, and execute).  
- _normalize_session_id (static method) (creates filesystem-safe session id with alnum and ._- allowed).  
- _resolve_saved_root (static method) (determines saved root from _saved_base_path, _runtime_base_path, or cwd and ensures it exists).  
- _normalize_under_saved (static method) (maps requested path into saved_root, enforces session scoping, categories, and fallback).  
- execute (async method) (performs actual write, directory creation, registry registration, and returns ToolResult).  
- parameters (dict) (JSON schema for path, content, append).  
- ToolResult (external type) (used to encapsulate success, content, or error).  
- get_logger / log (external logging) (used for error logging).  
- Path (pathlib) usage (expanduser, resolve, mkdir, relative_to manipulations).  
- kwargs keys referenced (_saved_base_path, _runtime_base_path, _session_id, _file_registry, _task_id).

Key logic:
1. The execute method starts by resolving the saved root using _resolve_saved_root, which prefers explicit saved base paths, falls back to a runtime base path's saved subfolder, and finally uses the current working directory's saved folder, creating it if necessary.  
2. The session id is normalized by _normalize_session_id to a safe token composed of alphanumeric characters and a limited set of punctuation, defaulting to "default" when empty.  
3. The requested path is normalized into the saved hierarchy by _normalize_under_saved, which first expands the path and distinguishes absolute from relative inputs.  
4. For absolute inputs, the method attempts to compute a path relative to saved_root; if that fails it constructs a relative hint from the absolute path parts to avoid placing files outside saved_root.  
5. The normalization strips empty and traversal parts, treats an empty or invalid path as "output.txt", and allows a leading "saved" token to be omitted so callers can use both "saved/..." and plain names.  
6. A set of known categories triggers creation of a scoped path [category, session_id, ...]; otherwise the file is placed under tmp/session_id/... to maintain session isolation.  
7. The candidate path is resolved and validated to be inside saved_root; if it would escape, a fallback path under saved_root/tmp/session_id is constructed using the final safe part.  
8. Once a concrete file_path is chosen, parent directories are created with mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True) to ensure the filesystem is ready for writing.  
9. The file is opened in "a" mode if append is True, otherwise in "w" mode, and content is written as UTF-8.  
10. A redirect note is computed when the requested path differs from the actual physical path to inform callers about the mapping.  
11. If a _file_registry is provided in kwargs, the tool attempts to register the logical-to-physical mapping along with an optional task id, but ignores exceptions from this best-effort registration.  
12. On success, the tool returns a ToolResult with success=True and a content string describing number of characters written and the file location; on exception it logs an error and returns a failing ToolResult with the error string.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/send_mail.py

Description:
1. This module defines a SendMailTool class that implements an asynchronous tool for sending email messages with optional file attachments.  
2. The tool supports three delivery providers: Mailgun and SendGrid via HTTP APIs, and direct SMTP delivery.  
3. It validates input parameters such as recipients, subject, and at least one of a plain text or HTML body before attempting delivery.  
4. Attachment paths are resolved, validated for existence and file-ness, size-checked against a configurable maximum, and read into memory as bytes.  
5. The module uses an httpx.AsyncClient for HTTP-based providers and constructs provider-specific payloads for Mailgun and SendGrid.  
6. For SMTP delivery it builds an email.message.EmailMessage, sets appropriate headers, handles text/HTML alternatives, and attaches files with proper MIME types.  
7. The SMTP path prefers the aiosmtplib async library and falls back to Python's smtplib executed in a thread when aiosmtplib is not available.  
8. Configuration values (provider selection, credentials, host/port, timeouts, limits) are read via get_config and environment-variable fallbacks for API keys.  
9. The execute method returns a ToolResult indicating success or failure and includes a human-readable detail string on success.  
10. A close method is provided to cleanly close the underlying httpx client when the tool is no longer needed.

Purpose:
This module provides a single, reusable tool implementation to send email from the application, encapsulating provider differences and common validation in one place. It exists to let other parts of the project dispatch email without duplicating delivery logic, offering a consistent interface and result format (ToolResult). The tool centralizes configuration lookup for provider selection, credentials, timeouts, and attachment limits so those settings are managed in config rather than scattered code. Supporting Mailgun, SendGrid, and SMTP allows flexible deployment choices depending on available services or preferences. Attachment handling lives here so callers can supply filesystem paths and rely on consistent size and type checks. By using an asynchronous httpx client and preferring aiosmtplib, the implementation aims to integrate cleanly into async application workflows while still providing a synchronous fallback for environments without aiosmtplib. Error handling and explicit failure ToolResult returns make it straightforward for callers to detect and report delivery failures. The module formats provider-specific payloads and authentication mechanisms, isolating API details from callers. It also normalizes headers and recipient handling (including CC and BCC) to ensure consistent envelope construction across providers. Finally, the provided close method enables proper cleanup of network resources, preventing client leaks in long-running processes.

Key elements:
- SendMailTool (class) (Tool subclass implementing email sending).  
- name, timeout_seconds, description, parameters (class attributes for tool metadata and JSON schema).  
- execute(...) (main async method that validates inputs, reads attachments, selects provider, and returns a ToolResult).  
- _send_mailgun(...) (async helper that posts multipart/form-data to Mailgun using httpx with basic auth).  
- _send_sendgrid(...) (async helper that posts JSON to SendGrid using Bearer token authorization and base64-encoded attachments).  
- _send_smtp(...) (async helper that composes EmailMessage, attaches files, and sends via aiosmtplib or smtplib fallback).  
- close(...) (async method to aclose the module's httpx.AsyncClient).  
- httpx.AsyncClient (used for HTTP API calls).  
- get_config (reads mail-related configuration).  
- EmailMessage (from email.message for SMTP message construction).  
- asyncio.to_thread (used to read files and run smtplib send in a thread).  
- mimetypes.guess_type, base64.b64encode, pathlib.Path (used for attachment MIME detection, encoding, and file handling).  
- ToolResult (return type used to signal success/error to callers).  

Key logic:
The execute method begins by normalizing and validating recipient lists, subject, and the presence of either plain text or HTML content, immediately returning failure if required inputs are missing. It reads mail-related configuration via get_config and chooses the provider string (mailgun, sendgrid, or smtp) along with sender information and numeric timeouts or limits. Attachments are processed in sequence: each given path is expanded, resolved, and verified to exist and be a regular file; file sizes are compared to a configurable max_attachment_bytes and large files cause a failure. Files are read into memory using asyncio.to_thread to avoid blocking the event loop, and mimetypes.guess_type is used to assign a MIME type fallback to application/octet-stream if unknown. After preparing attachment metadata, the method dispatches to a provider-specific helper based on the configured provider. The Mailgun helper builds form data and a files list suitable for multipart/form-data and posts to the Mailgun messages endpoint with basic auth using the API key; it raises errors for missing API key or domain. The SendGrid helper composes a JSON payload with personalizations, from/to objects, content parts for text and/or HTML, and encodes attachments as base64 strings while sending with a Bearer token header; it interprets a 202 response as accepted. The SMTP helper constructs an EmailMessage, sets From/To/Cc/Subject headers, handles text vs HTML variants properly using set_content/add_alternative, and attaches binary content with maintype/subtype parsed from the MIME type. For SMTP delivery the helper attempts to import aiosmtplib and send asynchronously; if that import fails it runs a synchronous smtplib SMTP sequence (starttls, login if provided, sendmail) inside asyncio.to_thread to preserve the async calling contract. Throughout, exceptions during provider calls are caught upstream in execute, logged, and converted into a failing ToolResult with the exception string. On success, execute composes a multi-line summary including provider, from/to/cc/bcc, subject, recipient count, attachment count, and provider detail string returned from the helper, and returns that in a successful ToolResult. The close method simply closes the httpx.AsyncClient to release network resources.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/registry.py

Description:
1. This module implements a tool registry system and a base Tool abstraction for registering, selecting, and executing tools.  
2. It defines utility functions to parse and analyze shell commands, including tokenization, segment splitting, and extraction of base executable tokens.  
3. A ToolResult Pydantic model encapsulates execution outcomes and normalizes error messages for failed executions.  
4. The abstract Tool base class specifies the interface and basic argument validation used by concrete tool implementations.  
5. ToolPolicy and ToolPolicyChain models provide structured allow/deny/also_allow rules and the logic to apply them in sequence.  
6. ToolRegistry stores registered Tool instances, manages metadata, enforces policies, and exposes methods to list and retrieve tools and their definitions.  
7. The registry contains logic to evaluate shell execution policies, check explicitly blocked shell commands, and optionally require approval callbacks.  
8. Execution of a tool is performed asynchronously with support for timeout handling, abort event bridging, and safe task cancellation.  
9. Global helper functions supply a singleton registry instance and allow replacing it with a custom registry.  
10. The module relies on configuration via get_config, logging via get_logger, and standard libraries for regex, fnmatch, shlex, asyncio, and pathlib.

Purpose:
This module exists to centralize management of tools that the application can use and to provide consistent control over which tools are available and how they are executed. It provides a formal base class and result model so that tools present a uniform interface and validation, simplifying integration with higher-level orchestrators or LLM-driven flows. The policy types and the ToolPolicyChain enable layered policy evaluation (global, session, task) so administrators or sessions can restrict or expand available tools dynamically. Shell-related utilities and policy evaluation focus on safety: they parse commands to determine base executables, support pattern-based deny/allow rules, and detect unparseable or empty commands. The registry's execute method coordinates the full lifecycle of running a tool, including argument validation, policy checks, approval prompts, execution with timeout, and abort propagation, which centralizes complexity and reduces duplication. It also provides path management for saved outputs by resolving a runtime base path and an isolated saved directory, preventing accidental escapes. The module integrates with project configuration and logging to make behavior configurable and observable. By exposing get_definitions and list_tools it supports downstream components like LLM function schemas or UIs that need metadata about available tools. The singleton accessors (get_tool_registry and set_tool_registry) make it easy to obtain or replace the global registry instance for tests or different runtime contexts. Overall, the file exists to provide a safe, configurable, and consistent mechanism to register, filter, and run tools while handling concurrency, timeouts, and cancellation robustly.

Key elements:
- _normalize_tool_name (function) (normalizes names for comparison).  
- _compile_shell_pattern (function) (compiles regex with literal fallback).  
- _tokenize_shell_command, _split_shell_segments, _extract_segment_base_command (functions) (tokenize and segment shell commands and extract base executables).  
- extract_shell_base_commands (function) (public helper to get base commands from a shell string).  
- is_blocked_shell_command (function) (evaluates a command against blocked patterns with parsed matching).  
- ToolResult (Pydantic model) (contains success, content, error and normalizes error on failure).  
- Tool (abstract base class) (defines name, description, parameters, timeout_seconds, execute, get_definition, validate_arguments).  
- ToolPolicy (Pydantic model) (policy fields: allow, deny, also_allow).  
- ToolPolicyChain (class) (applies policy steps and resolves allowed tools).  
- ToolRegistry (class) (register/unregister tools, manage metadata, policies, execute tools with timeout/abort handling).  
- _evaluate_shell_exec_policy and _shell_pattern_matches (methods) (determine allow/deny/ask for shell commands using glob-like patterns and targets).  
- get_tool_registry / set_tool_registry (global singleton accessors).  
- Dependencies: get_config (configuration), get_logger (logging), fnmatch, re, shlex, asyncio, pathlib, pydantic.

Key logic:
1. Shell parsing logic tokenizes commands using shlex with punctuation_chars set to separate common shell control operators and then splits tokens into segments by those separators.  
2. For each shell segment the extractor skips environment-like assignments and common wrapper tokens (sudo, command, builtin, nohup, time) to identify the actual executable token.  
3. extract_shell_base_commands returns the base executable for each segment; that list is used both for policy evaluation and pattern matching.  
4. is_blocked_shell_command first short-circuits empty or unparseable commands, then compiles each blocked pattern (falling back to literal escape on regex errors) and matches either the full segment text or the base commands depending on whether the pattern contains whitespace.  
5. ToolPolicyChain builds a normalized set of tool names and applies each policy step by intersecting with explicit allow lists, removing deny names, and unioning in also_allow limited to known tools.  
6. ToolRegistry maintains internal maps of tool instances and metadata and supports per-instance runtime base paths and a configurable saved directory name to derive safe save paths.  
7. When executing a tool, the registry resolves the effective set of available tools through the policy chain and raises ToolBlockedError if the requested tool is not allowed.  
8. For the special "shell" tool name the registry runs an extra policy evaluation (_evaluate_shell_exec_policy) which checks deny/allow patterns from configuration and returns deny/allow/ask; an approval callback may be invoked for "ask" decisions.  
9. The registry also checks configured blocked shell commands via is_blocked_shell_command and rejects empty or unparseable commands with specific error reasons.  
10. Argument validation is delegated to the tool via validate_arguments; missing required parameters raise ToolExecutionError.  
11. Execution is performed by creating an asyncio task for the tool.execute coroutine and a separate task that waits on a tool-specific abort event; an optional external abort event can be bridged to the tool abort event.  
12. The registry waits for either the execute task to complete, the abort wait task to trigger, or a timeout to elapse; it cancels tasks cleanly using an internal _cancel_task helper that awaits cancelled tasks to suppress warnings.  
13. If the execute task completes, its return value is validated to be a ToolResult; otherwise ToolExecutionError is raised for invalid payloads.  
14. If the abort event occurs the execute task is cancelled and an execution-aborted error is raised; if timeout occurs the execute task is cancelled and a timeout error including the elapsed seconds is raised.  
15. Exceptions during execution are logged and wrapped in ToolExecutionError except for already-raised ToolExecutionError and asyncio.CancelledError which are propagated appropriately.  
16. The registry supports per-call overrides for runtime base path, approval callback, and file registry references, and ensures the computed saved base path remains a descendant of the runtime base path to avoid path traversal.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/web_fetch.py

Description:
1. This module provides asynchronous tools to fetch web content and return either cleaned readable text or raw HTML.  
2. It constructs a shared-style httpx.AsyncClient configured with a timeout, follow-redirect behavior, and a custom User-Agent.  
3. An HTML-to-text extractor uses BeautifulSoup to remove non-content tags like script, style, noscript, template, svg, and canvas.  
4. Anchor tags are preserved by replacing them with their visible label followed by the absolute URL in parentheses, or just the absolute URL if no label exists.  
5. The extractor collects visible text lines, collapses whitespace, and preserves the document title at the beginning when appropriate.  
6. WebFetchTool implements a tool that always returns plain text extracted from a fetched page and prepends metadata headers.  
7. WebGetTool implements a tool that returns the raw HTML source of a fetched page with similar metadata headers.  
8. Both tools consult configuration for a default maximum character limit, accept an optional max_chars parameter, and truncate output with a clear marker when exceeded.  
9. HTTP errors and general exceptions are logged and returned as failure ToolResult objects with error messages.  
10. Each tool creates and holds its own AsyncClient instance and exposes an async close method to properly aclose the client.

Purpose:
This module exists to provide reusable web fetching capabilities for the project, exposing two specialized tools for different consumption needs. It centralizes HTTP client creation so both tools share consistent timeout, redirect, and header behavior. The readable-text extractor exists to convert HTML into a compact, human-friendly representation suitable for downstream consumption by other components. The raw-HTML fetcher is provided for cases that need the original markup for scraping, parsing, or DOM inspection. Both tools expose parameter schemas so callers or a tool registry can validate invocation arguments. The module integrates with project configuration (get_config) to apply a configurable default maximum character limit, giving operators control over result sizes. Logging via the project's logger is used to surface operational failures and contextual metadata about fetch operations. The design enforces that WebFetchTool always returns text by removing any extract_mode override, reducing ambiguity in usage. The replacement of anchor tags with absolute URLs helps preserve source references for later turns or citations. Exception handling differentiates HTTP-specific errors from other failures to provide clearer error messages. The included close methods ensure that client resources are released when tools are shut down. Overall, the module provides predictable, configurable, and safe ways to retrieve web content for the rest of the application.

Key elements:
- _make_http_client (function; constructs and returns httpx.AsyncClient with timeout, follow_redirects, and User-Agent header).  
- _extract_readable_text (function; uses BeautifulSoup to strip non-content tags, handle anchors, collapse whitespace, and preserve title).  
- WebFetchTool (class; name "web_fetch", parameters schema, always returns text, methods __init__, execute, close).  
- WebGetTool (class; name "web_get", parameters schema, returns raw HTML, methods __init__, execute, close).  
- execute (method on both tools; performs async GET, enforces max_chars, assembles metadata headers, returns ToolResult).  
- close (async method on both tools; closes the httpx client via aclose).  
- get_config (external call; used to read tools.web_fetch.max_chars default).  
- get_logger (external call; module-level logger used for info and error logging).  
- httpx (external dependency; AsyncClient, HTTPError, response handling).  
- BeautifulSoup (external dependency; HTML parsing and DOM manipulation).  
- urljoin from urllib.parse (used to resolve relative hrefs to absolute URLs).  
- re (standard library; used to collapse whitespace in extracted text).  
- Tool and ToolResult (external base classes/models from tools.registry used for tool interface and results).

Key logic:
The module begins by providing a helper to create a configured httpx.AsyncClient with a 30-second timeout, automatic redirect following, and a custom User-Agent header. The HTML extraction function parses raw HTML with BeautifulSoup, removes elements that do not contribute to readable content (script/style/noscript/template/svg/canvas), and then processes anchor tags to preserve a visible label paired with an absolute URL computed via urljoin when a base URL is available. After DOM cleanup, the extractor retrieves the document text, splits it into lines, collapses runs of whitespace on each line using a regular expression, and collects non-empty cleaned lines into a single newline-joined text. If a title element is present and the cleaned text does not already start with it, the extractor prefixes the title followed by a blank line. Both WebFetchTool and WebGetTool construct their own AsyncClient instances at initialization. In execute, each tool logs the fetch attempt and reads the global configuration to determine a configured max_chars default; an explicit max_chars parameter overrides this default, but the effective value is coerced to at least 1. The tools perform an async GET request to the provided URL and call response.raise_for_status() to surface HTTP errors. WebFetchTool passes response.text to the extractor to obtain readable text, while WebGetTool uses response.text directly for raw HTML output. Before returning, each tool truncates the content to the effective maximum length and appends "\n... [truncated]" when truncation occurs. Both tools format an output string that includes metadata headers ([URL:], [Status:], [Mode:], [Size:]) followed by the content, and they wrap the result in a ToolResult with success=True on success. HTTP-specific exceptions (httpx.HTTPError) are caught, logged with context, and returned as ToolResult failures containing an "HTTP error" message; other exceptions are similarly logged and returned with the exception string. The close methods asynchronously close their httpx clients to release network resources. WebFetchTool also explicitly removes any "extract_mode" kwarg passed in execute to guarantee it always returns text.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/shell.py

Description:
1. This module implements a ShellTool class for executing shell commands asynchronously.  
2. ShellTool is a Tool subclass that exposes metadata like name, description, parameters, and a configurable timeout.  
3. The tool reads configuration via get_config during initialization to set its default timeout and access allowed/blocked command lists.  
4. It validates commands using a private _is_command_safe method that consults is_blocked_shell_command and extract_shell_base_commands.  
5. The execute method runs commands with asyncio.create_subprocess_shell, capturing stdout and stderr.  
6. Execution supports an external abort Event passed via kwargs and enforces a timeout with asyncio.wait.  
7. The implementation decodes outputs as UTF-8 with replacement, combines stderr into the output with a “[stderr]” prefix, and truncates long outputs.  
8. The tool returns results as ToolResult objects indicating success, content, or an error message.  
9. Detailed logging is emitted for command execution, blocked commands, and exceptions via the project logger.  
10. Exceptions during execution are caught, logged, and converted into failed ToolResult responses.

Purpose:
This file exists to provide a controlled, asynchronous interface for running shell commands from the application while enforcing safety and resource limits. It centralizes command execution logic so other parts of the project can request shell operations without dealing with subprocess management, timeouts, or output handling. The module enforces security policies configured in the project's settings, including blocked patterns and an allowed command list, to reduce the risk of executing dangerous commands. It also integrates with the project's Tool and ToolResult abstractions so command execution results are returned in a consistent shape. By supporting an abort Event, it enables cooperative cancellation from higher-level workflows or task orchestrators. The timeout behavior is configurable and safeguarded by a minimum value to avoid accidental infinite waits. Output decoding, stderr merging, and truncation ensure that returned content is predictable in size and format for consumers such as UI components or logs. Logging calls provide observability for both successful runs and failure cases, aiding debugging and auditing. The tool isolates environment setup (like PATH) to provide consistent execution contexts across platforms. Centralizing subprocess creation and cleanup reduces duplication and the likelihood of resource leaks in the broader codebase. Overall, the file exists to offer a safe, observable, and standardized mechanism to run shell commands asynchronously within the project's architecture.

Key elements:
- ShellTool (class) (Tool subclass implementing shell execution).  
- name, description, timeout_seconds, parameters (class attributes describing the tool).  
- __init__ (method) (loads configuration and sets timeout).  
- _is_command_safe(command: str) -> tuple[bool, str] (private method that checks blocked patterns and allowed commands).  
- execute(command: str, timeout: int | None = None, **kwargs) -> ToolResult (async method that runs the command).  
- get_config (external call) (retrieves project configuration).  
- get_logger (external call) (obtains logger instance used for info/warning/error).  
- is_blocked_shell_command, extract_shell_base_commands (external utility calls used for safety checks).  
- asyncio.create_subprocess_shell, asyncio.create_task, asyncio.wait (asyncio APIs used to run and coordinate subprocess and abort handling).  
- ToolResult (external class) (used to return success, content, or error metadata).  
- os.environ and PATH handling (environment setup for subprocess).

Key logic:
The ShellTool initialization reads the project's configuration to set a default timeout and retain references to allowed/blocked command settings. Before running any command, execute calls _is_command_safe which first asks is_blocked_shell_command whether the command matches blocked patterns and returns explicit reasons for empty or unparseable commands. If an allowed_commands list is present in configuration, _is_command_safe extracts base commands with extract_shell_base_commands, normalizes them, and verifies each against the allowed set, returning a failure reason if any base command is not allowed. In execute, the tool logs the impending execution and determines the effective timeout, applying a minimum of one second. It checks for an abort_event passed via kwargs; if the abort Event is already set the method returns immediately with an aborted ToolResult. Environment variables are copied and PATH is ensured to have sensible defaults before spawning the subprocess. The command is executed with asyncio.create_subprocess_shell with stdout/stderr pipes, and a communicate task is created to read outputs. If an abort event is provided, a separate task waiting on abort_event.wait is created and both tasks are awaited concurrently using asyncio.wait with FIRST_COMPLETED. If the communicate task completes first, stdout and stderr bytes are decoded and post-processed. If the abort wait task completes first, the subprocess is killed, communication is cancelled and awaited or ignored if cancelled, and an aborted ToolResult is returned. If neither completes within the configured timeout, the subprocess is killed and the communicate task is cancelled, resulting in a timeout ToolResult. The implementation carefully handles asyncio.CancelledError to ensure subprocess is terminated and tasks are cancelled cleanly. After successful capture of output, stdout and stderr are decoded with UTF-8 replacement, stderr is appended with a “[stderr]” prefix if present, and the combined output is truncated to a 10000-character limit with a truncation marker that indicates total original length. The final ToolResult marks success based on the subprocess returncode and includes either the content or a “[no output]” placeholder. Any unexpected exceptions are logged and converted into a failed ToolResult containing the error string. Cleanup also cancels a pending abort wait task if it exists and suppresses its CancelledError to avoid leaking tasks.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/__init__.py

Description:
1. This module serves as the package initializer for the captain_claw.tools package.  
2. It imports key classes and functions from submodules within the same tools package.  
3. The imported names include registry-related types and many concrete Tool implementations.  
4. After importing, it defines the package's public API by populating the __all__ list.  
5. The file itself contains no function or class definitions beyond the import and export statements.  
6. Importing this module causes the referenced submodules to be imported and their top-level code to run.  
7. The module aggregates many tool implementations so callers can import them from a single location.  
8. The __all__ list explicitly enumerates the public symbols that should be exported from the package.  
9. The file acts as a convenient façade that centralizes tool names for external consumers.  
10. It is a lightweight module focused on namespace composition rather than implementing logic.

Purpose:
This module exists to present a single, consolidated public interface for the captain_claw.tools package so consumers can import frequently used tools and registry types from one location. By importing specific names from submodules and listing them in __all__, it documents and restricts what is considered the public API of the tools package. It reduces the need for external code to know internal submodule paths, simplifying imports like "from captain_claw.tools import ShellTool" instead of deeper module paths. The file ensures consistent exposure of registry primitives (Tool, ToolPolicy, ToolRegistry, ToolResult, get_tool_registry) alongside concrete Tool implementations. It collects a variety of tool implementations—file readers/writers, web fetchers, document extractors, and integrations—so the package consumer has immediate access to common functionality. The explicit __all__ helps tools like "from ... import *" behave predictably by listing intended exports. Because the initializer performs imports, it centralizes potential import-time side effects of submodules in one place. It also serves as documentation by naming the core building blocks and integrations the package provides. The module's existence supports maintainability by providing a single location to update which tools are public without editing every submodule's consumers. Finally, it keeps the package surface stable and readable, making it clear which components are part of the supported API.

Key elements:
- Tool (class from captain_claw.tools.registry; registry primitive)  
- ToolPolicy (class from captain_claw.tools.registry; policy abstraction)  
- ToolPolicyChain (class from captain_claw.tools.registry; policy composition)  
- ToolRegistry (class from captain_claw.tools.registry; registry management)  
- ToolResult (class from captain_claw.tools.registry; standardized result type)  
- get_tool_registry (function from captain_claw.tools.registry; access helper)  
- ShellTool (class from captain_claw.tools.shell; shell command tool)  
- ReadTool (class from captain_claw.tools.read; file read tool)  
- WriteTool (class from captain_claw.tools.write; file write tool)  
- GlobTool (class from captain_claw.tools.glob; filesystem globbing tool)  
- WebFetchTool (class from captain_claw.tools.web_fetch; HTTP fetcher)  
- WebGetTool (class from captain_claw.tools.web_fetch; HTTP GET helper)  
- WebSearchTool (class from captain_claw.tools.web_search; web search tool)  
- DocxExtractTool (class from captain_claw.tools.document_extract; DOCX extractor)  
- PdfExtractTool (class from captain_claw.tools.document_extract; PDF extractor)  
- PptxExtractTool (class from captain_claw.tools.document_extract; PPTX extractor)  
- XlsxExtractTool (class from captain_claw.tools.document_extract; XLSX extractor)  
- PocketTTSTool (class from captain_claw.tools.pocket_tts; text-to-speech tool)  
- SendMailTool (class from captain_claw.tools.send_mail; email sender)  
- GoogleDriveTool (class from captain_claw.tools.google_drive; Drive integration)  
- TodoTool (class from captain_claw.tools.todo; todo list tool)  
- ContactsTool (class from captain_claw.tools.contacts; contacts integration)  
- ScriptsTool (class from captain_claw.tools.scripts; script runner)  
- ApisTool (class from captain_claw.tools.apis; external API helper)  
- TypesenseTool (class from captain_claw.tools.typesense; Typesense integration)  
- __all__ (list; enumerates the module's public symbols)

Key logic:
1. The module's primary control action is importing selected names from submodules so they become attributes of the package namespace.  
2. Each import statement references a submodule and specific symbols, which triggers Python to load and execute those submodules if they are not already loaded.  
3. By importing registry types first, the file exposes foundational types used by other tool implementations.  
4. The subsequent imports gather concrete Tool implementations that depend on those registry types.  
5. After imports complete, the module constructs the __all__ list containing string names that mirror the imported symbols.  
6. The __all__ list determines which names are exported when clients use "from captain_claw.tools import *".  
7. The module does not perform runtime computation, configuration, or initialization beyond these imports and the __all__ assignment.  
8. Because imports execute submodule code, any top-level initialization in those modules runs as a side effect of importing this package initializer.  
9. The file acts as a namespace aggregator rather than implementing algorithms; its logic centers on composition and exposure of symbols.  
10. Changes to the imported list or __all__ alter the package's public API and affect how external code imports tools.  
11. The order of imports can influence import-time behavior if submodules have dependencies on each other or on registry symbols.  
12. Overall, the module's logic is simple and deterministic: import named symbols and publish them via __all__.
