## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/glob.py

Description:
1. This module implements a glob-based file discovery tool.  
2. It provides a GlobTool class that inherits from a generic Tool base class.  
3. The module defines metadata on the tool including a name, description, and a parameters JSON schema.  
4. The core feature is an asynchronous execute method that accepts a glob pattern, optional root, and a limit.  
5. The execute method uses pathlib.Path to combine a provided root with the pattern when a root is given.  
6. It delegates the actual filesystem globbing to Python's built-in glob.glob function executed inside an executor to avoid blocking the event loop.  
7. The method applies a configurable result limit and formats the matching file paths into a human-readable string.  
8. If no matches are found the tool returns a successful ToolResult with a message indicating that no files were found.  
9. Any exceptions raised during execution are caught, logged via the module logger, and returned as a failed ToolResult.  
10. The module imports and uses a ToolResult type to standardize success/error responses.

Purpose:
This file exists to expose a reusable, asynchronous file-finding capability within the codebase by wrapping standard globbing functionality in the project's Tool interface. By defining name, description, and parameters metadata it makes the glob operation discoverable and describable to any system components that inspect tool metadata (for example a tool registry or UI). The execute method offers a non-blocking implementation suitable for integration into asynchronous workflows and agents that expect coroutine-based tools. The parameters schema documents accepted inputs such as the glob pattern, optional root directory, and an optional limit on results, which supports validation and tooling around invocation. Returning a ToolResult ensures consistent success/error payload structure compatible with other tools in the same framework. The module centralizes error handling and logging so callers receive clear failure information while internal errors are recorded for debugging. Using run_in_executor to call glob.glob avoids blocking the event loop while reusing the standard library's globbing semantics including recursive patterns. The formatted output (count plus newline-separated paths) makes it straightforward for consumers to display or parse search results. Limiting results by slicing protects consumers from extremely large result sets by default. Overall, the file exists to provide a simple, documented, and async-friendly file search tool that fits into the project's tool registry and execution model.

Key elements:
- GlobTool (class) (subclass of Tool that implements the file-finding tool).  
- name (attribute) (tool identifier, set to "glob").  
- description (attribute) (short description of the tool's purpose).  
- parameters (dict) (JSON schema describing "pattern", optional "root", and "limit").  
- execute (async method) (main entry point that performs the glob search and returns a ToolResult).  
- pathlib.Path (usage) (used to join root and pattern when root is provided).  
- asyncio.get_event_loop and loop.run_in_executor (calls) (used to run glob.glob without blocking the event loop).  
- glob.glob (function) (standard library call used to perform the filesystem matching with recursive=True).  
- ToolResult (type) (used for structured success/error return values).  
- get_logger / log.error (logging) (module logger used to report failures).

Key logic:
The execute method begins by accepting a required pattern and optional root and limit parameters, with a default limit of 100. If a root is provided it constructs a combined pattern by joining the root path and the given pattern using pathlib.Path, ensuring the search starts from the specified directory. To perform the file matching without blocking asynchronous execution, it obtains the current event loop and schedules a synchronous glob.glob call in an executor via loop.run_in_executor. The glob.glob call is invoked with recursive=True so patterns like "**/*.py" will match across subdirectories. Once the executor returns the full list of matches, the method immediately applies slicing to enforce the provided limit and prevent returning more than the allowed number of results. If the matches list is empty after the search, the method returns a ToolResult that indicates success and contains a brief message stating no files were found for the provided pattern. If there are matches, the method composes a multi-line string that begins with "Found N file(s):" followed by each matched path on its own indented line, and returns that string in a successful ToolResult. The entire operation is wrapped in a try/except block; any exception raised during path handling, executor scheduling, or globbing is caught. On exception the code logs an error with the pattern and serialized error string using the module logger. After logging, the method returns a ToolResult marked as a failure with the error message included so callers can react accordingly. The method relies only on standard library globbing semantics and the surrounding Tool/ToolResult types to integrate results into the broader tool execution framework.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/apis.py

Description:
1. This module provides an ApisTool class for managing a persistent collection of API definitions across sessions.  
2. The tool registers metadata including name, description, and a JSON schema for accepted parameters.  
3. The main entrypoint is an asynchronous execute method that dispatches actions like add, list, search, info, update, and remove.  
4. Each action is implemented as a static asynchronous helper method prefixed with an underscore.  
5. The add action validates required fields and calls the session manager to create a new API record.  
6. The list and search actions fetch multiple API entries and format concise textual summaries.  
7. The info action retrieves a single API and assembles detailed fields into a multi-line description.  
8. The update action builds a dictionary of provided fields and calls the session manager to apply changes.  
9. The remove action verifies existence and delegates deletion to the session manager.  
10. Errors are caught at the top level, logged, and returned as failed ToolResult objects.

Purpose:
This file exists to centralize CRUD-like operations for APIs stored in the application's persistent session manager. It exposes a single tool implementing a consistent interface so other parts of the system can discover and invoke API management actions uniformly. By defining a parameters schema the tool makes its expected inputs explicit for tooling, validation, or UI generation. It delegates all storage and retrieval responsibilities to the session manager to keep persistence details out of the tool. The module formats human-readable results for list, search, and info actions so that callers receive concise textual output suitable for display. Validation checks prevent missing required fields from being sent to the session manager and provide clear error messages to callers. The update implementation supports partial updates by collecting only provided fields and refusing to call the session manager when nothing is supplied. The list and search methods impose default limits when requesting many items, providing predictable output sizes. Centralized logging of unexpected exceptions helps with troubleshooting and auditing of tool usage. The tool returns ToolResult instances uniformly for success and failure, integrating with the project's tooling framework. Overall, this module exists to be the authoritative, safe, and user-friendly interface for registering, discovering, inspecting, modifying, and deleting API definitions used by the application.

Key elements:
- ApisTool (class; subclass of Tool implementing API management actions).  
- name, description, parameters (module/class-level metadata; defines tool identity and JSON schema).  
- execute (async method; dispatches based on action parameter and handles top-level errors).  
- _add (static async; validates inputs and calls sm.create_api).  
- _list (static async; calls sm.list_apis and formats entries).  
- _search (static async; validates query and calls sm.search_apis).  
- _info (static async; calls sm.select_api and composes detailed output).  
- _update (static async; builds kwargs from provided fields and calls sm.update_api).  
- _remove (static async; calls sm.select_api then sm.delete_api).  
- get_session_manager (external call; obtains the session manager instance).  
- ToolResult (imported type; used for standardized success/error responses).  
- get_logger / log (logging setup; used to report errors).

Key logic:
The execute method begins by extracting an optional session identifier from kwargs and acquiring the session manager instance. It uses the provided action string to route the request to the corresponding helper method and wraps the entire dispatch in a try/except to log and return errors as ToolResult failures. The _add helper enforces that name and base_url are present and non-empty, then calls sm.create_api with provided fields and the source session, returning a success message containing a short form of the new API id. The _list helper requests up to 50 APIs from sm.list_apis, handles the empty case with a friendly message, and otherwise builds one-line summaries that include an index, optional auth type, base URL, use count, and shortened id. The _search helper requires a non-empty query, calls sm.search_apis with a 20-item limit, and formats matching results similarly to list. The _info helper requires an api_id, selects the API via sm.select_api, and then conditionally includes available attributes (auth, credentials, endpoints, description, purpose, tags, use count, timestamps) in a multi-line output. The _update helper requires an api_id, resolves the target via sm.select_api, then collects only the provided non-None fields into a kwargs dict and returns an error if no fields were given; it calls sm.update_api and reports success or failure accordingly. The _remove helper verifies the api exists with sm.select_api, calls sm.delete_api, and reports whether deletion succeeded. Throughout these helpers, returned messages are plain text composed for human consumption rather than structured objects. Top-level exception handling logs the action and error string and ensures the tool reports failure rather than raising. The module relies on the session manager for all persistent operations and on ToolResult to normalize function outputs.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/scripts.py

Description:
1. This module defines a ScriptsTool class that provides persistent cross-session management for script/file metadata.  
2. The tool exposes a parameters JSON schema describing accepted fields and the allowed actions.  
3. The main entrypoint is an asynchronous execute method that dispatches based on the action parameter.  
4. Supported actions are add, list, search, info, update, and remove, each handled by a corresponding static async helper.  
5. The add action validates required inputs and delegates creation to the session manager.  
6. The list and search actions query the session manager for matching script records and format human-readable summaries.  
7. The info action retrieves a single script record and assembles a multi-line detail view containing available fields.  
8. The update action selects a script, builds an update payload from provided fields, and requests the session manager to apply changes.  
9. The remove action validates existence and asks the session manager to delete the script.  
10. Errors during execution are logged and returned as failed ToolResult objects.

Purpose:
This file exists to provide a single, discoverable tool that other parts of the application can invoke to manage script metadata consistently. It centralizes CRUD-like operations for scripts so persistence details are encapsulated behind a uniform interface. By declaring a parameters schema it makes expected inputs explicit for validation, tooling, or UI generation. The tool persists and queries attributes such as name, file_path, description, purpose, language, created_reason, tags, usage counts, and timestamps via the session manager. It therefore acts as the application surface for registering, locating, inspecting, updating, and removing script records that survive across sessions. The implementation focuses on input validation, formatting of textual summaries, and clear success/error ToolResult responses. The class logs errors to aid debugging and returns structured failure messages instead of raising exceptions outward. Static helper methods keep each action's logic isolated and testable. The module avoids directly handling storage and instead relies on the session manager API, keeping concerns separated. Overall, it exists to make script metadata operations predictable, discoverable, and uniform for callers of the tools registry.

Key elements:
- ScriptsTool (class) — inherits from Tool and encapsulates script management functionality.  
- name, description (class attrs) — human-readable tool identity and long description.  
- parameters (class attr) — JSON schema specifying accepted properties and required action.  
- execute (async method) — main dispatcher that routes actions to helper methods and handles exceptions.  
- _add (static async) — validates inputs and calls session manager create_script.  
- _list (static async) — calls session manager list_scripts and formats a numbered summary.  
- _search (static async) — validates query and calls session manager search_scripts to format matches.  
- _info (static async) — calls session manager select_script and builds a detailed multi-line view.  
- _update (static async) — selects a script, assembles update kwargs, and calls session manager update_script.  
- _remove (static async) — selects a script and calls session manager delete_script.  
- get_session_manager (imported function) — used to obtain the session manager instance.  
- get_logger / log (imported) — logging facility used to record errors.  
- ToolResult (imported) — standardized return object for success/error responses.  
- session manager methods (external calls) — create_script, list_scripts, search_scripts, select_script, update_script, delete_script.

Key logic:
The module's control flow centers on the execute method which first extracts an optional session_id from kwargs and obtains the session manager instance. execute then checks the action string and forwards the call to the matching static helper, returning its ToolResult; unknown actions immediately produce a failure ToolResult. A top-level try/except around the dispatch ensures any unexpected exception is logged and returned as an error ToolResult. Each helper method performs focused validation for required parameters and returns explicit error ToolResult objects when validation fails. The _add helper requires a non-empty name and file_path, calls sm.create_script with provided metadata, and returns a success message including the short form of the new item's id. The _list helper requests up to 50 scripts, returns a "no scripts" message when empty, or formats each entry with index, optional language, path, use count, and truncated id. The _search helper requires a non-empty query, calls sm.search_scripts with a limit, and formats results similarly to list. The _info helper requires a script identifier, selects the script via sm.select_script, and conditionally appends available fields (language, description, purpose, tags, usage, timestamps) to a multi-line response. The _update helper selects the target script, accumulates only the provided fields into an update payload, refuses to proceed if no fields are supplied, and calls sm.update_script, returning success or failure accordingly. The _remove helper ensures the script exists via selection, calls sm.delete_script, and reports deletion success or failure. All helpers are asynchronous and static, enabling predictable concurrency behavior and making them easy to call without class state.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/document_extract.py

Description:
1. This module implements document extraction tools that convert PDF, DOCX, XLSX, and PPTX files into Markdown.  
2. It defines helper routines for normalizing text, escaping Markdown table cells, truncating output, and validating file paths.  
3. DOCX extraction reads the ZIP package, parses word/document.xml with ElementTree, and renders paragraphs and tables as Markdown.  
4. XLSX extraction reads shared strings and workbook relationships from the XLSX ZIP, resolves sheet targets, and emits sheet data as Markdown tables.  
5. PPTX extraction enumerates slide XML files, collects paragraph text from drawingML nodes, and formats slides as Markdown sections.  
6. PDF extraction attempts to import pypdf, reads pages up to a limit, and extracts text to Markdown while returning a dependency error if pypdf is not present.  
7. The module exposes four asynchronous Tool subclasses (PdfExtractTool, DocxExtractTool, XlsxExtractTool, PptxExtractTool) with JSON parameter schemas.  
8. Each Tool validates that the provided path exists and is a file, then runs blocking extraction logic on a thread via asyncio.to_thread.  
9. Extracted content is normalized, assembled into Markdown structures (headings, lists, tables), and truncated to a requested character limit.  
10. The code logs exceptions and returns structured ToolResult objects indicating success or error conditions.

Purpose:
This file exists to centralize file-format-specific extraction logic and present a uniform Markdown output interface for downstream consumers. It provides programmatic tools that other parts of the project can call to convert common document types into searchable, displayable Markdown. By grouping format parsing and normalization here, callers need not manage ZIP/XML parsing, shared strings resolution, or pypdf usage themselves. The tools expose parameter schemas so they can be invoked with validated inputs and consistent options such as maximum characters, pages, rows, or slides. Running heavy extraction on background threads via asyncio.to_thread keeps the asynchronous API non-blocking while reusing synchronous XML and ZIP parsing code. The module also encapsulates common sanitization behaviors, like escaping Markdown table separators and normalizing whitespace, ensuring consistent output across formats. Error handling for malformed archives, missing XML parts, and missing optional dependencies is centralized so callers receive clear messages. Logging of exceptions provides diagnostics while ToolResult objects deliver machine-readable status and content. The design supports safe truncation to avoid returning excessively large payloads. Overall, this module exists to make document-to-Markdown conversion reliable, consistent, and easy to call from the larger application.

Key elements:
- _escape_md_cell (function) — escapes '|' and newlines for Markdown table cells.  
- _normalize_text (function) — collapses internal whitespace while preserving line boundaries.  
- _truncate_markdown (function) — trims Markdown to a max character length with a truncation suffix.  
- _require_existing_file (function) — validates and resolves a filesystem path to an existing file.  
- _local_name (function) — strips XML namespace to obtain the local tag name.  
- _extract_docx_paragraph_text (function) — concatenates text nodes from a DOCX paragraph element.  
- _extract_docx_table_markdown (function) — converts a DOCX table element into Markdown table lines.  
- _extract_docx_markdown (function) — orchestrates DOCX document.xml parsing and Markdown rendering.  
- _xlsx_col_to_index / _xlsx_index_to_col (functions) — convert between Excel column letters and zero-based indices.  
- _extract_xlsx_markdown (function) — parses XLSX archive, shared strings, workbook relationships, and renders sheets as Markdown tables.  
- _extract_pptx_markdown (function) — finds slide XML entries and extracts paragraph text into slide sections.  
- _extract_pdf_markdown (function) — uses pypdf to read PDF pages and extract text; returns content and error.  
- PdfExtractTool, DocxExtractTool, XlsxExtractTool, PptxExtractTool (classes) — Tool subclasses exposing parameter schemas and async execute entrypoints.  
- External dependencies referenced (modules): zipfile, xml.etree.ElementTree (ET), re, asyncio, pathlib.Path, pypdf (optional), captain_claw.logging.get_logger, captain_claw.tools.registry.Tool and ToolResult.

Key logic:
1. The module begins with small utility functions to sanitize and normalize extracted text and to enforce a maximum returned character count.  
2. _require_existing_file centralizes path resolution and existence checks so each Tool execute method can quickly validate input before extraction.  
3. DOCX extraction opens the .docx ZIP, reads word/document.xml, locates the document body, and iterates child elements to classify paragraphs and tables.  
4. Paragraphs are processed by collecting all w:t nodes; paragraph styles and numbering properties are inspected to render headings and list items appropriately.  
5. DOCX tables are traversed row-by-row and cell-by-cell; cell paragraphs are concatenated, empty rows are skipped, the table is normalized to a consistent column width, and Markdown table syntax is generated with header and separator rows.  
6. XLSX extraction first reads sharedStrings (if present) to resolve string cell indices, then parses workbook.xml and its relationship file to map sheets to their XML parts inside the archive.  
7. For each sheet, rows are iterated up to max_rows; each cell's column index is computed from its reference, its type (inlineStr, s, b, or default) is used to determine how to read and normalize the value, and rows without content are skipped.  
8. The XLSX logic computes a header row (using existing header cells or fallback column letters), pads rows to equal width, and produces Markdown table lines with escaped cell content.  
9. PPTX extraction enumerates entries matching the slide filename pattern, sorts them, parses each slide XML, collects drawingML text nodes, and emits slide headings followed by bulleted paragraph text or a marker for empty slides.  
10. PDF extraction attempts to import pypdf, opening the reader and iterating pages up to max_pages, extracting page text via page.extract_text(), normalizing it, and assembling per-page Markdown sections; if pypdf is unavailable a descriptive error is returned.  
11. Each Tool subclass defines a JSON parameters schema, uses _require_existing_file in execute to validate the path, and then calls the corresponding extraction function on a background thread with asyncio.to_thread to avoid blocking the event loop.  
12. Returned content from extractors is truncated with _truncate_markdown according to max_chars before being wrapped in a successful ToolResult; known exceptions like KeyError or zipfile.BadZipFile are caught and translated into user-facing error messages.  
13. The module logs unexpected exceptions with context (path and error) and returns failed ToolResult objects when runtime errors occur.  
14. Overall, control flow emphasizes safe file validation, format-specific parsing strategies based on XML/ZIP structure, normalization and escaping for Markdown safety, and asynchronous wrappers that provide a consistent interface to callers.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/web_search.py

Description:
1. This module implements a WebSearchTool class that uses the Brave Search API to perform web searches.  
2. It defines the tool's metadata including name, description, and a JSON schema for accepted parameters.  
3. The class constructs an async httpx.AsyncClient with a custom User-Agent for performing requests.  
4. The execute method validates the incoming query, reads configuration, and enforces that the provider is Brave.  
5. API key resolution is attempted from configuration first and then from the BRAVE_API_KEY environment variable.  
6. The tool builds request parameters such as count, offset, country, search language, freshness, and safesearch.  
7. Requests include an X-Subscription-Token header for authentication and expect JSON responses from Brave.  
8. Response parsing extracts web results and formats them into a plain-text list with titles, URLs, and snippets.  
9. A helper _clean_text normalizes whitespace and truncates long fields for safe display in results.  
10. Errors from HTTP status failures and other exceptions are logged and returned as ToolResult error responses.

Purpose:
This file provides an integrated web search capability for the project by wrapping Brave Search into a reusable Tool object. It exists so higher-level components can perform web lookups through a consistent Tool interface and receive normalized, safe text output. The configuration-driven design allows administrators to supply API keys and override base URL, timeout, and default result limits without changing code. It centralizes authentication logic including support for an environment variable fallback (BRAVE_API_KEY). Parameter validation and clamping logic (e.g., min/max count and non-negative offsets) protect downstream consumers from invalid or excessive requests. The tool enforces a single supported provider ("brave") to keep implementation focused and predictable. Formatting of results into a compact, human-readable text block simplifies presentation for agents or logs that consume ToolResult content. Error handling captures HTTP status details and response bodies when available to aid debugging. The async client pattern and an explicit close method enable clean resource management in async runtimes. Overall, the module exists to offer a reliable, configurable, and easy-to-use web search primitive for the larger system.

Key elements:
- WebSearchTool (class) — main Tool implementation for Brave Search.  
- name, description, parameters (class attributes) — metadata and parameter schema.  
- __init__ (method) — constructs httpx.AsyncClient with custom User-Agent.  
- _clean_text (static method) — normalizes whitespace and truncates output.  
- execute (async method) — performs validation, builds request, calls Brave API, and formats results.  
- close (async method) — closes the httpx client.  
- httpx.AsyncClient (dependency) — used for async HTTP requests.  
- get_config (import) — reads runtime configuration for tool settings.  
- get_logger (import) — used for logging errors.  
- Tool, ToolResult (imports) — base types from the tools registry used for interface and results.  
- BRAVE_API_KEY (environment variable) — alternate source for the API key.  
- X-Subscription-Token header (HTTP header) — used for API authentication.

Key logic:
1. On construction, the class creates an httpx.AsyncClient configured to follow redirects and present a specific User-Agent.  
2. The _clean_text helper normalizes whitespace and enforces a maximum character length, appending an explicit truncation marker when needed.  
3. The execute method first trims and validates the required query string and returns a ToolResult error if it is missing.  
4. It loads tool-specific configuration via get_config and ensures the configured provider is "brave", otherwise returning an error.  
5. The method resolves the API key from configuration or the BRAVE_API_KEY environment variable and fails early if no key is found.  
6. It computes effective request parameters: base URL, timeout, default and requested counts (clamped between 1 and 20), offset (non-negative), and a validated safesearch value.  
7. Optional parameters country, search_lang, and freshness are included only when provided and non-empty.  
8. Headers are prepared with Accept: application/json and X-Subscription-Token set to the resolved API key.  
9. An asynchronous GET request is issued to the Brave endpoint with prepared params and headers; response.raise_for_status() is used to surface HTTP errors.  
10. On a successful response the JSON payload is inspected for a "web" block and a "results" list; non-list or malformed data is tolerated by normalizing to an empty list.  
11. Each result dictionary is sanitized using _clean_text for title and description, and results are rendered into a numbered plain-text summary including URL and snippet.  
12. HTTPStatusError handling extracts response body where possible, creates a concise error detail (including truncated body), logs the failure, and returns a ToolResult with the error.  
13. A generic exception handler logs and returns other unexpected errors as ToolResult failures.  
14. The close method asynchronously closes the underlying httpx client to release network resources.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/google_drive.py

Description:
1. This module implements a GoogleDriveTool class that provides actions to list, search, read, get info, upload, create, and update files on Google Drive.  
2. It communicates with the Google Drive REST API v3 using an httpx.AsyncClient and OAuth2 Bearer tokens obtained from a session-managed GoogleOAuthManager.  
3. The tool exposes a JSON schema for accepted parameters and validates required action names before dispatching.  
4. For reading files it inspects file metadata and either exports Google Workspace documents, downloads and extracts binary formats, lists folder contents, or returns text downloads for plain files.  
5. Exported Google Workspace files are requested in mapped export MIME types (with a fallback for unsupported markdown exports) and truncated if larger than a configured maximum.  
6. Binary files that match known extractable MIME types are downloaded to a temporary file and processed by dynamically loaded extract tools.  
7. Upload and create operations use a multipart/related upload implementation that constructs a boundary-delimited body and posts it to the Drive upload endpoint.  
8. Update operations send a media patch request to replace file content, handling either provided text content or a local file.  
9. The module centralizes error handling by translating HTTP status errors into user-friendly ToolResult messages for common Drive error codes.  
10. Utility helpers include metadata retrieval, size formatting, extraction tool resolution, and a close method to terminate the internal HTTP client.

Purpose:
This file exists to encapsulate all interactions with Google Drive into a single reusable Tool object so higher-level components can perform Drive operations without dealing with raw HTTP or OAuth details. It centralizes token retrieval and scope validation to ensure requests are authorized and the Drive scope is present before any API call. By providing a uniform execute(...) entrypoint and a parameters schema, the tool fits into the project's tool registry and can be invoked programmatically with predictable inputs and outputs. The read path handles multiple content types so the rest of the application receives readable text or descriptive errors regardless of whether a file is a Google Doc, a binary Office file, a PDF, or plain text. Upload, create, and update flows are implemented to support both Google Workspace conversion and standard file uploads, allowing users to create native Google Docs or store plain files. The module performs client-side checks and truncation for large content to protect downstream consumers from excessive payloads. Error mapping converts Drive API errors into concise messages that explain authentication, permission, not-found, and rate-limit issues, improving operator experience. The design avoids external Google SDKs by using direct REST calls, keeping dependencies minimal and the behavior transparent. Dynamic loading of extract tools enables integration with existing file-extraction utilities in the codebase without hard-coding those implementations. Overall, it exists to provide a high-level, robust, and consistent interface for Drive operations within the Captain Claw system while handling common edge cases like large files, conversion fallbacks, and multi-drive support.

Key elements:
- GoogleDriveTool (class) (main tool providing Drive actions and integrating with the tool registry)  
- name, description, parameters (class attributes) (tool metadata and JSON schema)  
- __init__ (constructor) (creates httpx.AsyncClient with custom User-Agent)  
- execute(action, **kwargs) (dispatch method, token retrieval, error handling)  
- _get_access_token (token retrieval via GoogleOAuthManager and session manager)  
- _auth_headers (builds Authorization header)  
- _handle_http_error (maps HTTPStatusError to ToolResult with friendly messages)  
- _action_list, _action_search, _action_read, _action_info, _action_upload, _action_create, _action_update (action handlers)  
- _export_google_file, _download_and_extract, _download_as_text (reading/exporting helpers for different mime types)  
- _multipart_upload (constructs multipart/related upload body and posts to upload API)  
- _get_file_metadata (fetches file metadata from Drive)  
- _get_extract_tool (dynamic importer for extract tools like pdf_extract, docx_extract)  
- _format_size (human-readable byte size formatting)  
- close (closes the internal httpx client)  
- Constants: _DRIVE_API, _UPLOAD_API, _DRIVE_SCOPE, _GOOGLE_EXPORT_MAP, _EXTRACTABLE_MIMES, _MAX_READ_BYTES (configuration and mappings)  
- External deps: httpx.AsyncClient, GoogleOAuthManager, get_session_manager, Tool/ToolResult, tempfile, io, json, pathlib.Path

Key logic:
The module's primary control flow begins in execute(...), which strips injected runtime kwargs, attempts to obtain an OAuth access token via a GoogleOAuthManager-backed session, and then dispatches to a specific action handler based on the provided action string. Token retrieval checks that tokens exist and that the Drive scope is granted, raising user-oriented RuntimeError messages if not. Handlers are looked up in a mapping and called with the resolved token; HTTP and generic exceptions are caught and converted into ToolResult error responses, with HTTPStatusError routed through a dedicated mapper that translates common status codes into helpful messages. Listing constructs a Drive files query for the given parent folder, requests the configured fields, and formats results into a readable list including size (formatted) and modified date. Search builds an escaped query that searches both filename and full text, uses a pageSize limit, and optionally applies ordering; it formats matched files similarly to list. Reading begins by fetching file metadata; behavior then branches by MIME type: Google Workspace types are exported using mapped export MIME types (with a fallback for markdown), extractable binary types are downloaded to a temporary file and passed to an extraction tool, folders invoke the list action for that folder, and other files are downloaded as text with truncation and decoding checks. Binary extraction enforces a maximum download size and writes content to a temp file before invoking a dynamically resolved extract tool; temporary files are cleaned up in a finally block. Upload and create flows build metadata and content bytes, determine content types (including guesses via mimetypes), and call _multipart_upload to send a multipart/related request to the Drive upload endpoint, optionally requesting conversion to Google Workspace types. Update performs a media patch against the upload API to replace file contents and supports either direct text content or uploading from a local path. The multipart upload implementation composes a custom boundary, writes the JSON metadata and raw content into an in-memory bytes buffer following Drive's multipart spec, posts with appropriate headers, and returns the JSON response. Utility helpers provide metadata fetching, extract-tool lookup by name with local imports, human-readable size formatting, and an async close method to terminate the httpx client. The module consistently enforces size limits configured by _MAX_READ_BYTES and other thresholds to avoid excessive memory or processing.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/todo.py

Description:
1. This module implements a TodoTool class that provides a simple persistent cross-session to-do list manager.  
2. The tool is a subclass of Tool and exposes a JSON schema for parameters that includes actions "add", "list", "update", and "remove".  
3. The module extracts an optional session identifier from provided kwargs and obtains a session manager via get_session_manager().  
4. The execute method dispatches based on the "action" parameter and forwards other parameters to internal helper methods.  
5. Helper methods _add, _list, _update, and _remove are defined as async static methods that interact with the session manager to perform storage operations.  
6. _add validates content, supplies default responsible and priority values, and calls sm.create_todo to persist a new item.  
7. _list queries sm.list_todos with optional filters and formats results into a numbered plain-text listing that includes truncated item ids.  
8. _update and _remove both select a target item via sm.select_todo and then call sm.update_todo or sm.delete_todo, returning success or error ToolResult values.  
9. The module uses a module-level _PRIORITY_ORDER mapping and a logger obtained via get_logger, and it wraps execution in a try/except to log and return errors.  
10. All operations return ToolResult objects indicating success, content messages, or error descriptions suitable for user-facing responses.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a reusable tool that external components can call to manage persistent to-do items across user or bot sessions.  
2. It centralizes to-do manipulation logic so callers need only specify a high-level action and minimal parameters instead of interacting with low-level storage APIs.  
3. By defining a JSON parameters schema the tool documents expected inputs and constrains allowed values for status, priority, and responsible fields.  
4. The tool integrates with the session management subsystem to attribute created items to a source session and to optionally scope listings to a session.  
5. It supports both human and bot assignment semantics through a responsible field and provides default behavior for common add operations.  
6. The list action supports simple filtering by status and responsible party, enabling callers to request focused views without post-filtering.  
7. Update and remove actions encapsulate selection semantics and error reporting when an item cannot be found, abstracting selection logic via the session manager.  
8. Returning ToolResult objects keeps the tool consistent with the broader tool registry and execution framework used by the project.  
9. The module logs unexpected exceptions to aid debugging while converting runtime failures into structured ToolResult errors for downstream handling.  
10. It provides textual, human-readable summaries for operations (e.g., created/updated/removed messages and formatted list lines) to simplify presentation in chat or UI contexts.  
11. The presence of a priority ordering mapping suggests integration with priority-aware sorting or display elsewhere, even though the mapping is not used within the file's methods.  
12. Overall, the module exists to make to-do item lifecycle operations simple, consistent, and accessible to other subsystems without exposing storage implementation details.

Key elements:
- _PRIORITY_ORDER (dict) (module-level priority ranking mapping: urgent→0, high→1, normal→2, low→3).  
- log (logger) (module logger via get_logger for error logging).  
- TodoTool (class) (Tool subclass implementing the to-do management interface).  
- TodoTool.name (str) (tool name "todo").  
- TodoTool.description (str) (human-readable tool description used by registry).  
- TodoTool.parameters (dict) (JSON schema describing accepted parameters and enums).  
- execute (async method) (dispatches "add", "list", "update", "remove" actions and handles exceptions).  
- _add (async static method) (validates content; calls sm.create_todo; returns creation message).  
- _list (async static method) (calls sm.list_todos; formats and returns a numbered list).  
- _update (async static method) (validates todo_id; selects item via sm.select_todo; calls sm.update_todo).  
- _remove (async static method) (validates todo_id; selects item via sm.select_todo; calls sm.delete_todo).  
- get_session_manager (external call) (used to obtain session manager instance).  
- ToolResult (type) (used for all method return values to indicate success/content/error).

Key logic:
1. The execute method begins by extracting a session identifier from kwargs and obtaining the session manager instance for subsequent storage operations.  
2. It uses the provided "action" parameter to choose which internal async helper to run: "add" → _add, "list" → _list, "update" → _update, "remove" → _remove.  
3. Each helper method performs its own input validation: _add requires non-empty content, while _update and _remove require a todo_id.  
4. For creating items, _add supplies defaults for responsible ("bot") and priority ("normal") when not provided, and passes tags and context through to sm.create_todo.  
5. _add returns a ToolResult with a success flag and a short message including the first eight characters of the created item's id.  
6. Listing queries sm.list_todos with limit and optional status/responsible/session filters, then iterates results to build formatted lines that include priority, responsible, content, status, optional tags, and truncated ids.  
7. The update flow selects the target via sm.select_todo(todo_id); if selection fails it returns an error ToolResult; if selection succeeds it calls sm.update_todo with provided fields and reports failure or success accordingly.  
8. The remove flow similarly selects the item and then calls sm.delete_todo, returning a failure ToolResult if deletion did not succeed or a success message when it does.  
9. All helper methods interact exclusively with the session manager interface (create_todo, list_todos, select_todo, update_todo, delete_todo) to keep storage details encapsulated.  
10. The module-level _PRIORITY_ORDER exists as a mapping for priority ranking but is not referenced by the implemented methods, indicating either future use or external reliance on the mapping.  
11. Errors raised during execute are caught, logged with context including the action and error string, and converted into a ToolResult with success=False.  
12. Output from each operation is deliberately textual and concise, optimized for presentation in user-facing contexts (chat/UIs) rather than returning raw data structures.
