## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/typesense.py

Description:
1. This module defines a TypesenseTool class that exposes index, search, and delete operations against a configured Typesense deep memory collection.  
2. The tool is a subclass of Tool and declares a JSON parameters schema describing allowed actions and their inputs.  
3. It prefers to delegate to an injected DeepMemoryIndex for chunking, embedding, hybrid search, and schema management when available.  
4. When DeepMemoryIndex is not provided the tool performs raw HTTP operations against a Typesense server using httpx.  
5. The tool lazily constructs an httpx.AsyncClient with configured timeouts and an API key header.  
6. Before performing operations it ensures the target collection exists, creating it via the canonical schema template if necessary.  
7. Indexing computes a deterministic doc_id using an SHA-1 hash of the reference and text snippet and either calls deep_memory.index_document or upserts a single document via the import endpoint.  
8. Searching uses deep_memory.search to run a hybrid query and format results or falls back to the /documents/search endpoint and formats hits.  
9. Deletion supports removing by document_id (deleting all chunks) or by a filter expression, delegating to DeepMemoryIndex when present or issuing HTTP delete requests otherwise.  
10. The module centralizes error handling for httpx and JSON errors, returning ToolResult objects indicating success or failure.  

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a tightly controlled interface for LLMs or other components to interact with application deep memory stored in Typesense.  
2. It restricts available operations to indexing, searching, and deletion and prevents creation or arbitrary selection of collections by callers.  
3. By routing through DeepMemoryIndex when available the tool leverages consistent chunking, embedding generation, doc_id management, and search ranking logic already implemented elsewhere in the project.  
4. The fallback HTTP paths exist to allow the tool to function even when DeepMemoryIndex is not wired in, using the configured Typesense host, port, protocol, and API key.  
5. Collection bootstrap code ensures the required schema is present and appends an embedding field sized from deep_memory configuration when appropriate.  
6. The tool exposes a parameter schema for validation and for the tools registry so callers know which inputs are accepted and required.  
7. It centralizes HTTP client configuration (timeouts, headers) and cleans up the client on close to avoid resource leaks.  
8. Error handling converts various httpx exceptions and JSON decoding errors into user-friendly ToolResult error messages and logs warnings for operational issues.  
9. Index and search handlers format human-readable results that include source tags, references, scores, and truncated previews to make responses concise and informative.  
10. Delete handlers support both single-document deletion by doc_id (removing all chunks) and bulk deletion by filter expressions to enable flexible memory management operations.  
11. Overall, the module exists to provide a safe, observable, and consistent bridge between the application’s tools subsystem and the Typesense-backed deep memory store.  
12. It is designed to be resilient by preferring application-level index/search implementations while remaining capable of direct Typesense operations for simpler deployments or bootstrapping scenarios.  

Key elements:
- TypesenseTool (class) (Tool subclass implementing index/search/delete backed by Typesense or DeepMemoryIndex).  
- name, description, timeout_seconds, parameters (class attributes describing tool metadata and JSON schema).  
- __init__ (initializes deep_memory reference, base URL, API key, default collection, timeouts, and lazy client state).  
- _get_collection (returns the enforced collection name from DeepMemoryIndex or default configuration).  
- _ensure_collection (creates/validates collection using DeepMemoryIndex.ensure_collection or raw HTTP and the _COLLECTION_SCHEMA_TEMPLATE).  
- _get_client (lazy-initializes httpx.AsyncClient with configured timeouts and API key header).  
- execute (dispatch method that validates config, ensures collection, routes actions, and handles exceptions).  
- _action_index (handles indexing, computes doc_id via hashlib.sha1, delegates to deep_memory.index_document or POSTs to /documents/import).  
- _action_search (handles query validation and per-page limits, delegates to deep_memory.search or GETs /documents/search and formats results).  
- _action_delete (supports deletion by document_id or filter_by, delegates to deep_memory or issues HTTP DELETE calls).  
- close (async cleanup to close the httpx client).  
- External dependencies: httpx (async HTTP), get_config (config access), get_logger (logging), hashlib/json/time, DeepMemoryIndex and _COLLECTION_SCHEMA_TEMPLATE from captain_claw.deep_memory, ToolResult and Tool base from tools.registry.  

Key logic:
1. The execute method first removes injected runtime kwargs, checks that an API key and collection name are configured, and then attempts to ensure the collection exists before dispatching to an action handler.  
2. A simple handlers mapping routes the action string to _action_index, _action_search, or _action_delete; unknown actions return a ToolResult error.  
3. Exception handling around handler invocation converts httpx connection, HTTP status, generic HTTP, JSON decode, and other exceptions into ToolResult responses and logs warnings for unexpected errors.  
4. _ensure_collection returns immediately if the collection was already ensured; if a DeepMemoryIndex is present it delegates to its ensure_collection method synchronously.  
5. In the fallback creation path _ensure_collection checks for collection existence with a GET, constructs a schema from the canonical template, appends an embedding field when embedding dimensions are configured, and attempts to POST the schema, treating 409 as a non-error.  
6. _get_client lazy-initializes an httpx.AsyncClient with configured timeout and connection timeout values and sets the X-TYPESENSE-API-KEY and Content-Type headers.  
7. _action_index validates that text is present, creates a tag list from a comma-separated string, and computes a deterministic doc_id by hashing reference and a text prefix; if deep_memory exists it calls index_document and returns a summary of chunk count and metadata.  
8. When DeepMemoryIndex is absent the index path constructs a single document dictionary with doc_id, doc_id-backed fields, text, chunk_index 0, and updated_at timestamp, serializes it, and posts it to /collections/{coll}/documents/import with action=upsert.  
9. _action_search enforces a non-empty query and a per_page limit, then either calls deep_memory.search and formats each result with snippet truncation, source tag, location, and score, or performs an HTTP GET to /documents/search with q, query_by, per_page, and optional filter_by and formats hits from the JSON response.  
10. _action_delete requires either document_id or filter_by; for document_id it either calls deep_memory.delete_document (which deletes all chunks) or issues a DELETE with a doc_id filter; for filter-based deletion it delegates to deep_memory.delete_by_filter or issues a DELETE with the provided filter.  
11. HTTP responses are raised for status (resp.raise_for_status()) to surface HTTP errors to the centralized exception handlers; JSON responses are parsed to extract found/hits or num_deleted values to include in ToolResult content.  
12. The close method asynchronously closes the httpx client if present and not already closed to release network resources and reset the client state.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/tools/read.py

Description:
1. This module defines a ReadTool class that provides an asynchronous execute method for reading file contents.  
2. The tool is declared with a name ("read"), a short description, and a JSON parameters schema that accepts path, limit, and offset.  
3. execute accepts a path string and optional numeric limit and offset values and returns a ToolResult describing success or failure.  
4. The implementation resolves the given path using pathlib.Path.expanduser and resolve, and checks whether the target exists.  
5. If the file is not found on the filesystem the tool attempts to resolve the path via an optional _file_registry passed in kwargs.  
6. If registry resolution fails it also inspects an optional _saved_base_path before reporting a not-found error.  
7. The tool rejects non-file paths and enforces a hard file size limit of 100,000 bytes, returning an error if exceeded.  
8. When allowed, the file is read as UTF-8, split into lines, and sliced according to the offset and limit parameters.  
9. The returned content is prefixed with metadata including the resolved path, character count, and an optional line range.  
10. All exceptions are caught, logged via the module logger, and converted into a failing ToolResult with an error message.

Purpose:
1. The file provides a reusable, well-scoped tool for reading file contents within the project tooling framework.  
2. By implementing a Tool subclass it integrates into the project's tool registry and can be invoked by other components that expect Tool/ToolResult semantics.  
3. The JSON parameters schema documents and enforces the expected inputs (path, limit, offset) for callers or for automated validation.  
4. Registry-based path resolution support allows callers to supply abstract or relative references that can be resolved by an external file registry object.  
5. The optional saved-base fallback mechanism provides an additional scope-aware resolution path for session-scoped file lookups.  
6. The explicit file size limit protects callers and the system from attempting to load excessively large files into memory.  
7. Returning a ToolResult with standardized success/error fields makes the tool's outcomes easy to interpret and chain with other tools.  
8. The inclusion of metadata (path, character count, line range) aids callers in quickly assessing what portion of a file was returned without parsing the content.  
9. Centralized exception handling and logging ensure operational issues are recorded and surface as structured errors rather than crashing callers.  
10. The async signature (async def execute) makes the tool compatible with asynchronous orchestrators even though the implementation performs synchronous file I/O.  
11. The module is minimal and focused, exposing a single primary class to keep the file-reading behavior consistent and auditable.  
12. Overall, it exists to provide a safe, discoverable, and integrable mechanism for reading files by other components in the project.

Key elements:
- ReadTool (class) (Tool subclass implementing file-reading behavior).  
- execute(self, path, limit=None, offset=None, **kwargs) (async method that performs resolution, validation, reading, slicing, and returns ToolResult).  
- name / description / parameters (class attributes declaring tool identity and JSON schema).  
- ToolResult (external type from captain_claw.tools.registry used for structured results).  
- get_logger / log (module logger used for error reporting).  
- Path (pathlib.Path usage for expanduser(), resolve(), is_file(), stat(), read_text()).  
- _file_registry resolution (optional kwargs-based call to file_registry.resolve(path)).  
- _saved_base_path (optional kwargs-based fallback scope value).  
- File size limit constant max_size = 100_000 (enforced before reading).  
- UTF-8 read_text call (file reading with explicit encoding).  

Key logic:
1. The execute method begins by converting the provided path string into a pathlib.Path and normalizing it via expanduser and resolve.  
2. It checks for the file's existence; if the resolved path does not exist it attempts to consult an optional _file_registry passed in kwargs.  
3. If a file_registry is present the code calls file_registry.resolve(path) inside a try/except and, if that returns a resolution, re-resolves that candidate path.  
4. If registry resolution yields a candidate that still does not exist the tool returns a failing ToolResult with a descriptive message.  
5. If no registry resolution is available the code optionally looks for a _saved_base_path but, when no fallback is found, it returns a not-found error.  
6. After a candidate path is established the method verifies the path points to a file (is_file()); non-files cause an immediate error result.  
7. Before reading, the method checks the file size via stat().st_size and compares it to a hard maximum (100,000 bytes), returning an error if the file is too large.  
8. If size checks pass the file is read using read_text with UTF-8 encoding, producing a string that is then split into lines for slicing.  
9. The offset parameter is interpreted as a 1-indexed start line with a floor of 1; selected_lines is taken from that start to the end and then truncated by limit if provided.  
10. The tool computes metadata including the resolved path, total returned character count, and if applicable the returned line range, formatting that as a prefix to content.  
11. A successful ToolResult is returned with success=True and content set to the metadata line followed by the sliced content.  
12. Any exception raised anywhere in the above steps is caught, logged via log.error (including path and the error string), and converted into a failing ToolResult with the exception message.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/llm/__init__.py

Description:
1. This module implements a small LLM provider framework with concrete providers for Ollama and LiteLLM-backed services.  
2. It defines dataclasses for Message, ToolCall, LLMResponse, and ToolDefinition to represent conversation items, tool invocations, and responses.  
3. An abstract LLMProvider base class declares the expected async methods complete, complete_streaming, and the synchronous count_tokens.  
4. Multiple helper functions normalize provider and model names, safely parse JSON, convert message and tool formats for different APIs, and extract usage counts.  
5. OllamaProvider is implemented to call a local or remote Ollama API with synchronous and streaming POST requests using httpx.AsyncClient.  
6. LiteLLMProvider is implemented to call litellm (if available), map providers like openai/anthropic/gemini to LiteLLM usage, and support streaming and token counting via litellm.  
7. Both providers parse tool call information from provider responses and convert tool arguments into dictionaries when possible.  
8. The module contains logic to resolve API keys from explicit arguments or environment variables and to special-case Gemini Vertex credentials.  
9. A create_provider factory constructs the appropriate provider by name and parameters, while get_provider and set_provider manage a global provider instance.  
10. The module maps provider-specific quirks such as OpenAI GPT-5 temperature constraints and provider-prefixed model names for LiteLLM.

Purpose:
1. The file centralizes LLM integration details so the rest of the project can use a uniform provider interface regardless of backend.  
2. It exists to encapsulate provider-specific request and response adaptation, so callers can work with Message and ToolDefinition objects rather than raw HTTP payloads.  
3. By providing OllamaProvider and LiteLLMProvider implementations, the module supports both a local Ollama deployment and litellm-based access to multiple cloud providers.  
4. Helper utilities ensure consistent behavior across providers: normalizing names, adjusting temperature constraints, and constructing the model identifiers LiteLLM expects.  
5. The file also handles authentication concerns by resolving API keys from parameters or environment variables and allowing injection of Google Vertex credentials for Gemini.  
6. Streaming and non-streaming completion are both provided in a standardized way, enabling consumers to choose synchronous or incremental output handling.  
7. Tool call extraction and normalization mean higher-level tooling can receive structured ToolCall objects representing function/tool invocation intents.  
8. The create_provider factory simplifies configuration-based initialization and enforces supported provider names, providing a single entrypoint for provider creation.  
9. Global provider management via get_provider and set_provider supports lazy initialization from the project's configuration and allows tests or runtime code to swap providers.  
10. Error translation wraps HTTP and JSON errors into project-specific exceptions (LLMAPIError and LLMError) so callers can handle failures consistently.  
11. Token counting fallbacks are implemented to provide approximate token estimates when provider-specific counters are unavailable.  
12. Overall, the module reduces duplication and centralizes LLM-specific behavior so other components remain provider-agnostic and focus on higher-level logic.

Key elements:
- OLLAMA_NATIVE_BASE_URL (constant) (default local Ollama URL).  
- Message (dataclass) (holds role, content, and tool call metadata).  
- ToolCall (dataclass) (represents an extracted tool invocation).  
- LLMResponse (dataclass) (encapsulates content, tool_calls, model, usage, finish_reason).  
- ToolDefinition (dataclass) (name, description, parameters JSON schema).  
- LLMProvider (ABC) (abstract methods: complete, complete_streaming, count_tokens).  
- _obj_get (helper) (safe attribute/dict access).  
- _safe_json_loads (helper) (robust JSON parsing returning dict).  
- _normalize_provider_name, _provider_model_name, _base_model_name (helpers) (normalize provider/model naming).  
- _is_openai_gpt5_family, _normalize_temperature_for_model (helpers) (provider-model specific constraints).  
- _resolve_api_key (helper) (resolve API keys from args or environment variables).  
- _convert_messages_for_openai_style, _convert_messages_for_ollama (helpers) (translate internal Message into provider formats).  
- _convert_tools_for_openai_style (helper) (translate ToolDefinition into function-style tool descriptions).  
- _extract_usage (helper) (normalize usage tokens from provider response objects).  
- OllamaProvider (class) (methods: __init__, complete, complete_streaming, count_tokens, close).  
- LiteLLMProvider (class) (methods: __init__, set_vertex_credentials, clear_vertex_credentials, _request_kwargs, complete, complete_streaming, count_tokens).  
- create_provider (factory) (constructs OllamaProvider or LiteLLMProvider based on normalized name).  
- get_provider, set_provider (global provider management) (lazy creation using captain_claw.config).

Key logic:
1. Message and tool conversion functions traverse lists of Message objects or tool definitions and produce the payload shapes required by different backends (OpenAI-style function entries for LiteLLM; role/content pairs plus tool metadata for Ollama).  
2. _obj_get provides a uniform accessor that works with either dicts or objects, avoiding repeated isinstance checks throughout parsing code.  
3. _safe_json_loads attempts to parse string arguments into JSON and falls back to returning the raw string under a key when parsing fails, ensuring tool argument extraction does not throw.  
4. Provider/model normalization functions ensure consistency in naming and prefixing: LiteLLM models are given provider/model prefixes and model base names can be extracted when needed.  
5. Temperature normalization enforces provider-specific constraints such as forcing temperature=1.0 for OpenAI GPT-5 family models.  
6. _resolve_api_key reads API keys from explicit parameters or standard environment variables depending on provider to centralize credential resolution.  
7. OllamaProvider.complete builds a JSON body with model, messages, options, optional tools, and then POSTs to the Ollama API, parsing JSON response content and extracting tool_calls and usage counts.  
8. OllamaProvider.complete_streaming uses httpx's AsyncClient.stream to iterate lines from a streaming endpoint, JSON-decodes each non-empty line, yields content pieces, and stops when a 'done' flag is encountered.  
9. LiteLLMProvider._request_kwargs prepares a dictionary for litellm.acompletion, injecting api_key or vertex credentials and remapping gemini to vertex_ai when Google OAuth credentials are provided.  
10. LiteLLMProvider.complete calls litellm.acompletion (imported at runtime), reads the first choice and its message to obtain content, and extracts tool_calls by parsing returned function call structures, converting argument strings via _safe_json_loads.  
11. LiteLLMProvider.complete_streaming requests a streaming acompletion and iterates chunks; it extracts delta content from choice deltas handling strings, lists of text parts, and other delta types, yielding assembled text increments.  
12. Both provider implementations wrap HTTP, JSON, and other runtime errors into project-specific exceptions (LLMAPIError when status codes are available, otherwise LLMError) to provide predictable error semantics to callers.  
13. Token counting implementations try provider-specific counters (litellm.token_counter) and otherwise fall back to a heuristic length//4 to approximate tokens when counters are not available.  
14. create_provider selects the correct provider class based on normalized provider name and environment/default values; unsupported names raise a ValueError.  
15. get_provider lazily initializes a module-global provider using configuration from captain_claw.config and create_provider, enabling configuration-driven defaults and singletons.  
16. set_provider allows overriding the global provider instance, facilitating tests or runtime swaps without needing to modify callers.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/rest_orchestrator.py

Description:
1. This module defines aiohttp REST handlers that expose orchestrator control, task management, workflow, and session endpoints.  
2. Each handler is an async function that accepts a WebServer-like server and an aiohttp.web.Request and returns a web.Response.  
3. Handlers use server._orchestrator and server.agent to forward requests to orchestrator and agent functionality.  
4. The module imports InstructionLoader to render prompts and get_logger for structured logging.  
5. Several endpoints perform JSON body parsing and validate required fields such as task_id, input, or name.  
6. Error conditions are handled by returning JSON error responses with appropriate HTTP status codes.  
7. The rephrase endpoint uses the configured LLM provider to convert casual user input into a structured orchestrator prompt.  
8. Prepare and workflow endpoints call orchestrator methods like prepare, save_workflow, load_workflow, and delete_workflow.  
9. Task control endpoints delegate actions such as edit, update, restart, pause, resume, and postpone to the orchestrator.  
10. Responses often serialize complex objects using json.dumps with default=str to ensure non-serializable values are handled.

Purpose:
This module exists to provide an HTTP surface for clients (typically the web UI) to inspect and control the orchestrator, manage tasks, and work with saved workflows and sessions. It centralizes request validation, error handling, and logging so higher-level code in the orchestrator and agent can focus on orchestration logic rather than HTTP concerns. By forwarding calls to server._orchestrator and server.agent, it maps REST operations to internal methods such as prepare, edit_task, update_task, restart_task, pause_task, resume_task, and postpone_task. The rephrase endpoint integrates the InstructionLoader and the configured LLM provider to produce a standardized prompt form of user input, which helps produce more predictable orchestration plans. The prepare endpoint supports previewing task decomposition without execution, enabling users to inspect proposed task graphs. Workflow endpoints let clients persist, load, list, and delete workflow templates through the orchestrator backend. Session and model listing endpoints expose agent-managed resources for per-task overrides and selections in the UI. The handlers uniformly parse JSON request bodies, validate required parameters, and return JSON responses with consistent structure for success and error cases. Logging calls record important events, input sizes, and errors to aid debugging and operational visibility. The module thus acts as a thin but essential translation layer between HTTP clients and the internal orchestrator/agent APIs.

Key elements:
- get_orchestrator_status (handler; returns orchestrator.get_status())  
- reset_orchestrator (handler; calls orchestrator.reset())  
- get_orchestrator_skills (handler; uses server.agent.list_user_invocable_skills() and server.agent.tools.list_tools())  
- rephrase_orchestrator_input (handler; uses InstructionLoader.render and provider.complete() with Message)  
- edit_orchestrator_task (handler; calls orchestrator.edit_task(task_id))  
- update_orchestrator_task (handler; calls orchestrator.update_task(task_id, description))  
- restart_orchestrator_task (handler; calls orchestrator.restart_task(task_id))  
- pause_orchestrator_task (handler; calls orchestrator.pause_task(task_id))  
- resume_orchestrator_task (handler; calls orchestrator.resume_task(task_id))  
- postpone_orchestrator_task (handler; calls orchestrator.postpone_task(task_id))  
- prepare_orchestrator (handler; calls orchestrator.prepare(user_input))  
- get_orchestrator_sessions (handler; uses server.agent.session_manager.list_sessions(limit=30))  
- get_orchestrator_models (handler; uses server.agent.get_allowed_models())  
- list_workflows, save_workflow, load_workflow, delete_workflow (handlers; CRUD for orchestrator workflows)  
- Dependencies: aiohttp.web, json, InstructionLoader, get_logger, captain_claw.llm.Message and provider APIs (used in rephrase)

Key logic:
The module follows a consistent handler pattern: check for the presence of server._orchestrator or server.agent as required, parse and validate the JSON body or route parameters, and call the corresponding orchestrator or agent method. When required parameters are missing (for example task_id, input, or name), handlers immediately return a JSON error with status 400. JSON parsing of request bodies is wrapped in try/except blocks to return a clear "Invalid JSON" error when parsing fails. For actions that modify orchestrator state (reset, edit, update, restart, pause, resume, postpone), the handler simply forwards validated arguments to the orchestrator method and returns its result. The prepare endpoint logs input size and preview, then awaits orchestrator.prepare(user_input) and returns its result; failures are logged and converted to a 500-style JSON error. The rephrase endpoint constructs a prompt via InstructionLoader.render and then attempts to call the configured LLM provider.complete with a Message; it uses a 60-second asyncio wait_for and falls back to the original input if the provider call fails or returns empty. Some responses that may include non-serializable objects use json.dumps with default=str passed as the dumps argument to web.json_response to ensure safe serialization. Skill and tool listing queries call agent APIs and guard against exceptions by returning empty lists on error. Session listing calls agent.session_manager.list_sessions with a fixed limit and converts session objects into id/name pairs for the response. The save_workflow handler accepts optional name, task_overrides, and model fields, normalizes model to a stripped string if present, and delegates to orchestrator.save_workflow. Load and delete workflow handlers validate the workflow name and forward to orchestrator.load_workflow and orchestrator.delete_workflow respectively. Throughout, errors are logged via the module logger with contextual information such as input previews and exception types to aid troubleshooting.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/chat_handler.py

Description:
1. This module implements WebSocket-based chat handling for the web UI.  
2. It exposes an async handle_chat function that validates the agent state and schedules background work.  
3. When a chat arrives it checks whether an agent is initialized and whether the server is busy, returning error messages over the WebSocket if not.  
4. If accepted, it sets server._busy, broadcasts a thinking status, and invokes a thinking callback to update UI state.  
5. The user's message is echoed to all connected clients via server._broadcast.  
6. The heavy work is delegated to an asyncio background task created from the internal _run_agent coroutine so the WebSocket read-loop remains responsive.  
7. The background _run_agent coroutine routes messages prefixed with '/orchestrate' to the orchestrator when available.  
8. For non-orchestrate messages it calls server.agent.complete to obtain an assistant response, handling tool calls and guards there.  
9. After producing a response _run_agent broadcasts assistant messages, usage statistics, and session information to clients.  
10. Exceptions during agent processing are logged and broadcast as error messages, and the finally block clears busy state and notifies clients that the server is ready.  

Purpose:
This module exists to bridge incoming WebSocket chat messages from the web UI to the server-side agent and orchestrator logic. It centralizes validation of agent availability and busy state to prevent concurrent processing conflicts. By offloading processing to a background coroutine it keeps the WebSocket reader free to accept control messages such as cancel or stop. It provides user feedback via server._broadcast for status, chat messages, errors, usage, and session details so the UI can stay synchronized. The special '/orchestrate' prefix is handled here so UI users can directly invoke orchestrator workflows through the same chat channel. The module also updates the server's active task reference so long-running operations are tracked and not garbage-collected. It integrates with existing server-side hooks like _thinking_callback to present intermediate UI state while the agent reasons. Error handling and logging are localized to this component to ensure failures are reported back to clients and recorded. The file is lightweight and intentionally delegates the domain-specific work to server.agent and server._orchestrator implementations. This separation keeps the handler focused on message orchestration, lifecycle management, and client communication semantics. Because it manipulates server internals like _busy and _active_task, it enforces single-turn processing semantics and predictable cleanup. Overall, the module exists to provide a resilient, responsive link between UI chat input and backend reasoning/orchestration services.

Key elements:
- handle_chat (async function; validates state, broadcasts status, schedules background work).  
- _run_agent (async coroutine; performs orchestrator routing or agent completion and final broadcast).  
- server._busy (server attribute; used to prevent concurrent processing).  
- server._active_task (server attribute; stores background asyncio.Task reference).  
- server._broadcast (method; used to send messages to all clients).  
- server._send (method; used to send direct WebSocket responses, e.g., errors).  
- server._thinking_callback (callable; used to provide intermediate UI thinking text).  
- server.agent.complete (external call; obtains assistant responses and handles tools/guards).  
- server._orchestrator.orchestrate (external call; invoked for '/orchestrate' commands if available).  
- server._session_info (method; provides session information for broadcasting).  
- asyncio.create_task (used to spawn background execution without awaiting).  
- get_logger / log (module-level logger; used for error logging).  
- aiohttp.web.WebSocketResponse (type hinting; indicates WebSocket interactions).

Key logic:
1. handle_chat first verifies that an agent is present and returns an error message through server._send if not.  
2. It then checks server._busy to reject simultaneous requests with a clear error broadcast.  
3. If the incoming message is allowed, handle_chat sets server._busy to True, broadcasts a 'thinking' status, and calls server._thinking_callback to update UI text.  
4. The handler broadcasts the user's message to all clients to keep the shared chat state consistent.  
5. It spawns _run_agent as an asyncio background task via asyncio.create_task and stores that task on server._active_task so it is not garbage-collected.  
6. _run_agent strips and inspects the message to detect a '/orchestrate ' prefix and, if found and an orchestrator is attached, invokes orchestrator.orchestrate with the remainder.  
7. If an orchestrate invocation lacks a request body, _run_agent broadcasts a usage error message rather than calling the orchestrator.  
8. For regular messages _run_agent delegates to server.agent.complete to obtain an assistant response, relying on the agent implementation to perform any tool calls or guard checks.  
9. After receiving a response, _run_agent broadcasts the assistant reply and then broadcasts usage statistics extracted from server.agent.last_usage and server.agent.total_usage.  
10. It also broadcasts session information by calling server._session_info to keep clients aware of session state changes.  
11. Any exceptions raised during processing are caught, logged via the module logger, and an error message is broadcast to clients to surface the failure.  
12. In the finally block _run_agent resets server._busy to False, clears server._active_task, and broadcasts a 'ready' status so the system can accept new chat turns.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/openai_proxy.py

Description:
1. This module implements OpenAI-compatible API proxy handlers for chat completion and model listing endpoints.  
2. It exposes functions to parse Bearer tokens from the Authorization header and to build OpenAI-style JSON completion responses.  
3. The api_chat_completions handler validates request JSON, extracts the last user message, and supports both immediate JSON and SSE streaming responses.  
4. Streaming responses are produced by write_sse_streaming_response which sends Server-Sent Events that chunk the assistant text into word groups.  
5. Agent instances are obtained from server._api_pool using a session id provided in the Authorization header.  
6. The module calls agent.complete to generate a text response and consults agent.get_runtime_model_details and agent.last_usage for metadata and usage.  
7. It handles a range of error conditions and returns proper OpenAI-style error objects with HTTP status codes for invalid JSON, missing messages, authentication errors, and internal failures.  
8. api_list_models returns a list of available models derived from server.agent.get_allowed_models and ensures a default 'captain-claw' model entry.  
9. Utility functions use standard libraries such as json, time, uuid and depend on aiohttp.web types and server attributes.  
10. Logging via the project's get_logger is used for error reporting during agent initialization and completion failures.  

Purpose:
This module exists to provide an OpenAI-compatible HTTP API surface that front-ends can call instead of talking directly to the internal agent implementation. It translates incoming OpenAI-style requests into operations on internal agent sessions and translates agent outputs back into OpenAI-style JSON and SSE formats. By requiring a Bearer session token this proxy maps HTTP requests to server-managed agent sessions in an API pool. The module centralizes validation of request structure, extraction of the most recent user message, and consistent error responses for malformed calls. It also encapsulates handling of streaming versus non-streaming responses so callers can request incremental SSE output or a single completed JSON object. Error handling and logging are concentrated here to ensure failures in session creation or completion are reported and converted into appropriate HTTP errors. The api_list_models handler provides a simple model discovery endpoint based on the live server.agent allowed models, guaranteeing a baseline 'captain-claw' model when absent. The write_sse_streaming_response function implements a deterministic chunking strategy that splits text into small word groups for SSE delivery. The module relies on server-side objects and lifecycle managed by the enclosing WebServer, keeping network-facing concerns separated from agent internals. It exists so external clients or tools that expect OpenAI semantics can integrate with the Captain Claw agent without knowledge of internal APIs. The file therefore provides a compatibility layer and a place to implement OpenAI-like behaviors such as usage reporting and completion identifiers. Overall, it reduces duplication by providing reusable builders for responses and a consistent approach to agent acquisition, release, and response formatting.

Key elements:
- extract_api_session_id (function: parse "Authorization: Bearer <token>" header)  
- build_chat_completion_response (function: construct OpenAI-style completion JSON)  
- write_sse_streaming_response (async function: prepares aiohttp StreamResponse and emits SSE chunks)  
- api_chat_completions (async handler: POST /v1/chat/completions entrypoint)  
- api_list_models (async handler: GET /v1/models entrypoint)  
- nested _sse (async inner helper in write_sse_streaming_response: writes SSE "data:" lines)  
- server._api_pool (external dependency: used to get_or_create and release agent sessions)  
- server.agent (external dependency: used by api_list_models and to enumerate allowed models)  
- agent.complete (agent method: invoked to produce assistant text)  
- agent.get_runtime_model_details (agent method: used to obtain model name)  
- agent.last_usage (attribute: used for prompt/completion/total token counts)  
- aiohttp.web.StreamResponse / web.json_response (framework integration)  
- json, time, uuid (standard libs used for payloads, timestamps, ids)  
- get_logger / log.error (logging facility used for error reporting)

Key logic:
1. api_chat_completions begins by verifying that server._api_pool exists and returns a 503 error payload if the API proxy is disabled.  
2. It extracts the session id from the Authorization header using extract_api_session_id and returns a 401 JSON error if no valid Bearer token is present.  
3. The handler attempts to parse the request body as JSON and will return a 400 error if parsing fails.  
4. It validates that the "messages" field is a non-empty list and returns a 400 error when that condition is not met.  
5. To locate the user prompt it iterates messages in reverse order finding the most recent dict with role "user"; for message content it supports either a plain string or a list of part objects where parts with type "text" contribute their "text" field.  
6. After extracting the user message it determines whether streaming is requested via the "stream" boolean in the body.  
7. The handler obtains an agent via server._api_pool.get_or_create(session_id) inside a try/except that logs initialization failures and returns a 500 error if creation fails.  
8. It constructs a completion id with uuid, invokes agent.complete(user_message) to produce the response text, and ensures the session id is released back to the pool in a finally block; completion failures are logged and returned as 500 errors.  
9. The code attempts to read model metadata from agent.get_runtime_model_details and falls back to "captain-claw" if unavailable; usage counters are read from agent.last_usage or defaulted to zeros.  
10. If streaming is not requested the handler returns a single JSON response built by build_chat_completion_response containing id, model, choices, and usage.  
11. If streaming is requested it delegates to write_sse_streaming_response which prepares an SSE StreamResponse, emits an initial assistant role chunk, then splits the response text into fixed-size word groups (chunk_size=5) and writes each group as a chat.completion.chunk SSE event, preserving spacing between chunks.  
12. The streaming logic emits a final chunk with finish_reason "stop" including usage, writes the "data: [DONE]" sentinel, calls write_eof, and returns the StreamResponse. api_list_models separately queries server.agent.get_allowed_models when available, assembles model entries with timestamps/ownership, ensures a "captain-claw" entry is present, and returns the aggregated list as JSON.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/rest_loops.py

Description:
1. This module defines REST handlers and execution logic for running workflows in a loop.  
2. It exposes HTTP endpoints to start a loop, check its status, and request a stop.  
3. start_loop validates the agent state, request JSON, workflow name, and iteration definitions before scheduling execution.  
4. The handler prepares per-iteration metadata and stores a short UUID and ISO timestamp in server._loop_runner_state.  
5. A background asyncio task is created to run the work via the run_loop coroutine.  
6. get_loop_status returns the current loop state or an idle response if none exists.  
7. stop_loop sets a stop flag that causes the running loop to cancel remaining iterations.  
8. run_loop iterates sequentially over provided iteration configs and uses a SessionOrchestrator to load and execute workflows.  
9. Each iteration broadcasts events for start, completion, failure, and the overall loop lifecycle using server._broadcast.  
10. The module records durations, previews, statuses, and errors and logs lifecycle events.

Purpose:
This file implements the HTTP-facing control surface and background execution engine for repeating workflow runs. It exists to allow clients to request repeated execution of a named workflow with varying variable sets and to monitor and control that execution asynchronously. By validating input and creating a dedicated loop task, it prevents blocking the request thread and centralizes loop state on the server object. The code coordinates with a SessionOrchestrator to load workflows, resolve variables, and perform the actual workflow execution, keeping orchestration details separate. It provides structured per-iteration metadata (status, duration, preview, error) so UIs or other clients can present progress and results. The module also supports graceful stopping, marking remaining iterations as cancelled and broadcasting a stop event. Logging calls record lifecycle milestones and failures for operational visibility. Broadcasting of events via server._broadcast gives real-time updates to connected clients or dashboards. Error handling around workflow loading and execution ensures failed iterations are captured and reported without crashing the whole loop. The file enforces a single concurrently running loop by checking server._loop_runner_task, preventing overlapping executions. UUID-based loop ids and ISO timestamps provide consistent identifiers and timing information. The module integrates configuration (via get_config) to control orchestrator limits like parallelism and agent counts.

Key elements:
- start_loop (async function; HTTP POST handler that validates input and starts run_loop).  
- get_loop_status (async function; HTTP GET handler returning current loop state or idle).  
- stop_loop (async function; HTTP POST handler that signals a running loop to stop).  
- run_loop (async function; core loop executor that runs iterations sequentially).  
- _make_loop_broadcast (inner closure in run_loop; adapts orchestrator events to loop events).  
- SessionOrchestrator (external class used to load and execute workflows via orchestrator.load_workflow and orchestrator.execute).  
- get_config (imported function used to read orchestrator-related configuration values).  
- server attributes accessed: agent, _loop_runner_task, _loop_runner_state, _loop_runner_stop, _broadcast.  
- log (module logger from captain_claw.logging used for lifecycle and error logging).  
- Standard libraries and aiohttp: asyncio, json, time, uuid, datetime.UTC, aiohttp.web for request/response handling.

Key logic:
1. start_loop first ensures the main agent exists and that no other loop task is currently running; it returns appropriate HTTP error responses for those conditions.  
2. The handler parses JSON from the request, validates presence of a workflow name and an iterations list, and returns 400 errors for malformed input.  
3. A short loop_id is generated from a UUID, and an iterations list of dictionaries is constructed containing index, variable values, and initial status metadata.  
4. The server's loop state fields (_loop_runner_stop, _loop_runner_state) are initialized and a background task is created to run run_loop, allowing immediate HTTP response while execution proceeds asynchronously.  
5. run_loop reads configuration using get_config and then processes iterations sequentially, checking the stop flag before each iteration to support cancellation.  
6. If stop is requested, remaining iterations are marked "cancelled", loop state is set to "stopped", and a loop_stopped event is broadcast with the index at which it stopped.  
7. For each iteration, the code sets status to "running", broadcasts an iteration_started event, and records a start timestamp for duration calculation.  
8. A SessionOrchestrator is instantiated with parameters taken from config and the server agent plus a broadcast callback that converts orchestrator events into loop-scoped events.  
9. The orchestrator attempts to load the named workflow; failure to load raises and is handled by marking the iteration as failed and broadcasting an iteration_failed event.  
10. When a workflow loads, default variables are combined with per-iteration variable overrides to produce effective_vars, then orchestrator.execute is awaited to run the workflow and synthesize results.  
11. On success the iteration is marked "completed", duration and a result preview (first 500 chars) are recorded, and an iteration_completed event is broadcast; errors are captured and logged when exceptions occur.  
12. After each iteration the orchestrator is shut down in a finally block if it was created; when all iterations finish normally the loop state is set to "completed" and a loop_completed event is broadcast.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/slash_commands.py

Description:
1. This module implements handling of slash-style commands received over the web UI WebSocket.  
2. The primary entry point, handle_command, parses a raw command string into the command and arguments and routes to specific handlers.  
3. It supports many top-level commands such as /help, /clear, /config, /stop, /history, /compact, /new, /session, /sessions, /models, /pipeline, /planning, /skills, /monitor, /exit, /approve, /orchestrate, /orchestrate-execute, /todo, /contacts, /scripts, and /apis.  
4. Several commands directly mutate server or agent state (for example creating or switching sessions, toggling planning or pipeline modes, setting cancel flags).  
5. Subcommands for session management are implemented in handle_session_subcommand and include list, switch/load, new, rename, description, model, and protect.  
6. Entity-specific handlers implement CRUD and search flows for todos, contacts, scripts, and APIs via handle_todo_command, handle_contacts_command, handle_scripts_command, and handle_apis_command.  
7. Those handlers use a session manager API to list, create, select, update, delete, and search domain items and format human-readable text responses.  
8. The module uses shlex-based tokenization for parsing field=value update strings and JSON parsing for orchestrator execution overrides.  
9. Results and events are communicated back to the client using server._send for single-reply messages and server._broadcast for session or state updates.  
10. A format_help function builds grouped Markdown help content from a COMMANDS registry for the /help command.

Purpose:
This file exists to provide a concise mapping from text-based slash commands entered in the web UI to programmatic actions on the server and agent components. It centralizes command parsing and routing so the WebSocket layer can remain simple and just forward raw command strings. By grouping related behaviors (session management, todos, contacts, scripts, APIs) into separate handler functions, the module keeps per-entity logic organized and reusable. It also enforces consistent output formatting for command results, including truncation or summarization for history and id-prefixing for items. The module integrates with the agent's session manager API to perform persistent operations and to ensure that created or updated entities are saved and optionally broadcast to other clients. It bridges interactive control (like /stop and /approve) with asynchronous components such as an orchestrator and chat handler by importing and invoking those components when needed. Error handling around the top-level dispatcher ensures that command exceptions produce readable error messages rather than crashing the WebSocket handler. The file provides a help generator that reflects the command registry so the UI can present up-to-date guidance without duplicating command metadata. Parsing utilities (shlex and JSON) are used to accept structured update and execute payloads from users while keeping input handling relatively simple. Overall, this module exists so that end users can manipulate sessions, data entities, model/runtime settings, and orchestration features from a compact command syntax inside the web interface.

Key elements:
- handle_command(server, ws, raw) (main dispatcher for slash commands).  
- handle_session_subcommand(server, args) (handles /session subcommands and session lifecycle operations).  
- handle_todo_command(server, args) (CRUD and listing for to-do items via session_manager).  
- handle_contacts_command(server, args) (CRUD, search, and info display for contacts).  
- handle_scripts_command(server, args) (manage script records including add/info/search/update/remove).  
- handle_apis_command(server, args) (manage API records including add/info/search/update/remove).  
- format_help() (builds grouped Markdown help from captain_claw.web_server.COMMANDS).  
- get_config (configuration helper used for /config output).  
- _shlex (shlex imported as _shlex for parsing field=value tokens).  
- json (used to parse orchestrator override payloads).  
- server._send and server._broadcast (WebSocket send and broadcast mechanisms).  
- server.agent and server.agent.session_manager (primary stateful objects manipulated by commands).  
- server._orchestrator (optional orchestrator used by /orchestrate-execute).  
- handle_chat and handle_approve_command (dynamically imported handlers invoked by specific commands).

Key logic:
The module begins by splitting an incoming raw command into a command token and the rest of the arguments, normalizing the command to lowercase for routing. The handle_command function implements a long chain of conditional branches that map known command strings to their corresponding behavior, preparing a human-readable result string in most cases. Many branches interact with server.agent and its session_manager to list, create, select, update, or delete domain entities; these interactions are synchronous in flow but generally await asynchronous session_manager calls. Commands that change shared state (like creating a session, switching sessions, or updating session metadata) trigger server._broadcast calls to notify other UI components of the change. The /session command delegates to handle_session_subcommand which implements subcommand parsing, selection logic, model setting, description auto-generation, and toggling of memory protection flags. Entity handlers parse a top-level subcommand (list/add/info/search/update/remove) and map those to session_manager methods; list operations format paginated summaries, info operations assemble multi-line detail strings, and update operations use shlex tokenization to accept field=value pairs and validate allowed fields. For /orchestrate-execute the code attempts to parse JSON arguments into task_overrides and variable_values then calls server._orchestrator.execute and broadcasts the result, handling exceptions and broadcasting errors on failure. The module treats unrecognized commands with a default "Unknown command" message and wraps the entire dispatch in a try/except to convert exceptions into an error result sent via server._send. Helper behaviors include truncating long history messages for the /history output, formatting id previews with the first 8 characters, and mapping item attributes (importance, tags, status icons) into concise lines. Some commands, such as /orchestrate, import and hand off processing to a chat handler and return early to avoid duplicate response building. The format_help function inspects a COMMANDS registry, groups commands by category, and constructs Markdown lines for display by the client. Overall, control flow is straightforward imperative dispatch with per-entity helper functions encapsulating repeated CRUD and formatting patterns.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/telegram.py

Description:
1. This module provides a Telegram bridge integration for the web server.  
2. It initializes and manages long-polling, a worker loop, and message handling tasks when Telegram is enabled.  
3. start_telegram sets up a TelegramBridge instance, loads persisted approval and pairing state, and starts background poll and worker tasks.  
4. stop_telegram cancels running tasks and closes the bridge.  
5. _telegram_poll_loop performs repeated get_updates calls and enqueues incoming updates for processing.  
6. _telegram_worker pulls queued updates and spawns concurrent handlers for each message.  
7. _handle_telegram_message routes messages through pairing checks, command execution, and agent forwarding while handling business messages.  
8. execute_telegram_command implements several slash-style commands such as /clear, /config, /history, /compact, /new, /session, /sessions, /models, /pipeline, /planning, /skills, /monitor, /approve and /orchestrate.  
9. _tg_process_with_typing runs agent.complete or orchestrator.orchestrate while sending periodic typing actions and broadcasting status and usage updates.  
10. Helper functions handle sending messages, loading and saving approval/pairing state, cleaning expired pairings, generating tokens, pairing unknown users, and approving pending pairings.  

Purpose:
1. The file's role is to bridge Telegram chats into the web server's chat and agent workflow.  
2. It exists to allow remote users to interact with the Captain Claw agent over Telegram using plain text and a subset of slash commands.  
3. Lifecycle functions (start_telegram / stop_telegram) allow enabling or disabling the integration according to server configuration and presence of a bot token.  
4. The long-polling and worker design separates update retrieval from message processing, improving responsiveness and enabling concurrent handling.  
5. Pairing and approval mechanics ensure only approved Telegram users can send messages to the agent while allowing operators to approve pending tokens.  
6. The module persists approved and pending pairing state through the agent's session_manager app state APIs so that approvals survive restarts.  
7. Command handling maps Telegram slash commands to server and agent operations to mirror functionality present in the Web UI.  
8. Typing indicator management and broadcasting keep Telegram users informed and also update connected web clients about agent status and usage.  
9. The module delegates heavy lifting to the server and agent objects (e.g., session management, model info, compacting, orchestration) rather than reimplementing those concerns.  
10. Token generation and expiration cleanup provide a safety mechanism to avoid stale pairing tokens and enforce TTLs.  
11. Error handling aims to log failures, notify the Telegram user, and broadcast error messages to the web UI when processing fails.  
12. Overall, the file encapsulates the Telegram-specific input/output and security workflows while integrating tightly with server-side persistence, session, and broadcasting APIs.  

Key elements:
- start_telegram (initializes TelegramBridge, loads state, starts poll/worker tasks)  
- stop_telegram (cancels tasks and closes bridge)  
- _telegram_poll_loop (long-polling loop calling TelegramBridge.get_updates and enqueuing updates)  
- _telegram_worker (dequeues updates and spawns message handlers)  
- _handle_telegram_message (per-message processing, pairing checks, command dispatch, broadcasting)  
- execute_telegram_command (parses and executes supported slash commands)  
- _tg_process_with_typing (manages typing heartbeat, busy locking, calls orchestrator or agent, broadcasts responses and usage)  
- _tg_send (sends messages via TelegramBridge.send_message with error logging)  
- _tg_load_state / _tg_save_state (persist/load JSON state via agent.session_manager.get_app_state and set_app_state)  
- _tg_cleanup_expired (removes expired pairing tokens based on ISO timestamp)  
- _tg_generate_pairing_token (generates unique 8-character pairing tokens)  
- _tg_pair_unknown_user (creates pending pairing entries, persists state, and notifies user and web UI)  
- handle_approve_command (validates token, moves pending pairing to approved users, persists state, notifies approved user)  
- Dependencies: TelegramBridge, TelegramMessage, server._broadcast, server.agent, server.agent.session_manager, server._orchestrator  

Key logic:
1. start_telegram checks configuration and bot token presence, creates a TelegramBridge, loads persisted approved and pending pairing maps, runs a cleanup for expired pairings, saves state, and then starts a polling task and worker task.  
2. stop_telegram cancels the poll and worker tasks if running and closes the bridge connection to ensure a graceful shutdown.  
3. The poll loop repeatedly calls get_updates with an offset and timeout, updates the stored offset to avoid reprocessing, and places each update on an asyncio queue for downstream processing.  
4. The worker loop continuously consumes that queue and creates an independent asyncio task to handle each TelegramMessage so processing of one message does not block retrieval of others.  
5. _handle_telegram_message first attempts to mark business messages as read, enforces approval by checking server._approved_telegram_users and initiating pairing for unknown users, and ignores empty messages.  
6. It normalizes bot-mention forms of slash commands, provides built-in handlers for /start and /help, and otherwise tries to run execute_telegram_command for leading slash commands; if a command returns None it falls through to agent processing (notably /orchestrate).  
7. Non-command messages are broadcast into the web UI with a user label and then processed by _tg_process_with_typing which performs the actual agent or orchestrator invocation.  
8. execute_telegram_command tokenizes the raw command, verifies agent availability, and implements command-specific flows such as clearing session messages, compacting sessions via agent.compact_session, creating new sessions via session_manager.create_session, listing sessions, retrieving allowed models, toggling pipeline/planning modes, listing skills, and delegating session subcommands to slash_commands.handle_session_subcommand.  
9. For /approve it delegates to handle_approve_command which validates and approves a pending token by moving data from _pending_telegram_pairings to _approved_telegram_users and persists the change.  
10. _tg_process_with_typing acquires a busy lock to serialize agent access, sets a busy flag, broadcasts a thinking status, and spawns a typing heartbeat that periodically sends chat_action "typing" via the bridge until the work completes.  
11. While typing is active, the function either calls orchestrator.orchestrate for explicit /orchestrate requests or agent.complete for normal messages, sends the resulting text back to the Telegram chat, and broadcasts assistant messages, usage, and session_info to the web UI.  
12. Exceptions during message handling are logged, the user is informed via Telegram when possible, and error events are broadcast to the web UI; the typing heartbeat is stopped and busy state cleared in a finally block.  
13. State persistence uses JSON serialization and the agent.session_manager app-state API to store both approved users and pending pairings; loading validates the parsed JSON is a dict.  
14. Pairing token generation uses a restricted alphabet to create an 8-character token, ensures uniqueness relative to existing pending tokens, and pending entries include creation and ISO-formatted expiration timestamps which are honored and cleaned up by _tg_cleanup_expired.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/rest_workflows.py

Description:
1. This module provides REST handlers used by a workflow browser within the web server.  
2. It exposes functions to list available workflows and to retrieve workflow output files.  
3. workflows_dir determines the workflows directory under the resolved workspace path and ensures it exists.  
4. list_workflow_outputs scans the workflows directory for .json workflow definitions and for markdown output files.  
5. The listing function builds a summary structure for each workflow including name, filename, user_input, task_count, and outputs.  
6. It parses each .json file to extract workflow metadata and falls back to filename-derived defaults on parse failure.  
7. Output markdown files are associated with workflows by matching filename stems using a "-output-" pattern and an inferred-key fallback.  
8. The handler sorts outputs for each workflow by their timestamp and returns the assembled list as a JSON response.  
9. get_workflow_output validates requested filenames to prevent path traversal, reads the markdown file, and returns its content.  
10. Both handlers use aiohttp.web responses and perform error handling for missing files and file-read exceptions.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide HTTP endpoints that allow a browser-based workflow UI to discover and inspect persisted workflows and their generated outputs.  
2. It centralizes filesystem access logic related to workflows so the web server can present structured information without embedding path handling elsewhere.  
3. By ensuring the workflows directory is present, workflows_dir prepares the runtime environment for storing workflow metadata and outputs.  
4. list_workflow_outputs aggregates information from two kinds of filesystem artifacts — .json workflow descriptors and output .md files — into a single consumable representation.  
5. The JSON returned by the listing handler is suitable for populating UI lists, showing recent outputs, and providing basic metadata such as task counts and user input.  
6. The handler's robust parsing and fallback behavior means malformed or missing metadata files do not prevent discovery of outputs.  
7. get_workflow_output provides a safe way for the UI to fetch the textual content of a particular workflow output while preventing path traversal attacks.  
8. The module leverages the project's configuration to resolve workspace paths, keeping filesystem layout consistent with other orchestrator components.  
9. Sorting outputs and workflows ensures predictable presentation order for callers and avoids exposing raw filesystem ordering.  
10. Error responses are returned with appropriate HTTP status codes and JSON error messages to simplify client-side handling.  
11. The functions are asynchronous handlers compatible with aiohttp's web framework, fitting into the web server's routing and request lifecycle.  
12. Overall, the module encapsulates the minimal file-IO, parsing, and validation logic required to support a workflow browser UI without implementing UI or orchestration logic itself.

Key elements:
- workflows_dir (function) — resolves and ensures existence of the "workflows" directory under the configured workspace.  
- list_workflow_outputs (async function) — handler for listing workflows and their outputs as JSON.  
- get_workflow_output (async function) — handler for returning the content of a specified output markdown file as JSON.  
- get_config (imported call) — used to obtain configuration and the resolved workspace path.  
- Path.glob and Path.read_text (pathlib) — used for discovering files and reading their contents.  
- json.loads (standard library) — used to parse workflow .json files.  
- aiohttp.web.json_response (imported) — used to return JSON responses with status codes.  
- Filename validation checks (simple string checks for ".." and "/") — used to prevent directory traversal.  
- File stat and st_size access (Path.stat) — used to determine file sizes for outputs.  
- Glob patterns "*.json" and "*-output-*.md" — define which files are treated as workflows and outputs.  
- TYPE_CHECKING and WebServer typing hint — provides a type hint for handler signatures without runtime import.

Key logic:
1. workflows_dir calls get_config() to obtain the resolved workspace path and constructs a "workflows" subdirectory, creating it if necessary.  
2. list_workflow_outputs begins by scanning the workflows directory for files matching "*.json" and builds an initial dictionary keyed by each file's stem.  
3. For each .json file the handler attempts to read and parse JSON to extract workflow_name, user_input, and a task list length; failures fall back to inferred defaults.  
4. Each workflow entry is initialized with name, filename, user_input, task_count, and an empty outputs list to which matching markdown outputs will be appended.  
5. The function then scans for files matching "*-output-*.md" and attempts to match each output file to an existing workflow key by testing whether the file stem starts with "workflowkey-output-".  
6. If a direct prefix match is found the code extracts the timestamp portion from the stem, attempts to get the file size, and appends a metadata object for that output to the corresponding workflow's outputs list.  
7. If no direct match is found the code tries to infer a workflow key by locating the last occurrence of "-output-" and splitting the stem there, creating a new workflow entry if necessary to record the output.  
8. File size retrieval is wrapped in exception handling so that errors obtaining stat information do not abort processing and instead yield a size of zero.  
9. After collecting outputs the handler sorts each workflow's outputs by the timestamp string in descending order to present recent outputs first.  
10. The workflows dictionary is converted to a sorted list by workflow name and returned as a JSON response via aiohttp.web.json_response.  
11. get_workflow_output checks the requested filename for invalid characters or patterns (empty string, "..", or "/") to block path traversal and returns a 400 error for invalid names.  
12. If the requested file exists the function reads its content in UTF-8 with exception handling and returns the filename and content as JSON, otherwise returning 404 for missing files or 500 for read errors.

---

- No functions, classes, or module-level variables defined (explicitly empty).  
- Placeholder/extension point (intended location for potential future package-level initialization or export control).  

Key logic:

7. The absence of code also means unit tests or runtime diagnostics cannot rely on package-initialization hooks from this module.  
8. Packaging tools that traverse the project will treat the directory as a regular package due to the file's presence.

10. Namespace resolution will continue into subpackages and modules beneath captain_claw.web when those are imported explicitly.
