## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/rest_config.py

Description:
1. This module defines asynchronous REST handlers related to configuration, session listings, and available commands.  
2. It exposes three main aiohttp handler functions that return JSON responses for different API endpoints.  
3. get_config_summary constructs a safe configuration summary that purposely omits secrets and sensitive information.  
4. The config summary uses runtime details from a server.agent when available and falls back to static configuration values otherwise.  
5. list_sessions_api queries the session manager to retrieve up to twenty sessions and returns summarized session metadata.  
6. get_commands_api returns a JSON representation of the COMMANDS object imported from the web server module.  
7. All handlers accept a WebServer instance and an aiohttp.web.Request object as parameters and are declared async.  
8. The module relies on captain_claw.config.get_config to obtain the canonical configuration object.  
9. Responses are created using aiohttp.web.json_response to serialize Python structures to JSON.  
10. The module contains no class definitions and focuses exclusively on lightweight request-to-JSON transformations.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide simple REST endpoints that surface runtime and configuration-related information to clients such as UIs or administrative tools.  
2. By presenting a safe config summary it allows front-end components to display model, context, tool, and guard settings without exposing secrets.  
3. Integrating runtime agent details when available enables the handlers to reflect dynamic state changes from an active agent rather than only static config.  
4. The session-listing handler centralizes the logic for summarizing stored sessions for management consoles or session browsers.  
5. Returning a limited number of sessions (limit=20) prevents excessive payload sizes and discourages expensive large-list operations in the handler itself.  
6. The commands endpoint delegates to a central COMMANDS definition so the UI can retrieve the set of available commands from the running web server.  
7. Implementing these as async aiohttp handlers allows them to be integrated into the existing asynchronous web server and handle concurrent requests.  
8. The module keeps the REST surface minimal and focused, avoiding business logic beyond assembling safe summaries and transforming objects into JSON-serializable dicts.  
9. Placing this logic in a dedicated module separates concerns between web routing, session management, configuration access, and runtime agent introspection.  
10. The handlers are small and suitable for reuse and testing, because each function's responsibility is narrow and its inputs and outputs are well defined.  
11. By depending on higher-level interfaces like get_config and get_session_manager, the module remains decoupled from storage or configuration implementation details.  
12. The overall role is to serve as the glue between internal runtime/config state and external consumers requesting that information over HTTP.

Key elements:
- get_config_summary (async function; builds and returns a safe config summary as JSON).  
- list_sessions_api (async function; retrieves sessions via session manager and returns summarized list).  
- get_commands_api (async function; returns COMMANDS from captain_claw.web_server).  
- get_config (call to captain_claw.config.get_config; used to read static configuration).  
- get_session_manager (imported inside list_sessions_api; provides session listing API).  
- COMMANDS (imported from captain_claw.web_server inside get_commands_api; represents available commands).  
- web.json_response (aiohttp utility used to produce JSON responses).  
- server.agent.get_runtime_model_details (optional call when server.agent is present to obtain live model settings).  
- Access to session attributes: id, name, messages, created_at, updated_at, metadata (used to build session summaries).

Key logic:
1. get_config_summary begins by retrieving the canonical configuration object via get_config and initializing an empty details mapping.  
2. If the provided WebServer instance has an agent attribute, the handler attempts to obtain runtime model details by calling agent.get_runtime_model_details, and uses those values to override config-sourced defaults.  
3. The response payload is explicitly constructed with top-level keys "model", "context", "tools", and "guards", each populated from either the runtime details or the static config.  
4. Within the "model" mapping the handler includes provider, model, temperature, and max_tokens fields, preferring runtime-provided values and falling back to cfg.model.* when absent.  
5. The "context" mapping includes max_tokens and compaction_threshold drawn directly from the configuration object.  
6. Tool availability is reported via cfg.tools.enabled and guard settings are reported via cfg.guards.input.enabled, cfg.guards.output.enabled, and cfg.guards.script_tool.enabled.  
7. list_sessions_api dynamically imports get_session_manager and invokes list_sessions with a fixed limit=20 to obtain recent or available sessions.  
8. For each returned session object, list_sessions_api constructs a summary dict containing id, name, a computed message_count via len(s.messages), timestamps, and a description extracted from session metadata if present.  
9. The session description defaults to an empty string when metadata or the description key is absent, ensuring JSON-serializable and consistent output shapes.  
10. get_commands_api performs a local import of COMMANDS from the web_server module and immediately returns it as a JSON response without transformation.  
11. All handlers rely on aiohttp.web.json_response to convert Python dicts and lists into HTTP JSON responses with appropriate content type and serialization.  
12. The module avoids side effects and does not perform mutation of configuration or sessions; it solely reads state and formats it for consumption by clients.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/rest_cron.py

Description:
1. This module implements aiohttp REST handlers for managing cron jobs via an HTTP API.  
2. It defines endpoints to list, create, run, pause, resume, update, delete, and retrieve history for cron jobs.  
3. Each handler first checks that the server.agent is initialized and returns a 503 error if it is missing.  
4. The list_cron_jobs handler queries the session_manager for up to 200 jobs and returns a JSON array of job summaries.  
5. The create_cron_job handler validates JSON input for kind, schedule, payload, and session_id, computes the next run time, and creates a job via the session_manager.  
6. The run_cron_job handler loads a job by id and triggers its execution asynchronously using an execute_cron_job function.  
7. The pause_cron_job and resume_cron_job handlers toggle a job's enabled state and update status or next_run_at via the session_manager.  
8. The update_cron_job_payload handler patches only the payload field of a job after validating the request body.  
9. The delete_cron_job handler removes a job by id and reports a 404 error when the job is not found.  
10. The get_cron_job_history handler returns stored chat and monitor history for a job and serializes the response with json.dumps(default=str) to handle non-serializable objects.  

Purpose:
1. The file exists to expose an HTTP API that allows clients (such as UIs or administrative tools) to perform CRUD and control operations on scheduled cron jobs managed by the agent.  
2. It centralizes input validation and error handling for cron-related operations so that callers receive consistent JSON responses and HTTP status codes.  
3. By delegating persistence and job lifecycle actions to the session_manager, the module keeps HTTP-layer logic separate from storage and scheduling mechanics.  
4. The create handler supplements user-provided schedules with a human-readable "_text" and computes the canonical next_run_at in UTC, ensuring schedules are normalized before storage.  
5. The run handler enables immediate, manual execution of a cron job without altering its persisted schedule and does so asynchronously to avoid blocking the web request.  
6. Pause, resume, update, and delete handlers provide lightweight endpoints that translate client intentions into session_manager updates and appropriate status reporting.  
7. The module performs conservative validation on inputs (e.g., allowed kinds and schedule structure) to prevent malformed jobs from being created.  
8. Returning structured JSON for job listings and history supports front-end rendering and debugging tools by exposing job metadata and execution traces.  
9. The handlers use common patterns (checking server.agent, loading jobs by id, mapping errors to HTTP responses) to make the behavior predictable and easy to integrate with other server routes.  
10. The module also integrates with cron-specific utilities (compute_next_run, schedule_to_text, to_utc_iso) to ensure time calculations and schedule descriptions are consistent with the rest of the codebase.  
11. Error pathways are explicit and informative, mapping parsing errors, validation failures, and missing resources to appropriate HTTP status codes and JSON messages.  
12. Overall, the file functions as the thin web-facing adapter that translates HTTP requests into session_manager operations and scheduling actions used by the agent runtime.  

Key elements:
- list_cron_jobs (async function; lists jobs via session_manager.list_cron_jobs)  
- create_cron_job (async function; validates input, computes next run, and calls session_manager.create_cron_job)  
- run_cron_job (async function; loads job and triggers execute_cron_job via asyncio.create_task)  
- pause_cron_job (async function; calls session_manager.update_cron_job to disable a job)  
- resume_cron_job (async function; computes next run and updates job to enabled)  
- update_cron_job_payload (async function; patches a job's payload via session_manager.update_cron_job)  
- delete_cron_job (async function; removes a job via session_manager.delete_cron_job)  
- get_cron_job_history (async function; returns job.chat_history and job.monitor_history with json.dumps default=str)  
- server.agent.session_manager (external dependency; used for job CRUD and queries)  
- compute_next_run, schedule_to_text, to_utc_iso (imported cron utilities used for scheduling logic)  
- execute_cron_job (imported from captain_claw.cron_dispatch; used to run jobs)  
- aiohttp.web.json_response and request.json() (framework usage for HTTP I/O and responses)  

Key logic:
1. Each handler begins by checking for server.agent and immediately returns a 503 JSON error when the agent is not initialized, preventing further operations.  
2. list_cron_jobs calls session_manager.list_cron_jobs with a limit and active_only flag, iterates returned job objects, and builds a list of dictionaries with selected job fields for the JSON response.  
3. create_cron_job reads and parses the request body as JSON, validates that "kind" is one of the allowed types, ensures schedule is a dict containing "type", and that payload is a dict and session_id is present.  
4. For schedule handling, create_cron_job augments the schedule with a "_text" generated by schedule_to_text and then computes the next run time using compute_next_run followed by to_utc_iso; failures in these steps produce 400 errors with explanatory messages.  
5. Upon successful validation and computation, create_cron_job calls session_manager.create_cron_job with the normalized schedule, kind, payload, session_id, and next_run_at, returning the created job id and next_run_at.  
6. run_cron_job retrieves the job id from request.match_info, loads the job via session_manager.load_cron_job, and returns 404 if missing; it then obtains a web runtime context from server._get_web_runtime_context and schedules execute_cron_job(ctx, job, trigger="manual") via asyncio.create_task to run asynchronously.  
7. pause_cron_job and resume_cron_job both use request.match_info to get the id, then interact with session_manager.update_cron_job to set enabled=False/True and update last_status and next_run_at as appropriate, mapping nonexistence to 404 responses.  
8. resume_cron_job recomputes next_run_at from the existing job.schedule using the same compute_next_run and to_utc_iso utilities before updating the job to pending and enabled.  
9. update_cron_job_payload validates the presence of a "payload" field in the parsed JSON body and then calls session_manager.update_cron_job to replace the payload, returning a 400 error for missing payload and 404 if the job is not found.  
10. delete_cron_job delegates deletion to session_manager.delete_cron_job and returns a simple {"ok": True} on success or a 404 error when deletion fails.  
11. get_cron_job_history loads the job and returns its chat_history and monitor_history in a JSON response, supplying a custom dumps function that uses json.dumps with default=str to serialize non-standard objects safely.  
12. Error handling across handlers is consistent: parse errors return 400, missing resources return 404, uninitialized agent returns 503, and unexpected failures in triggering execution return 500 with the exception string.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/rest_entities.py

Description:
1. This module implements aiohttp REST handlers for CRUD operations on Todos, Contacts, Scripts, and APIs.  
2. Each handler first verifies that server.agent is present and returns a 503 JSON error if it is not.  
3. List and search handlers call the session_manager to retrieve collections with fixed limits and serialize results using a JSON dumper that falls back to str for non-serializable objects.  
4. Create handlers parse and validate JSON request bodies, sanitize and default incoming fields, and call session_manager.create_* methods returning 201 on success.  
5. Get handlers load single entities via session_manager.load_* and return 404 when the entity is not found.  
6. Update handlers read JSON bodies, build kwargs from allowed fields, perform small field-specific adjustments (e.g., clamping importance), and call session_manager.update_* returning 404 if the target is missing.  
7. Delete handlers call session_manager.delete_* and return a 404 when deletion fails or an {"ok": True} on success.  
8. Search endpoints require a non-empty query parameter and return 400 when q is missing.  
9. The module consistently converts incoming values to strings with strip(), casts numeric inputs where needed, and uses explicit limits for list/search operations.  
10. Error handling covers invalid JSON bodies, missing required fields, missing entities, and uninitialized agent state with appropriate JSON responses and HTTP status codes.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to expose a simple HTTP API layer that translates external HTTP requests into calls against the application's session_manager persistence/service layer.  
2. It centralizes request validation, sanitization, and HTTP-level error reporting for several entity types so higher-level business logic can remain focused in the session manager and models.  
3. Grouping handlers by entity type (Todos, Contacts, Scripts, APIs) provides a clear structure that mirrors the backend session_manager capabilities and keeps routes organized.  
4. The module enforces minimal input validation (required fields, non-empty query parameters) to prevent malformed data from reaching storage.  
5. It standardizes JSON serialization across handlers through a shared dumper that safely converts non-standard objects.  
6. By returning conventional HTTP status codes (201 for creation, 400 for bad requests, 404 for missing resources, 503 for uninitialized agent) the file enables predictable client behavior and easier integration with UIs and tools.  
7. The handlers apply simple normalization for incoming fields (str(...).strip(), optional defaults), reducing duplication of that boilerplate across the codebase.  
8. Limited list and search sizes (limits like 50 or 200) provide a basic protection against heavy queries via the API surface.  
9. The file intentionally delegates persistence, domain validation, and complex business rules to the session_manager, acting mainly as a thin translation and validation layer.  
10. Its design allows the web server to be started even if agent is not yet initialized while providing clear 503 responses until the backend is ready.  
11. The module is designed to be minimal and easily extendable with additional entity handlers or fields by following the established patterns.  
12. Overall, it exists to provide a predictable, consistent, and lightweight REST interface that maps HTTP semantics to the internal session management operations.

Key elements:
- _JSON_DUMPS (lambda) (JSON dumper using json.dumps(default=str) for safe serialization).  
- list_todos (handler) (lists todos with optional filters).  
- create_todo (handler) (validates and creates a todo via session_manager.create_todo).  
- update_todo (handler) (patches todo fields and calls session_manager.update_todo/load_todo).  
- delete_todo (handler) (deletes a todo via session_manager.delete_todo).  
- list_contacts (handler) (lists contacts).  
- search_contacts (handler) (requires q and searches contacts).  
- create_contact (handler) (validates and creates a contact with many optional fields).  
- get_contact (handler) (loads a single contact).  
- update_contact (handler) (patches contact, clamps importance, sets importance_pinned).  
- delete_contact (handler) (deletes a contact).  
- list_scripts / search_scripts / create_script / get_script / update_script / delete_script (handlers) (CRUD and search for scripts).  
- list_apis / search_apis / create_api / get_api / update_api / delete_api (handlers) (CRUD and search for API definitions).  
- Dependencies on aiohttp.web (web.Response/json_response), json, and the server.agent.session_manager API methods (list_*, search_*, create_*, load_*, update_*, delete_*).  
- Use of request.json(), request.query, and request.match_info for input.

Key logic:
1. Every handler begins by verifying the presence of server.agent and short-circuits with a 503 JSON error if the agent is not initialized.  
2. List handlers call the corresponding session_manager.list_* method with a hard-coded limit (usually 200) and serialize returned model objects by calling to_dict on each item.  
3. Search handlers extract the q parameter, trim it, and return a 400 error if q is empty; they then call session_manager.search_* with a smaller limit (usually 50).  
4. Create handlers attempt to parse the JSON body, return 400 on parse failure, validate required fields (e.g., name/base_url/file_path/content), and construct creation arguments by trimming string inputs and providing defaults or None for optional fields.  
5. On successful creation handlers return the created item's to_dict serialized JSON with HTTP 201.  
6. Get handlers extract an id from request.match_info, call session_manager.load_*, and return 404 if the item is not found otherwise returning its to_dict.  
7. Update (PATCH) handlers parse JSON, iterate over an allowed list of fields to build kwargs, convert values to trimmed strings or None, and for numeric fields perform conversions and constraints (for example, clamping contact importance between 1 and 10 and setting an importance_pinned flag).  
8. Update handlers call session_manager.update_*, check the boolean response to detect missing targets (returning 404), and then load and return the updated object when available.  
9. Delete handlers call session_manager.delete_*, return 404 if deletion reports failure, and otherwise return a simple {"ok": True} JSON response.  
10. Throughout the module, input normalization is consistently applied via str(...).strip() and int(...) where used, preventing accidental storage of raw structures.  
11. The shared _JSON_DUMPS function is used when serializing lists or objects to ensure that any non-serializable fields are represented as strings instead of breaking responses.  
12. Error responses are explicit and consistent: invalid JSON yields 400, missing parameters yield 400, missing resources yield 404, and uninitialized backend yields 503, enabling straightforward client-side handling.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/ws_handler.py

Description:
1. This module implements a WebSocket protocol handler for the web UI.  
2. It defines an async ws_handler function that prepares and manages WebSocket connections using aiohttp.web.WebSocketResponse.  
3. When a client connects the handler registers the socket in server.clients and sends a welcome payload containing session info, allowed models, and available commands.  
4. If an Agent with an active session exists the handler replays prior session messages to the connecting client, translating stored roles and tools into chat or monitor messages.  
5. Replayed messages distinguish between user, assistant, and tool roles and may convert specific tool messages like task_rephrase into visible chat panels.  
6. The module reads incoming messages in a loop, decodes JSON text frames, and reports invalid JSON back to the client.  
7. Decoded messages are dispatched to handle_ws_message which routes chat messages, slash/command invocations, cancellation signals, and approval responses.  
8. Chat messages beginning with a slash are forwarded to a slash command handler while other chat text is sent to the chat handler.  
9. The ws_handler logs WebSocket errors and ensures the client is removed from server.clients when the connection closes.  
10. The module relies on server methods such as _send and _session_info and on Agent helpers to filter monitor-only tools.  

Purpose:
1. This file exists to provide a centralized gateway between the browser-based UI and the server-side Agent and session state.  
2. It supplies an entry point for incoming WebSocket connections and ensures each connected client receives the current session context and configuration.  
3. By replaying past session messages it brings newly connected clients up to date without requiring additional REST calls.  
4. The handler translates internal session message representations into structured UI events (chat_message, monitor, replay_done) that the front end can render.  
5. It validates and normalizes incoming WebSocket payloads, returning structured error messages for invalid JSON.  
6. Messages are dispatched to specialized modules (slash_commands and chat_handler) so that command parsing and chat processing remain modular and testable.  
7. The ws_handler also surfaces control actions like cancellation to the running Agent by setting a cancel_event, allowing UI-driven interruption of operations.  
8. Implementation choices such as max_msg_size, server.clients tracking, and explicit use of server._send enforce resource limits and centralized delivery semantics.  
9. Use of Agent._is_monitor_only_tool_name allows the handler to suppress monitor messages that should not be shown to users, centralizing visibility policy.  
10. Having a dedicated WebSocket module simplifies lifecycle management including connection preparation, error logging, and cleanup on disconnect.  
11. The module therefore exists to provide reliable, real-time bidirectional communication, integrate server agent state with the UI, and delegate domain logic to other components.  
12. Its responsibilities are narrowly scoped to connection and message dispatch so higher-level behaviors remain in agent and handler modules.  

Key elements:
- ws_handler (async function; prepares WebSocket, registers client, sends welcome, replays session, receives messages).  
- handle_ws_message (async function; dispatches message types: chat, command, cancel, approval_response).  
- aiohttp.web.WebSocketResponse (used to manage WebSocket connection; configured with max_msg_size).  
- server.clients (set; tracks active WebSocket clients).  
- server._send (method called to send structured events to a client).  
- server._session_info (method used to include session metadata in welcome payload).  
- server.agent.get_allowed_models (call to populate allowed models in welcome payload, guarded by server.agent presence).  
- COMMANDS (imported from captain_claw.web_server; included in welcome payload).  
- Agent._is_monitor_only_tool_name (helper used to filter out monitor-only tool messages).  
- Delegated handlers: captain_claw.web.slash_commands.handle_command and captain_claw.web.chat_handler.handle_chat.  
- JSON parsing with json.loads and JSONDecodeError handling.  
- server.agent.cancel_event (used to propagate cancel requests).  
- Logging via captain_claw.logging.get_logger for errors and cancellation notices.  

Key logic:
1. The ws_handler coroutine creates a WebSocketResponse with a configured max message size and awaits its preparation with the incoming request.  
2. It immediately registers the socket in server.clients to track active connections and constructs a welcome payload by calling server._session_info and retrieving allowed models from server.agent if present.  
3. COMMANDS is imported from the web_server module and included in the welcome payload so the client knows available slash commands.  
4. If an agent session exists the handler iterates over session.messages and inspects each message's role, content, and tool metadata to determine how to forward it.  
5. Messages with roles 'user' or 'assistant' are forwarded as chat_message events while certain tool messages are rendered as rephrase chat panels and other tool outputs are sent as monitor events unless filtered by Agent._is_monitor_only_tool_name.  
6. After replaying messages the handler sends a replay_done event to indicate the replay sequence is complete.  
7. The main receive loop uses async for raw_msg in ws to process incoming frames and checks the message type to handle text frames and track errors.  
8. Text frames are parsed as JSON; JSONDecodeError triggers an error response back to the client and the loop continues without dispatch.  
9. Valid messages are handed to handle_ws_message which inspects a top-level type field and routes to appropriate behavior.  
10. For type 'chat' the message content is normalized, empty content is ignored, and content starting with '/' is treated as a slash command while other chat text is passed to the chat handler.  
11. For type 'command' the handler normalizes and forwards the command string to the command handler.  
12. For type 'cancel' the function sets server.agent.cancel_event when available to request cancellation and logs the action.  
13. The type 'approval_response' is recognized but currently a no-op placeholder.  
14. On exit from the receive loop the finally block ensures the socket is removed from server.clients and the WebSocketResponse is returned to complete cleanup.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/google_oauth.py

Description:
1. This module implements HTTP handlers for Google OAuth2 flows used by the web server.  
2. It provides endpoints to start the login flow, handle the OAuth callback, report status, and perform logout.  
3. The login handler validates configuration, generates a PKCE verifier/challenge pair and a random state, records the pending state, and redirects the browser to Google's authorization URL.  
4. The callback handler validates the returned code and state, exchanges the authorization code for tokens, and optionally fetches user profile information.  
5. On successful token exchange it stores tokens and user info via the server's OAuth manager and injects credentials into an LLM provider when applicable.  
6. A status handler returns JSON indicating whether Google OAuth is enabled, connected, and includes stored user info when connected.  
7. The logout handler instructs the OAuth manager to disconnect and clears injected credentials from the active provider.  
8. Utilities in the module purge stale pending PKCE states older than ten minutes to avoid replayed or expired states.  
9. The module uses aiohttp.web types and responses and constructs HTML responses for human-facing error and success pages.  
10. It relies on helper functions from captain_claw.google_oauth for PKCE generation, URL building, token exchange, and user info retrieval.  

Purpose:
1. This file exists to integrate Google OAuth2 authentication into the web component of the application and to centralize the HTTP endpoints related to that integration.  
2. It enables users to authenticate via Google and allows the server to obtain, store, and use OAuth tokens and user profile information.  
3. The handlers enforce basic configuration checks so OAuth is only available when enabled and properly configured.  
4. By generating PKCE pairs and state tokens the module improves security and prevents CSRF/replay attacks during the OAuth flow.  
5. The callback handler converts the OAuth authorization code into usable tokens and handles errors with informative HTML responses to aid debugging or user feedback.  
6. Storing tokens and user info through the server's OAuth manager decouples credential persistence from HTTP handling and centralizes token lifecycle operations.  
7. Injecting credentials into the Gemini (Vertex) provider allows LLM-related functionality to access Google services when required, bridging authentication and model provider configuration.  
8. The status endpoint provides a simple JSON API for frontend components to show connection state and the connected user's identity.  
9. The logout endpoint allows administrators or users to revoke stored credentials and to remove those credentials from any active providers.  
10. Logging is included to record token exchange failures and user info fetch issues so administrators can diagnose problems.  
11. The module is intentionally lightweight and delegates heavy lifting (token exchange, PKCE, user info fetching) to dedicated helper functions and an OAuth manager implementation.  
12. Overall, the file exists to provide a secure, user-facing OAuth flow and to make acquired credentials available to other server components in a controlled way.  

Key elements:
- auth_google_login (async function) — starts OAuth flow, generates state and PKCE, stores pending state, redirects to Google.  
- auth_google_callback (async function) — handles OAuth callback, validates state/code, exchanges code for tokens, fetches user info, stores tokens, and injects credentials.  
- auth_google_status (async function) — returns JSON with connected/enabled flags and user info when connected.  
- auth_google_logout (async function) — revokes/disconnects stored tokens and clears injected credentials.  
- inject_oauth_into_provider (async function) — retrieves vertex credentials from OAuth manager and injects into LiteLLMProvider (Gemini) if active.  
- clear_oauth_from_provider (function) — clears vertex credentials from an active LiteLLMProvider.  
- generate_pkce_pair, build_authorization_url, exchange_code_for_tokens, fetch_user_info (external helpers from captain_claw.google_oauth).  
- server._pending_oauth (dict) — in-memory pending state storage keyed by state with verifier and timestamp.  
- server._oauth_manager (pluggable manager) — used to store tokens, store user info, check connection, get credentials, disconnect.  
- get_config (external call) — reads google_oauth settings such as enabled, client_id, client_secret, scopes, project_id, location, and web port.  
- LiteLLMProvider and its methods set_vertex_credentials / clear_vertex_credentials (used when provider == "gemini").  
- aiohttp.web responses and exceptions (web.Response, web.json_response, web.HTTPFound) — used for HTTP interactions.  
- logging via get_logger — logs token exchange failures and user info fetch warnings.  

Key logic:
1. The login endpoint first reads configuration and returns an error JSON response if Google OAuth is not enabled or missing client_id.  
2. It purges any pending PKCE states older than 600 seconds to limit the validity window and prevent stale state reuse.  
3. A random URL-safe state token is generated and a PKCE verifier/challenge pair is created; the verifier is saved alongside a timestamp under server._pending_oauth[state].  
4. The module constructs a redirect_uri pointing to localhost with the configured web port and builds the Google authorization URL using provided scopes and the PKCE challenge, then issues an HTTP redirect to that URL.  
5. The callback handler inspects the query for an error parameter and returns an HTML error page if present, providing user-facing diagnostics.  
6. It validates presence of both code and state, then attempts to pop the matching pending state; missing or expired state results in an HTML error response.  
7. The handler performs the token exchange by calling exchange_code_for_tokens with the authorization code, client credentials, redirect URI, and the stored PKCE verifier; token exchange failures are logged and returned as HTML error pages.  
8. After obtaining tokens it tries to fetch Google user info with the access token, logs a warning on failure, and proceeds with empty user info if necessary.  
9. If an OAuth manager is configured on the server, the handler stores the tokens and user info through that manager and then calls inject_oauth_into_provider to pass vertex credentials into a Gemini provider if present.  
10. The successful callback returns a small HTML page that indicates the connected account and automatically redirects the browser back to the home page.  
11. The status handler reads configuration and the server's OAuth manager to return a JSON object describing whether OAuth is enabled, whether a connection exists, and the stored user info when connected.  
12. The logout handler asks the OAuth manager to disconnect, then calls clear_oauth_from_provider to remove any injected vertex credentials from the active provider, and returns a JSON confirmation.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/rest_instructions.py

Description:
1. This module provides aiohttp REST handlers for managing markdown instruction files used by the application.  
2. It exposes handlers to list available instruction files, read a specific instruction, save a personal override, and revert a personal override to the system default.  
3. The listing handler merges files from a system directory and a personal overrides directory, marking files that are overridden.  
4. The read handler validates the requested file name, prefers a personal override if present, and returns the file content as JSON.  
5. The save handler validates the name and resolved path, writes content into the personal overrides directory, and reports whether the file was created or updated.  
6. The revert handler deletes a personal override (if present), ensures a system default exists, and returns the reverted system content.  
7. All file reads and writes use UTF-8 encoding and report file sizes from the filesystem.  
8. Name validation prevents path traversal and requires the filename to end with the ".md" suffix.  
9. When changes occur the handlers clear the agent's instruction cache for the named file if an agent is attached to the server.  
10. Responses are returned as JSON objects with status details, file metadata, and content when applicable.

Purpose:
1. This file exists to provide HTTP endpoints that let clients manage instruction markdown files used by the application.  
2. It centralizes the filesystem operations and validation logic for instruction content so that web clients can view, edit, and revert instructions through the web API.  
3. By supporting both a system directory and a personal overrides directory, it enables a default set of instructions to be shipped while allowing user-specific customizations.  
4. The module enforces filename and path safety to prevent directory traversal and accidental writes outside the intended personal directory.  
5. Returning metadata such as file size and overridden status helps clients present a combined view of available and overridden instructions.  
6. Clearing the agent's cached instruction entry when a personal file is saved or reverted ensures consumers of instructions will see updated content.  
7. The handlers return clear error JSONs and HTTP status codes for invalid names, missing files, and invalid revert attempts, supporting robust client behavior.  
8. Using simple JSON responses keeps the API straightforward to consume from JavaScript frontends or other HTTP clients.  
9. The module is lightweight and focused on file management concerns, delegating higher-level instruction parsing or agent behavior to other components.  
10. It exists as part of the web server layer, mapping REST endpoints to safe filesystem operations and coordinating cache invalidation with the agent when present.  
11. The separation of system and personal directories implemented here supports an expected workflow of shipping defaults while preserving user edits.  
12. Overall, it provides a controlled, auditable mechanism for manipulating instruction files via HTTP.

Key elements:
- list_instructions (async handler) — merges system and personal instruction directories and returns a sorted JSON list.  
- get_instruction (async handler) — validates a filename, selects personal or system file, reads content, and returns JSON.  
- put_instruction (async handler) — validates filename and path containment, writes content to personal directory, creates directories as needed, and clears agent cache.  
- revert_instruction (async handler) — validates filename, removes the personal override, verifies system default exists, reads system content, and clears agent cache.  
- server._instructions_dir (filesystem Path) — system instruction directory used as the default source.  
- server._instructions_personal_dir (filesystem Path) — personal override directory where edits are written.  
- server.agent.instructions._cache (dict access) — cache that is popped to invalidate cached instruction content when files change.  
- web.json_response (aiohttp) — used to construct JSON HTTP responses with optional status codes.  
- Path.read_text / write_text / stat / unlink / is_file / is_dir / iterdir (pathlib) — filesystem operations used throughout.  
- path.resolve().relative_to(...) check — used to ensure saved paths remain inside the personal directory.

Key logic:
1. The listing handler builds a dictionary keyed by filename to deduplicate system and personal entries, processing system files first and then overwriting entries with personal overrides so overridden status and size reflect the personal file.  
2. Both directories are iterated in sorted order and only files with a ".md" suffix and that are regular files are collected.  
3. The final list returned by the listing handler is sorted by filename and returned as JSON objects containing name, size, and overridden flag.  
4. Filename validation in the read, put, and revert handlers rejects names containing "..", forward slashes, backslashes (for put/revert), or names not ending with ".md" and returns a 400 error JSON for invalid names.  
5. The read handler constructs personal and system paths, determines whether the personal path exists, chooses the appropriate path, checks existence, reads the file content with UTF-8, and returns name, content, and overridden flag; missing files produce a 404 JSON.  
6. The save (put) handler additionally checks that the resolved target path is actually inside the personal directory using resolve().relative_to(...); a ValueError from that check triggers a 400 invalid path response.  
7. The save handler reads JSON body content from the request, ensures the personal directory exists by creating parents if necessary, writes the content with UTF-8, and determines whether the action created a new file or updated an existing one to set the status field.  
8. After writing or deleting a personal file, handlers check server.agent and, if present, remove the named entry from server.agent.instructions._cache to force downstream refreshes of instruction content.  
9. The revert handler ensures a personal override exists and that a system default also exists before unlinking the personal file; if the system default is missing it returns a 400 error indicating revert cannot proceed.  
10. On successful revert, the handler reads the system file text and returns a JSON response with status "reverted", the content, size, and overridden false.  
11. All handlers rely on aiohttp.web.Request match_info to obtain the requested filename and use aiohttp.web.json_response for uniform structured HTTP responses.  
12. Error conditions are handled with appropriate HTTP status codes (400 for invalid input or bad path, 404 for not found) and explanatory JSON error messages.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/web/static_pages.py

Description:
1. This module defines asynchronous aiohttp request handlers that serve static pages for the web UI.  
2. It computes a STATIC_DIR path relative to the module file and uses it as the source for static assets.  
3. Several handlers return web.FileResponse objects that point to specific HTML files inside STATIC_DIR.  
4. The serve_favicon handler checks for the presence of a favicon.svg file and returns it if present.  
5. If the favicon file is not present, serve_favicon returns a web.Response with status 204 instead of a file.  
6. Handlers are declared to accept a server object (typed as WebServer under TYPE_CHECKING) and the aiohttp request.  
7. The module imports pathlib.Path for filesystem path manipulation and aiohttp.web for response types.  
8. All HTML filenames used by handlers are hard-coded (e.g., home.html, index.html, orchestrator.html).  
9. The module contains no additional routing logic, error handling beyond the favicon check, or dynamic content generation.  
10. The overall design is a lightweight static-file-serving layer for the application's frontend pages.

Purpose:
1. This file exists to centralize and expose simple aiohttp handlers that deliver the web application's static HTML pages.  
2. By resolving STATIC_DIR relative to the module, it makes the static assets location explicit and portable across deployments.  
3. The handlers provide a clear mapping between logical endpoints (home, chat, orchestrator, etc.) and concrete HTML files.  
4. Implementing these handlers as async functions maintains compatibility with aiohttp's handler model and the rest of the web server.  
5. The serve_favicon handler includes a small optimization/guard to avoid returning a missing-file response when the favicon is absent.  
6. Typing the server parameter via TYPE_CHECKING with WebServer documents the intended server context without requiring runtime imports.  
7. Keeping filenames hard-coded simplifies the routing and reduces configuration complexity for the static UI assets.  
8. The module is intentionally minimal so it can be reused or extended easily if additional static pages are added.  
9. It separates concerns by handling only static page delivery while leaving routing registration and business logic to the web server.  
10. This separation makes tests and maintenance easier because the handlers have deterministic behavior tied to files.  
11. The module relies on aiohttp.web primitives so it integrates directly with middleware, static resource handling, and server lifecycle.  
12. Overall, the purpose is to provide a simple, maintainable bridge between HTTP endpoints and the frontend's static HTML files.

Key elements:
- STATIC_DIR (pathlib.Path) — base directory for static files resolved relative to this module.  
- serve_home(server, request) — async handler that serves "home.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- serve_chat(server, request) — async handler that serves "index.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- serve_favicon(server, request) — async handler that serves "favicon.svg" if it exists, otherwise returns web.Response(status=204).  
- serve_orchestrator(server, request) — async handler that serves "orchestrator.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- serve_instructions(server, request) — async handler that serves "instructions.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- serve_cron(server, request) — async handler that serves "cron.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- serve_workflows(server, request) — async handler that serves "workflows.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- serve_loop_runner(server, request) — async handler that serves "loop-runner.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- serve_memory(server, request) — async handler that serves "memory.html" via web.FileResponse.  
- Imports: pathlib.Path (for path resolution) and aiohttp.web (for FileResponse and Response).  
- TYPE_CHECKING + WebServer typing (used for type hints without runtime import).

Key logic:
1. On import, STATIC_DIR is computed as the "static" subdirectory located next to the module file, using Path(__file__).resolve().parent / "static".  
2. Each handler is an async function that accepts a server parameter and the incoming aiohttp request, matching the expected handler signature.  
3. For most endpoints, the handler constructs a path by joining STATIC_DIR with a hard-coded HTML filename and returns web.FileResponse pointing to that path.  
4. The use of web.FileResponse delegates file serving to aiohttp's response mechanism rather than reading file contents into memory inside the handler.  
5. The serve_favicon handler first resolves the favicon.svg path and checks favicon.is_file() to decide whether to return a FileResponse or a 204 Response.  
6. There is no other file existence checking or explicit error handling in the handlers; they rely on aiohttp's FileResponse behavior for file delivery.  
7. Handlers do not inspect request attributes, query parameters, or headers; they always serve the same static file for a given endpoint.  
8. The presence of TYPE_CHECKING and an import annotation for WebServer means the server parameter is intended to be used by the caller or for future extensions but is not used at runtime here.  
9. Because filenames are fixed, adding new static endpoints requires adding a new handler that returns the corresponding FileResponse for the new file.  
10. The module's control flow is straightforward and synchronous at the application level: compute path, check favicon existence when applicable, return appropriate aiohttp response.  
11. Any filesystem or permission errors when aiohttp attempts to open the files will be handled by aiohttp or surface as exceptions; this module does not catch them.  
12. The design favors simplicity and low overhead, making the handlers easy to register with the web server's routing table and predictable in behavior.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/session/__init__.py

Description:
1. This module implements session and cross-session persistence using an SQLite database accessed asynchronously via aiosqlite.  
2. It declares multiple dataclasses representing domain entities such as Message, Session, CronJob, TodoItem, ContactEntry, ContactMention, ScriptEntry, and ApiEntry.  
3. The SessionManager class encapsulates database initialization, schema creation, and CRUD operations for sessions, cron jobs, to-dos, contacts, scripts, and APIs.  
4. Database initialization creates tables and indexes and includes a migration step to add missing cron_jobs columns for backward compatibility.  
5. Many fields that are structured (messages, payloads, histories, metadata) are serialized to and from JSON when stored in the SQLite tables.  
6. Selection helpers accept flexible selectors (exact id, named entity, or numeric index using optional "#" prefixes) for sessions, cron jobs, todos, scripts, and APIs.  
7. The module implements utility behaviors such as computing a UTC ISO timestamp, archiving old todos, incrementing usage counters, and appending per-job history with size trimming.  
8. Contact importance can be auto-computed from mention frequency, recency, and the number of distinct sessions, and that computed value is persisted.  
9. A simple global singleton pattern exposes a module-level SessionManager via get_session_manager and set_session_manager functions.  
10. The module depends on standard libraries (json, uuid, datetime, pathlib, dataclasses, typing) and on project-specific get_config and get_logger utilities.

Purpose:
1. The file exists to provide a centralized, persistent store for conversational sessions and various cross-session memories required by the application.  
2. It exists to make session data durable between runs by mapping in-memory dataclasses to SQLite rows and JSON blobs in a consistent schema.  
3. By encapsulating schema creation and migration logic in _ensure_db and _ensure_cron_jobs_migrations, the module ensures forward- and backward-compatible storage across releases.  
4. It supplies a single abstraction (SessionManager) that other parts of the application can call to create, load, list, update, and delete sessions and related domain objects.  
5. The selection helpers and list/search methods provide convenient, user-facing resolution semantics (id/name/index/fuzzy match) so UI or CLI code can resolve items flexibly.  
6. The module centralizes auxiliary app state storage and last-active-session tracking so session lifecycle and user context can be preserved.  
7. Cron job persistence and related helpers are included so scheduled or pseudo-cron tasks can be managed, queried for due work, and have execution history recorded.  
8. To-do items, contacts, scripts, and API memories are stored here to enable cross-session features such as reminders, address-book functionality, script reuse, and API endpoint management.  
9. The auto-importance and archival routines provide simple domain-specific logic (importance scoring, tombstoning old items) that keeps stored data actionable without external tooling.  
10. JSON serialization of structured columns and indices for common access patterns (name, updated_at, use_count, importance) optimize typical queries executed by UI and orchestration layers.  
11. The global singleton accessor is provided to avoid duplicating connection setup and to make manager reuse easy across the codebase.  
12. Methods that increment usage and timestamps support telemetry-style bookkeeping (use_count, last_used_at) for prioritization and ordering in lists and searches.  
13. The module's async API is tailored for an asynchronous application architecture, allowing non-blocking database access from web handlers, schedulers, or background tasks.  
14. Overall, it exists to be the authoritative, durable store for conversational context and related artifacts needed by other project components.

Key elements:
- _utcnow_iso (function): returns current UTC time in ISO format.  
- Message (dataclass): lightweight message record with role, content, tool metadata, tokens, timestamp.  
- Session (dataclass): conversation session with id, name, messages, created_at, updated_at, metadata; methods add_message, to_dict, from_dict.  
- CronJob (dataclass): persisted pseudo-cron job with from_row constructor and fields for schedule, history, status.  
- TodoItem (dataclass): to-do entry with from_row and to_dict.  
- ContactEntry (dataclass): contact/address-book entry with from_row and to_dict.  
- ContactMention (dataclass): mention log with from_row.  
- ScriptEntry (dataclass): stored script/file memory with from_row and to_dict.  
- ApiEntry (dataclass): stored API memory with from_row and to_dict.  
- SessionManager (class): core manager handling DB path config, _ensure_db, schema creation, and extensive CRUD for sessions, cron jobs, todos, contacts, scripts, and apis.  
- SessionManager methods of note: get_or_create_session, load_session, save_session, list_sessions, delete_session; create_cron_job, list_cron_jobs, get_due_cron_jobs, update_cron_job, append_cron_job_history; create_todo, list_todos, update_todo, archive_old_todos; create_contact, search_contacts, update_contact, increment_contact_mention, compute_auto_importance; create_script/search_scripts/update_script/increment_script_usage; create_api/search_apis/update_api/increment_api_usage; close.  
- App state helpers: get_app_state, set_app_state, delete_app_state, get_last_active_session_id, set_last_active_session, load_last_active_session.  
- Global singleton: _manager, get_session_manager, set_session_manager.  
- External dependencies: aiosqlite (async DB), json (serialization), uuid (ids), get_config (config retrieval), get_logger (logging), pathlib.Path, datetime.UTC.

Key logic:
1. On first use, SessionManager._ensure_db opens an aiosqlite connection, creates required tables, and defines multiple indexes to support efficient queries; it then runs migrations for cron_jobs to add missing columns when needed.  
2. Structured fields (lists, dicts) are marshaled to JSON strings for storage and unmarshaled on read; this pattern is used for messages, payloads, schedules, histories, and metadata.  
3. Session creation assigns a UUID, default timestamps, and immediately persists the new session with save_session which updates updated_at and writes a JSON-encoded messages field.  
4. Session selection supports three resolution strategies: direct id lookup, latest session with matching name, and numeric index into the recent sessions list parsed from selectors that may start with "#".  
5. List methods build SQL queries with ORDER BY clauses optimized for their domain (e.g., sessions ordered by updated_at, scripts and apis ordered by use_count then updated_at, contacts ordered by importance and mention_count).  
6. Update methods construct dynamic SQL assignments from provided keyword arguments, prepend an updated_at timestamp, and execute a single UPDATE statement, returning a boolean based on affected rowcount.  
7. Cron job retrieval includes filters for enabled jobs and next_run_at comparisons to implement get_due_cron_jobs; append_cron_job_history reads the job, appends events, trims lists to max_entries, and writes the updated JSON back via update_cron_job.  
8. To-do listing composes WHERE clauses conditionally for status/responsible/session filters and applies a CASE-based priority ordering to surface urgent items first; update_todo sets completed_at when status transitions to done.  
9. archive_old_todos computes age using SQLite julianday differences and marks long-completed items as cancelled in a single UPDATE statement.  
10. Contact management includes fuzzy search using SQL LIKE with COLLATE NOCASE, mention recording that inserts into contact_mentions and atomically increments mention_count and last_seen_at on the contact row.  
11. compute_auto_importance reads mention_count and last_seen_at to compute a recency factor (21-day half-life), queries distinct session mentions for a diversity factor, computes a log2-based score, clamps it between 1 and 10, and persists the computed importance via update_contact.  
12. Script and API memories support create/read/update/delete plus search by LIKE patterns and ordering by use_count to help discover frequently used items; increment_*_usage updates use_count and timestamps.  
13. Selector helpers for scripts, apis, cron jobs, and todos share similar behaviors: try direct id, then numeric index when prefixed with "#", then fallback to search returning the first match.  
14. The module maintains a simple global singleton manager instance lazily instantiated by get_session_manager to centralize connection lifecycle; set_session_manager allows tests or alternative instances to be injected.

---

## captain-claw-src/captain_claw/agent_tool_loop_mixin.py

Description:
1. The AgentToolLoopMixin module provides a comprehensive set of helpers for parsing, executing, and managing tool calls produced by an LLM-driven agent. 
2. It implements robust mechanisms for scale-aware processing, including guards against off-track behavior, duplicate call detection, and context trimming to keep the conversation size bounded. 
3. The mixin supports a micro-turn scale loop that extracts, processes with a single isolated LLM call, and writes results per item to avoid context growth and LLM confusion. 
4. It includes utilities to derive item labels, detect the appropriate extractor for a given item (URL, file path or extension), and build concise item-specific prompts that include optional format references. 
5. The code instruments execution with progress and thinking indicators, precise timing, and token accounting to monitor performance and ETA. 
6. Tool call extraction supports many embedded formats (code blocks, XML-like invocations, JSON blobs, and pseudo-DSL patterns) and normalizes them to ToolCall objects. 
7. Execution of tool calls is mediated by guards (scale guard), duplicate-call limits, and stateful vs stateless tool classification. 
8. After tool execution, the mixin updates internal scale progress, emits outputs into the session, and triggers trimming of large extractor outputs to reclaim context tokens. 
9. It also contains helper methods for friendly rewrite of raw tool output, clipping long outputs for rewrite prompts, and heuristics about whether the runtime model supports tool-result followups. 
10. Overall, the module is focused on reliable, incremental, and scalable execution of tool-driven agent workflows.

Purpose:
1. The primary purpose of AgentToolLoopMixin is to make large-scale, item-by-item processing dependable and efficient when orchestrated by an LLM, by enforcing a strict extract→process→write pattern that prevents the LLM from re-discovering or re-reading items and avoids quadratic context growth. 
2. It provides a scale guard that actively blocks or redirects off-track tool calls (like re-globbing, reading output files, or re-extracting already-processed items) so the agent behaves like a state machine and follows the intended incremental workflow. 
3. The mixin implements a micro-turn loop that isolates each item's processing into a single short LLM conversation, thereby keeping latency and context size constant regardless of list length and allowing thousands of items to be processed without LLM confusion. 
4. It centralizes tool-call parsing from free-form model responses, turning varied embedded syntax into structured ToolCall objects for consistent handling. 
5. The mixin also performs duplicate-call detection with configurable thresholds and special allowances during scale tasks, which reduces wasted executions and prevents repeated expensive operations. 
6. It tracks progress transparently (total, completed, remaining) and injects a compact progress note into LLM calls so the model never needs to re-glob or re-check the output. 
7. When writes occur, the mixin attempts to detect which item was written and marks items as done, updating internal counters and optionally compressing older assistant/tool message pairs to conserve tokens. 
8. The mixin supports multiple output strategies (single shared file, per-item files, or no-file sinks like typesense/email) and routes writes accordingly. 
9. It exposes hooks and emits structured monitoring messages so the hosting agent can surface human-friendly progress and diagnostics. 
10. Finally, the mixin coordinates cancellation, error accumulation, and retry-friendly behaviors (like rolling back duplicate counters on failure) to make large automated runs robust and recoverable.

Key elements:
- Methods (major): _trim_processed_extracts_in_session, _scale_guard_intercept, _build_scale_progress_note, _derive_member_label, _detect_item_extractor, _build_scale_item_prompt, _resolve_per_item_filename, _run_scale_micro_loop, _scale_loop_ready, _get_scale_task_description.
- Methods (utilities): _tool_thinking_summary, _extract_command_from_response, _supports_tool_result_followup, _collect_turn_tool_output, _turn_has_successful_tool, _clip_tool_output_for_rewrite, _friendly_tool_output_response, _extract_tool_calls_from_content, _handle_tool_calls.
- Objects / attributes: self.session (session message list), self._scale_progress (tracking dict), Message, ToolCall, cancel_event, instructions, tools registry, various helper counters (e.g. _turn_tool_call_counts).
- External calls / hooks: _execute_tool_with_guard (executes named tools), _complete_with_guards (LLM completion wrapper), _emit_thinking (status line), _emit_tool_output (UI/log output), _add_session_message (store tool results), _count_tokens (token accounting), get_config(), get_logger().
- Data flows: tool call parsing → guard/dup checks → _execute_tool_with_guard → session append + emit → scale progress updates → optional trimming and monitoring emits.

Key logic:
1. The mixin implements a layered guarding strategy to keep scale tasks on-track: a scale guard intercepts calls that would rediscover items or re-read output files and returns a redirect message instead of executing the tool. 
2. Duplicate-call detection computes a canonical signature per tool invocation (path, url, pattern, or serialized args) and tracks counts per turn; once a threshold is reached the mixin blocks further redundant executions and returns a helpful DUPLICATE CALL BLOCKED message. 
3. Extraction detection maps items to extractor tools by checking for explicit URLs, embedded URLs, known file extensions, or falling back to a file read. 
4. The micro-turn scale loop follows a strict four-step flow for each item: extract content with the detected tool, call the LLM once with a minimal prompt to produce a processed summary, write or sink the result according to the output strategy, and update progress tracking. 
5. For no-file strategies the loop supports sinks like typesense (indexing), send_mail, or in-memory reply accumulation, and handles sink failures separately from extract/LLM errors. 
6. The loop instruments time and token usage for each item to compute ETA and performance metrics, and it captures the last written summary to provide a format reference to later LLM calls so outputs remain consistent. 
7. After each successful write the mixin attempts to match written content or filenames to items and mark them done; it also records resolved absolute output paths and tracks when multiple distinct output files exist (which can prevent micro-loop takeover). 
8. The mixin prunes large extractor tool results and compresses older assistant/tool message pairs to prevent linear context growth, using configurable thresholds and keeping a small window of recent full pairs for continuity. 
9. Tool result handling appends helpful hints when the agent appears to be skipping write steps, and it rolls back duplicate counters on failures to allow retries. 
10. Embedded tool-call extraction supports many syntaxes: annotated blocks, DSL-like maps, JSON blobs, and XML-ish invokes; parsed calls are normalized into ToolCall objects with deduplication of identical signatures. 
11. Friendly rewrite logic clips long raw output into representative blocks and asks the LLM to produce a user-facing summary using stored prompt templates, with fallback to returning the raw output if the rewrite fails. 
12. Throughout, cancellation checks are performed at safe points (between items, after extract, after LLM) so long runs can be stopped promptly and cleanly. 
13. The mixin also provides heuristics for model/runtime compatibility (e.g., whether tool-role messages can be followed up) and exposes hooks for auto-capturing contacts, scripts, and APIs after certain successful tool calls. 
14. Finally, the mixin logs structured diagnostics at key events (start/finish per item, write results, errors) and returns a summarized result dict at loop completion describing processed, failed, cancelled, and error details.
